401 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Telles v. Carter


No. 5687


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


57 N.M. 704; 1953-NMSC-105; 262 P.2d 985; 1953 N.M. LEXIS 1044



November 3, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 3, 1953


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding contesting results of city election for office of City Commissioner. The District Court, Otero County, George T. Harris, J., entered judgment favorable to contestant, and contestee appealed. The Supreme Court, Seymour, J., held that under statutes providing that elector shall mark a cross in square on ballot, that cross shall be two lines intersecting at any angle within circle or square, that elector can vote only by making such cross with pen and ink or indelible pencil and that no elector shall place any mark upon his ballot by which it may afterwards be identified, ballots which were marked by placing of check mark inside square opposite name of certain candidate would be rejected.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contestee sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Otero County, New Mexico, that found in favor appellee contestant in a proceeding to contest the results of a city election for the office of city commissioner. The contestee argued that ballots marked with a check mark rather than a cross, as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 56-312, 56-313 (1941), were nonetheless valid.


OVERVIEW: Twenty-seven ballots cast in the city election were marked with a check in the box beside the contestee's name. If the ballots marked with a check were counted, the contestee would win. If the ballots were rejected, the contestant would be the winner of the election. The court held that the general election provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 14-303, 56-720 (1941) were applicable to elections for municipal officers. As to the check marks, the court noted that there was no allegation of fraud. The court also noted the competing interests of voters' intent and ballot secrecy. However, the court rejected the minority view that upheld the intent of the voter. The court followed the majority view and concluded that the statutory provisions requiring a voter to mark a ballot by a cross were mandatory. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 56-501 (1941) prohibited voters from placing a mark on a ballot that could later identify that voter. Interpreting the marking provisions as mandatory promoted ballot secrecy. The voter had to be held to strict performance. This also relieved voters from the consequences of election officials' failure to perform their statutory duties. The trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the contestant that effectively declared the contestant the winner of the election was affirmed.

 

402 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


No. 5566


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


57 N.M. 459; 1953-NMSC-072; 260 P.2d 370; 1953 N.M. LEXIS 1003



August 18, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: August 18, 1953


PRIOR HISTORY: Prosecution for skinning one neat calf belonging to another without permission from the owner. The District Court, Lea County, George T. Harris, D. J., granted defendant's motion to quash the information, and the state appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., held that the statute, providing for the punishment of all persons who, without the permission of the owner, skin or remove the hide from the carcass of neat cattle found dead, but exempting all employees of railroad company so doing when the animal was killed by the railroad company, was constitutional.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Lea County (New Mexico), which granted a motion by defendant to quash an information charging him with skinning one neat calf belonging to another without permission of the owner, a violation of N.M. Comp. Stat. § 41-418 (1941).


OVERVIEW: After the trial court granted defendant's motion to quash the indictment charging him with the skinning of one neat calf belonging to another without permission in violation of N.M. Comp. Stat. § 41-418, the State appealed. The court noted that the grounds upon which the motion to quash was based were that the statute was unconstitutional because it discriminated against all persons except employees of railroad companies by whom cattle were killed. The court noted that the legislature could classify for legislative purposes without offending the constitutional requirement of equal protection of the laws as long as the classification was based upon some rational and substantial basis inherent in the subject matter or some difference in situation which distinguished those within the class from those without and which rationally justified different or unequal treatment. The court reversed the trial court's decision to quash the indictment and remanded the cause, holding that the statute's purpose was to prevent theft and protect the industry of stock raising and that the exemption of railroad employees was rationally related to the statute's purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court that quashed the indictment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

403 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Middle Rio Grande Water Users Ass'n v. Middle Rio Grande Conservancy Dist.


No. 5544


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


57 N.M. 287; 1953-NMSC-035; 258 P.2d 391; 1953 N.M. LEXIS 981



May 11, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On Application for Approval of Amendatory Contract June 29, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: The Middle Rio Grande Conservancy District brought proceedings against the Middle Rio Grande Water Users Association to determine validity of reclamation contract between the United States and the District. The District Court of the Second Judicial District, sitting as Conservancy Court, Waldo H. Rogers, R. F. Deacon Arledge, and Edwin L. Swope, District Judges, entered judgment in favor of the District, and the Association appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that contract is valid in all particulars, except as to provision giving Secretary of Interior power to withhold water from water user for failure to pay assessment declared irregular or void by Court of competent jurisdiction or as to which collection has been enjoined by any such court; and, except as to a 160 acre limitation imposed by contract. The Supreme Court, Sadler, C. J., held the contract was valid in all particulars, save as to the powers conferred on the Secretary of the Interior on the conditions named. Federici, D. J., dissented insofar as the court failed to approve the contract in toto.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an association of agricultural water users (association) within appellee conservancy district (district), sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Second Judicial District (New Mexico) sitting as Conservancy Court, which validated a contract between the district and the United States.


OVERVIEW: The district and the United States entered into a contract pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 77-3101 through 77-3124 (1941) and the Reclamation Act, 43 U.S.C.S. §§ 371-670. Under the contract, the irrigation and drainage system operated by the district would be conveyed to the United States, which would rehabilitate and extend it, with the cost reimbursed by the district over 40 years. The association challenged the contract and the New Mexico statutes, but the conservancy court found them valid and constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed, with the exception of one contractual provision. That provision allowed the United States to deny water rights to any user whose assessment was judicially determined to be invalid. The court found that the contract could not override the right of a user to have his day in court. The court held that the conveyance to the United States was proper, as it was only for purposes of security, with reconveyance to be made upon payment. The court found that limitation of water delivery to those with vested rights to water in an amount that was more than sufficient to irrigate 160 acres was valid and constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court held that, with the exception of one provision, the contract between the district and the United States and the statute at issue were valid. The court reversed the conservancy court's judgment with regard to a provision of the contract that allowed the United States to deny water rights to any user whose assessment was judicially determined to be invalid.

 

404 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Shoup Voting Mach. Corp. v. Bd. of Comm'rs


No. 5559


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


57 N.M. 196; 1953-NMSC-032; 256 P.2d 1068; 1953 N.M. LEXIS 970



May 6, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: May 6, 1953


PRIOR HISTORY: Suit was brought for declaratory judgment concerning constitutionality of statute authorizing county commissioners to purchase voting machines and to provide for payment thereof, in annual installments not exceeding ten years. The District Court of Bernalillo County, R. F. Deacon Arledge, D. J., entered judgment holding statute unconstitutional, and defendants appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., held that statute violates constitutional provision forbidding contraction of any debt for any purpose other than for erecting necessary public buildings or constructing or repairing public roads and bridges.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Board of Commissioners of Bernalillo County appealed a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) that held that 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 192 was unconstitutional. Plaintiff voting-machine corporation had brought the case under N.M. Comp. Stat. § 25-601 (1941) as one for a declaratory judgment on constitutionality. The corporation had entered into a contract with the Board for voting machines.


OVERVIEW: The error committed by the trial court as presented on appeal was that it had mistakenly ruled that as a matter of law the contract between the corporation and the Board was null and void because 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 192 contravened the N.M. Const. art. 9, § 10. According to the court, the N.M. Const. art. 9, § 10 indubitably prohibited a county from the contracting of any debt for any purpose except the erection of necessary public buildings or the construction or repair of public roads and bridges and then only after a proposition to incur such debt was submitted to the qualified county electors and approved by a majority of those voting on it. Ergo, the court ruled that the Board did not have authority to bind the County of Bernalillo by a contract with the corporation for voting machines to be provided by the corporation for the use of the County.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

405 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spears


No. 5543


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


57 N.M. 400; 1953-NMSC-033; 259 P.2d 356; 1953 N.M. LEXIS 992; 39 A.L.R.2d 595



May 6, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Granted July 7, 1953. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Denied July 14, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: Prosecution for engaging in business as real estate broker without first obtaining a license. The District Court, Lea County, George T. Harris, D. J., overruled defendant's motion to quash information, and defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., held that statute, which authorizes real estate board to issue real estate broker's licenses and which provides for punishment of persons, corporations, and associations but not for firms, partnerships, and copartnerships, for violations of statute, is not unconstitutional on ground that it fails to provide penalties equally applicable to all persons coming within its prohibition.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which overruled defendant's motion to quash the information filed against him by the State for engaging in business as real estate broker without first obtaining a license, in violation of 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 224 (Act).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had engaged in the real estate business for eight years but never had a real estate broker's license in New Mexico. The court held that the Act was constitutional. The Act was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power because it had to be presumed that the board would exercise fairly and impartially the powers conferred and its regulations did not determine what the law should be. The Act did not deny equal protection by exempting those already licensed from taking the examination. Such persons, who had rights already recognized by the law, were not similarly situated with those who had a mere hope or expectation of embarking in the same calling at a future date. The business of real estate broker was one properly subject to police regulation, and in the exercise of its police power the State could require that all applicants be honest, trustworthy, and of good moral character and reputation before a license was issued to them to engage in business. The Act did not deny equal protection by not prescribing a penalty for partnerships, which were not recognized as separate from their component members, insofar as criminal responsibility was concerned.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

406 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Shepard v. Mechem


No. 5593


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


56 N.M. 762; 1952-NMSC-105; 250 P.2d 897; 1952 N.M. LEXIS 978



December 12, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 12, 1952


PRIOR HISTORY: Original mandamus proceeding to prevent alleged illegal diversions of trust funds produced by lands granted by the Congress of the United States for specific purposes, and to compel restoration of moneys to proper funds. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that statutes authorizing use of funds produced by lands obtained from the United States under Enabling Act which granted lands to State in trust and restricted use of money derived therefrom to certain specified purposes, which grants were accepted by State in Constitution with their trust provisions and limitations, to help defray general government expenses were unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An action in mandamus was instituted by petitioner State of New Mexico, on the relation of the Commissioner of Public Lands (New Mexico), to prevent alleged illegal diversions of trust funds produced by lands granted by the Congress of the United States for specific purposes. Petitioner also sought to compel restoration of such monies to the proper funds.


OVERVIEW: 1953 N.M. Laws ch. 181 and the Appropriation Act, 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 227 authorized the use of funds produced by lands obtained from the United States under the Enabling Act (Act), Act of June 20, 1910, 36 Stat. 557, to help defray general governmental operating expenses. The Act granted lands to the state in trust and restricted the use of money derived therefrom to certain specified purposes, most of which were for the benefit of specific educational and penal institutions. The state accepted the grants with such restrictions by the terms of N.M. Const. art. 21, §§ 9, 10. Acting on orders of the state board of finance and the state auditor, the state treasurer diverted certain sums from the fund created pursuant to the Act to the general fund, where the funds became intermingled. The court held that 1953 N.M. Laws ch. 181 and the Appropriation Act, 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 227, were unconstitutional. Mandamus was available to enforce the provisions of the Act, and the contemplated use of the funds would be a breach of trust. The state had agreed, by constitutional provisions irrevocable without congressional consent, to the restrictive language in the Act granting the lands.


OUTCOME: The court made the alternative writ absolute.

 

407 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Vigil v. State


No. 5408


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


56 N.M. 411; 1952-NMSC-054; 244 P.2d 1110; 1952 N.M. LEXIS 927



May 29, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: May 29, 1952


PRIOR HISTORY: Action instituted on behalf of four minor plaintiffs by their next friend to recover for personal injuries suffered by them through negligence of employees of State Penitentiary. The District Court, Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, J., entered judgment for plaintiffs, and defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that statute granting consent by State to be sued for personal injuries suffered by such four minors through negligence of employees of State Penitentiary was unconstitutional as a special law enacted where a general law could have been applicable.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, cause remanded with directions to dismiss causes of action sued upon.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order from the District Court for Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff injured parties in a suit to recover for personal injuries suffered by plaintiffs through the negligence of the employees of the State Penitentiary. The State contended that the statute granting consent by the State to be sued was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, who were minors, were injured as a result of allegedly negligent treatment by employees of the State penitentiary. Plaintiffs, through their parents, filed suit under the authority of a statute that granted consent by the State to be sued for such injuries. The trial court granted judgment in favor of plaintiffs, and the State appealed. The State contended that the statute was unconstitutional as a special law enacted where a general law could have been applicable in violation of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 24. The court reversed and remanded, holding that a previous, identical statute had been held to be unconstitutional. The statute represented an unconstitutional instance of a special law in a field where a general law could have been made applicable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.

 

408 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Fowler v. Corlett


No. 5478


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


56 N.M. 430; 1952-NMSC-055; 244 P.2d 1122; 1952 N.M. LEXIS 929



May 29, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: May 29, 1952


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by Jack Fowler, doing business as the Santa Fe Beverage Company, against Charles H. Corlett, as Commissioner of Revenue, and another for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of an act amending the act relating to funds for the Commission on Alcoholism. From a judgment of the District Court, Sante Fe County, David W. Carmody, J., sustaining the constitutionality of the amendatory act, plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that the amendatory act is not unconstitutional as not expressing or embracing its subject-matter in its title, delegating the Legislature's taxing power to the State Revenue Bureau, incorporating provisions of the Liquor Control Act by reference to its title only, denying due process and equal protection of laws, or providing for double taxation.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant businessman sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), in favor of appellee Commissioner of Revenue in the businessman's declaratory judgment action regarding the constitutionality of 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 218. The trial court ruled that ch. 218 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the businessman contended that ch. 218 was unconstitutional because its subject matter was not expressed or embraced in its title and that this failure contravened the requirements of the N.M. Const. art. 4, § 16. The court ruled that the title of 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 218 left no doubt as to its purpose and thus satisfied the chief purpose of N.M. Const. art. 4, § 16, which was to prevent the legislature from being defrauded or surprised by means of hidden or concealed provisions of bills. The court rejected another asserted basis of invalidity for ch. 218, i.e., that it amounted to an illegal delegation to the Bureau of Revenue of the taxing power of the legislature. The court further rejected a challenge to ch. 218 asserted on the basis of vagueness. The court commented that, if the businessman truly did not understand what the term "alcoholic beverage" meant, the court declined to enlighten him. The court found no due process violation or double taxation because the levy imposed a blanket tax against all alcoholic beverages. No group or class was taxed to the exclusion of any other group or class.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the Commissioner, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Brown v. Bowling


No. 5406


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


56 N.M. 96; 1952-NMSC-017; 240 P.2d 846; 1952 N.M. LEXIS 889



February 6, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: February 6, 1952


PRIOR HISTORY: Paul Brown and wife sued James T. Bowling, if living, or if deceased, his unknown heirs, and all unknown claimants of interests adverse to plaintiffs' estate in certain land, to quiet title thereto. Mary E. Gardner and others intervened as heirs of James T. Bowling, deceased. From a judgment of the District Court, Rio Arriba County, Edwin L. Swope, J., quieting title in intervenors, plaintiffs appealed. The Supreme Court, Anderson, D. J., held that plaintiff wife, employed by the County Board of Education as a rural school teacher, was not a county employee prohibited by statute from purchasing from the State Tax Commission land sold to the State for delinquent taxes.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a husband and wife, sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Rio Arriba County (New Mexico), which was rendered in favor of appellee heirs of the decedent in an action to quiet title in certain land the husband and wife had purchased from the New Mexico State Tax Commission.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife were the grantees in a tax deed from the State Tax Commission covering 640 acres of land. The land had been sold to the State for delinquent taxes. The husband and wife filed an action seeking to quiet title. The heirs of the deceased intervened. The heirs contended that the wife, who was a rural school teacher, was an employee of the state and was barred by N.M. Comp. Laws § 76-707 (1941) from purchasing property from the state. The trial court held that deed from the State Tax Commission to the husband and wife should be declared to be void and that title of the heirs be quieted when the husband and wife had been reimbursed for all monies paid by them for the property and for the value of improvements made. The court held that the wife was not a county employee prohibited by § 76-707 from purchasing from the State Tax Commission land sold to the State for delinquent taxes. The court noted that it was error to find that the wife, as a school teacher was an employee of a county and the State, as the finding was not supported by any substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which was rendered in favor of the heirs of decease in an action to quiet title in certain land the husband and wife had purchased from the State Tax Commission. The cause was remanded to the district court with a direction to vacate its judgment and render one quieting title in the husband and wife.

Wiggs v. City of Albuquerque


No. 5441


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


56 N.M. 214; 1952-NMSC-013; 242 P.2d 865; 1952 N.M. LEXIS 903



January 19, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected on Denial of Rehearing April 4, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by Clarence Wiggs against the City of Albuquerque, New Mexico, and others, to enjoin defendants from adopting or acting upon a proposed ordinance to issue bonds for the construction of a municipal auditorium, and for other relief. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Edwin L. Swope, J., rendered an adverse judgment, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, J., held that the revenue bonds in question would create a debt within the prohibition of article 9, § 12 of the Constitution in absence of an approving vote at a referendum.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Bernalillo (New Mexico), which granted a judgment in favor of appellee, City and associated individuals, in the citizen's action to enjoin the City and associated individuals from adopting or acting upon a proposed ordinance to issue bonds for the construction of a municipal auditorium, and for other relief.


OVERVIEW: The City and associated individuals submitted to qualified electors of the City the proposition whether the municipality should issue its general obligation bonds in a certain amount for the acquisition of a site for a municipal auditorium, including cost of construction and equipment. The proposition was adopted, whereupon negotiable bonds in said amount were issued. When money raised under a second proposition and money realized from the sale of City property was insufficient to construct the auditorium, the associated individuals directed an attorney to prepare an ordinance under the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 6-301 to 6-308 (1941) to authorize the issuance and sale of revenue bonds in a certain sum for the purpose of raising additional funds. The citizen sought to enjoin the adoption and the acting upon of the proposed ordinance. The lower court granted a judgment in favor of the City and associated individuals. The court reversed that judgment and remanded the case. The court held that the issuance of the revenue bonds under the proposed ordinance would create a debt within the prohibition of N.M. Const. art. 9, § 12 in the absence of an approving vote at a referendum.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the City and associated individuals and remanded the matter to the district court with a direction to it to set aside its judgment and enter and order permanently enjoining the City and associated individuals in accordance with the court's opinion.

Kaiser v. Thomson


No. 5355


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


55 N.M. 270; 1951-NMSC-037; 232 P.2d 142; 1951 N.M. LEXIS 740



May 9, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 18, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by Gus Kaiser against Guy Thomson and Ada Thomson, and others, to establish and foreclose a mechanic's lien, or for the reasonable value of labor and materials on a quantum meruit basis. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Henry G. Coors, J., entered an order of dismissal with prejudice, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, J., held that plaintiff's failure to comply with statute requiring contractor's license at time cause of action arose, precluded his recovery for labor and materials furnished defendants.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which dismissed the contractor's claim against appellee building owners that sought to establish and foreclose on a mechanic's lien for the reasonable value of labor and materials on a quantum meruit basis.


OVERVIEW: The contractor instituted an action against the building owners, seeking a judgment for labor and materials supplied in the construction and alteration of a building, to establish and foreclose on a mechanic's lien, and for attorney fees. The contractor also sought judgment for the reasonable value of his labor and materials on a quantum meruit basis. The trial court dismissed the action with prejudice for the contractor's failure to allege that he was the holder of a contractor's license as required by N.M. Comp. Laws § 51-901 (1941). The court held that the contractor's failure to comply with statute requiring contractor's license at time cause of action arose, precluded his recovery for labor and materials furnished to the building owners. The court concluded that where a statute rendered a contract of artisans, professional, or business men void, or expressly provided that there shall be no recovery thereon for noncompliance with the statute, that no actionable cause arose from such a contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which dismissed the contractor's claim against the building owners that sought to establish and foreclose on a mechanic's lien for the reasonable value of labor and materials on a quantum meruit basis.

 

412 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Lucero v. N.M. State Highway Dep't


No. 5259


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


55 N.M. 157; 1951-NMSC-017; 228 P.2d 945; 1951 N.M. LEXIS 718



March 13, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: March 13, 1951


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by Alfredo Lucero against New Mexico State Highway Department to recover for injuries when he was struck by a tire blown from a wheel of a road grader being operated by a state employee. The Mountain States Mutual Casualty Company intervened and sought subrogation for amount paid on account of claim under compensation act. The District Court, Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, J., rendered an adverse judgment, and the defendant and intervenor appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that statute consenting to and authorizing a suit by the plaintiff against the State of Mexico for such injuries was a special law in a field where a general law could be made applicable, was therefore void, and that action could not be maintained thereunder.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the New Mexico State Highway Department, and intervenor, its workmen's compensation insurer, sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which awarded damages to plaintiff, a Department employee, for personal injuries sustained when he was struck by a tire blown from the wheel of a road grader being operated by another state employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed suit under authority of 1947 N.M. Laws ch. 162, which was passed by the state legislature to consent to a suit by one particular plaintiff, to waive sovereign immunity to the suit, and to authorize the payment of damages should any be awarded. Defendants contended that the act was unconstitutional in that it was a special law in a field where a general law could be made applicable. The court reversed the judgment entered in favor of the employee. It held that the act met the definition of a special law, in that it was enacted for the sole purpose of allowing the employee to sue the State; further, the court held that a tort action could not be maintained against the State absent legislative permission. The court held that the act violated N.M. Const. art. 4, § 24, and was therefore void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to vacate the judgment and dismiss the suit.

Crosthwait v. White


No. 5338


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


55 N.M. 71; 1951-NMSC-003; 226 P.2d 477; 1951 N.M. LEXIS 705



January 15, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 15, 1951


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by Lynn Crosthwait, and others, on behalf of themselves and all others similarly situated, against Len O. White, and others, attacking the sufficiency of a petition, filed with the board of county commissioners of Harding County, for an election to determine whether a portion of the county should be annexed to the adjoining county of Quay. The District Court, Harding County, David W. Carmody, J., rendered a judgment for the defendants, and the plaintiffs appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that 1941 Comp. §§ 15-3305 to 15-3311 providing for annexation of portions of counties was constitutional.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county residents sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Harding County (New Mexico), which was rendered in favor of appellee qualified voters on the sufficiency of their petition for an election to determine whether a portion of the county should be annexed to an adjoining county.


OVERVIEW: A majority of qualified voters of a precinct and part of another precinct, acting pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 14-3305 to 15-3311 (1941), filed a petition with the Board of County Commissioners of Harding County (New Mexico), requesting that an election be called to determine whether such part of the county should be annexed to the adjoining county. The board found the petition was in proper form and had been signed by the requisite number of qualified electors, and then ordered that the election be held. County residents instituted an action attacking the sufficiency of the petition and the constitutionality of the statute. The trial court held that all of the conditions of the statute were present and that the requirements of the statute had been met by the qualified electors and the commissioners. The court held that the statute providing for the annexation of portions of counties was constitutional. The court concluded that the statute was available to the county residents of any areas in the State where the conditions prescribed in the statute existed. The court concluded that the statute was a general and not a special law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which was rendered in favor of the qualified voters and against the county residents on the sufficiency of their petition for an election to determine whether a portion of the county should be annexed to an adjoining county.

 

414 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bliss v. Dority


No. 5296


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


55 N.M. 12; 1950-NMSC-066; 225 P.2d 1007; 1950 N.M. LEXIS 652



December 22, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 22, 1950


PRIOR HISTORY: The State of New Mexico, on the relation of John H. Bliss, State Engineer, brought separate suits against Bert Troy Dority, Loman Wiley, and S. A. Lanning, Jr., to enjoin defendants from unlawfully using water drawn from the Roswell Artesian Basin and valley fill above it, which plaintiff asserted were subject to appropriation. The suits were consolidated for trial. The District Court, Chaves County, C. Roy Anderson, J., entered a decree adverse to defendants, and defendants appealed. The Supreme Court, Brice, C. J., held, inter alia, that artesian water and underground reservoir in valley fill overlying such artesian basin, were reserved on or before date Desert Land Act became effective, to state as trustee for public, and were subject to use by public at any time thereafter by authority of state statutes, even though passed after date of patents to land of defendants.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant users appealed a decree of the District Court, Chaves County (New Mexico), which enjoined them from using water drawn from an underground water basin in an action against them brought by plaintiff state.


OVERVIEW: The state brought an action against the users alleging that the users were unlawfully using water drawn from an underground water basin for the irrigation of their land. The trial court held in favor of the state and entered a decree enjoining the users from using the water basin. The users appealed the decree enjoining them from using unappropriated water, arguing that they had a vested interest in the title to the water under their lands. The court ruled that the public waters of the state were owned by the state as trustee for the people and that the state was authorized to institute suits to protect the public waters against unlawful use. Further, the court held that waters of underground rivers with defined banks were subject to appropriation and that all water that could be used for irrigation was reserved to be used beneficially by the public. The court affirmed the decree enjoining the users, concluding that the water involved was reserved to the state as trustee for the public.


OUTCOME: The decree enjoining the users from using the underground water for the irrigation of their lands was affirmed.

 

415 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Strawn v. Russell


No. 5270


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


54 N.M. 221; 1950-NMSC-028; 219 P.2d 292; 1950 N.M. LEXIS 618



June 5, 1950 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 5, 1950


PRIOR HISTORY: W. A. Strawn and others sued John W. Russell and others to enjoin consolidation of two rural school districts and to adjudge resolutions of the Roosevelt County Board of Education and the State Board of Education, recommending and directing the consolidation, arbitrary and unreasonable. From a judgment of the District Court, Roosevelt County, E. T. Hensley, Jr., J., dismissing the petition for an injunction, plaintiffs appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that the boards' actions were not arbitrary or unreasonable and that the order of consolidation was not unconstitutional as denying some pupils of the two districts a free school by creating such a large district that they could not go to school and back home each day.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, residents and taxpayers, challenged a judgment of the District Court of Roosevelt County (New Mexico) dismissing their action against appellees, Roosevelt County Board of Education and the State Board of Education, seeking to enjoin the boards from consolidating two rural school districts. Appellants contended that the consolidation resolutions were arbitrary and unreasonable.


OVERVIEW: Due mostly to the increase in farm sizes in the rural districts, the number of students had decreased as families farmed larger and larger plots. Resulting cuts in school budgets had reduced the number of teachers and those remaining were required to teach more classes. The boards decided that the two districts would be consolidated. The residents and taxpayers filed an action to enjoin consolidation, and the trial court denied to grant their injunction. On appeal the court held, as an initial matter, that the boards had been given authority in effecting consolidation, and absent arbitrariness or unreasonableness, the decision of the boards could not be overturned. The court further held that while the extended bus trips of students in the new district was unfortunate, because it did not make it impossible to go to and return from school in one day, the consolidation was not unreasonable. The court noted that N.M. Const. art. 12, § 1 required a uniform system of education, free to all school-aged children, but that the consolidation did not violate that requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

416 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Albuquerque Bus Co. v. Everly


No. 5214


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


53 N.M. 460; 1949-NMSC-058; 211 P.2d 127; 1949 N.M. LEXIS 718



November 3, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 3, 1949


PRIOR HISTORY: The Albuquerque Bus Company, a copartnership, brought action against Ernest Everly and others, as members of the City Commission of the City of Albuquerque, and another challenging sufficiency of a petition asking that a referendum election be held with respect to plaintiff's franchise to operate buses.

The District Court of Bernalillo County, Edwin L. Swope, J., rendered judgment against plaintiff, and plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., affirmed the judgment, holding that 1941 Comp. § 14-3501 providing that where petition objecting to granting of a franchise is signed by 10 per cent of adult residents of a municipality, governing body must submit question of granting of franchise to vote of qualified electors, prevailed over referendum provisions of city charter requiring 20 per cent of registered voters to petition for referendum election, and that § 14-3501 is constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bus company sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Bernalillo County, New Mexico, in favor of appellees, a city clerk and commissioners, in the bus company's suit to challenge a petition and referendum election on its franchise. The bus company argued that N.M. Comp. Stat. § 14-3501 (1941) did not control over city charter provisions for referendum elections and that § 14-3501 was invalid under N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16.


OVERVIEW: By ordinance, the city granted the bus company a franchise to operate over its streets for a specified term. When the term ended, more than 10 percent of the city's adult residents petitioned to hold a referendum election on the franchise. The city ordered an election and directed the bus company to cover the expenses. The bus company challenged the petition on the ground that Albuquerque, N.M., City Charter § 2, art. 3 required that a petition be signed by 20 percent of the city's adult residents. A delegation of power to cities to grant franchises was strictly construed in favor of the public. N.M. Comp. Stat. § 14-3501 (1941) was a special act that applied to all municipalities, whether organized under general or special laws. The court held that the referendum provisions of § 14-3501 that dealt specially with popular referenda on franchise ordinances prevailed over the referendum provisions of the city charter, which applied to ordinances generally and not to franchise ordinances specifically. The title of § 14-3501 was sufficiently clear and did not violate N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16, because it stated that it was amending a prior statute that related to franchises.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of defendants and holding that the referenda statute was constitutional was affirmed.

 

417 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Tindall v. Bryan


No. 5207


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


54 N.M. 112; 1949-NMSC-051; 215 P.2d 354; 1949 N.M. LEXIS 737



August 29, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: August 29, 1949


PRIOR HISTORY: J. M. Tindall brought an action against Ira Bryan and recovered a judgment in the District Court of Union County, Luis E. Armijo, J., and defendant appealed.

Plaintiff moved to dismiss the appeal on jurisdictional grounds.

The principal question was whether Laws 1947, c. 175, repealing Laws 1917, c. 43, conferring appellate jurisdiction on the Supreme Court, and many other laws, is constitutional.



DISPOSITION: The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., overruled the motion, holding that the 1947 act is unconstitutional and inoperative as not clearly expressing the subject thereof in its title and as containing more than one subject.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a motion to dismiss the appeal of defendant of a judgment from the District Court of Union County (New Mexico). Defendant asserted that 1947 N.M. Laws ch. 175, which repealed the statute conferring appellate jurisdiction on the court, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: N.M. Comp. Stat. § 19-201 conferred jurisdiction on the court of appeals from final judgments rendered in civil actions. The legislature enacted 1947 N.M. Laws ch. 175, which repealed certain obsolete and superseded laws and many other laws including the appellate jurisdiction of the court. The act was entitled "An Act To Repeal Obsolete And Superseded Laws Which Are Not Included In The New Mexico 1941 Compilation, As Shown In Parallel Reference Table Volume VI Of The 1941 Compilation." The court concluded that chapter 175 violated N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16 because the title did not clearly express the subject of the bill and it contained more than one subject. Therefore, the court concluded that the statute was invalid and that the court had jurisdiction over the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss the appeal.

Rubalcava v. Garst


No. 5190


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


53 N.M. 295; 1949-NMSC-035; 206 P.2d 1154; 1949 N.M. LEXIS 694



June 8, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 8, 1949


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Socorro County; A. W. Marshall, Judge.

Action by Margarita Rubalcava against Stephen Q. Garst, administrator of the estate of Emilio Papa, deceased, for performance of deceased's oral contract to devise property to plaintiff. Judgment for plaintiff, and defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant estate administrator appealed a decision of the District Court of Socorro County (New Mexico), which enforced a decedent's oral contract to devise property to plaintiff adopted daughter.


OVERVIEW: The birth mother of the daughter, then a widow, gave the daughter to a childless couple in consideration of their oral promise to take the daughter into their home, raise her as their own child, and devise to her all property of which they died seized. The daughter lived with the couple and served them as their child until she married, with the consent of such couple, at the age of 17. The adoptive mother died and 10 years later the adoptive father died intestate. The administrator claimed that 1947 N.M. Laws ch. 66, § 1, which prohibited oral contracts to devise property in consideration of giving up a child for adoption, was applicable. In affirming the trial court's decision to enforce the oral agreement, the court held that, because the agreement was fully performed by the daughter prior to the statute's effective date, application of the statute would violate N.M. Const. art. II, § 19, which barred enactment of ex post facto laws, bills of attainder, and laws impairing the obligations of contracts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

419 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. McKinley


No. 5113


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


53 N.M. 106; 1949-NMSC-010; 202 P.2d 964; 1949 N.M. LEXIS 666



February 11, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: February 11, 1949


PRIOR HISTORY: Error to District Court, Bernalillo County; R. F. Deacon Arledge, Judge.

Prosecution by the State of New Mexico against R. L. McKinley for contributing to the delinquency of a female minor under the age of 18 years. From judgment sustaining defendant's motion to quash information, the state brings error.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment from the District Court, Bernalillo County, New Mexico, that sustained defendant's motion to quash an information charging defendant with contributing to the delinquency of a female minor under the age of 18 years in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 44-116 (Supp. 1941). The information was dismissed on the ground that § 44-116 was so vague as to render it null and void.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with contributing to the delinquency of a minor by having sexual intercourse with her. The court disagreed that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 44-116 (Supp. 1941) was vague. Section 44-116 proscribed an act or omission that caused or tended to cause or encourage the delinquency of persons under 18 years of age but did not specify or define the particular act or omission that constituted the offense. The court found that the common sense of the community and the sense of decency and morality that most people entertained were sufficient t point out what particular conduct was criminal under § 44-116. The indelicacy of the subject prevented a particular definition of what constituted the crime. The district court took notice that the juvenile court had exclusive jurisdiction over the offense under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 44-102 (Supp. 1941). The court held that that portion of § 44-102 was unconstitutional and void. When the legislature made the offense a felony, it automatically placed cases arising under it for trial in district courts. Under N.M. Const. art. VI, §§ 13, 23, the legislature had no authority to divest the district courts of jurisdiction over felony offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment that quashed the information and held that the statute criminalizing the offense of contributing to the delinquency of a minor was unconstitutional was reversed. The cause was remanded with directions to set the judgment aside and enter an order overruling defendant's motion to quash.

Associated Petroleum Transp., Ltd. v. Shepard


No. 5106


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


53 N.M. 52; 1949-NMSC-002; 201 P.2d 772; 1949 N.M. LEXIS 659



January 5, 1949 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 24, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Santa Fe County; Carmody, Judge.

Action by Associated Petroleum Transport, Limited, and others against Guy Shepard, personally and as State Treasurer of the State of New Mexico, for a declaratory judgment that statute under which plaintiffs were taxed was unconstitutional, that defendant was wrongfully withholding plaintiffs' money without authority of law, and that plaintiffs were entitled to a refund. From a judgment dismissing the complaint, the plaintiffs appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of an order from the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by defendant, the Treasurer of the State of New Mexico, in an action challenging the constitutionality of a property tax.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers had railroad cars that they rented to common carrier railroad companies at a rate of compensation fixed by order of the United States Interstate Commerce Commission. The cars were moved by common carrier railroads into, out of, and across the State of New Mexico, but none of them were permanently located in the State or any taxing district. The taxpayers brought an action against the Treasurer, seeking a declaratory judgment that the statute under which they were taxed was unconstitutional, that the Treasurer was wrongfully withholding their money without authority of law, and that they were entitled to a refund. The trial court granted the Treasurer's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that the taxpayers, having selected the United States mail as the means of delivering their protest, were chargeable with any delay. Hence, if their protest failed to reach the State Tax Commission within the statutory period, it was their fault. Because the taxpayers' protest was not timely filed with the Commission, the Commission had no jurisdiction to hear it. The taxpayers did not exhaust their statutory remedy before filing their lawsuit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Arledge v. Mabry


No. 5144


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


52 N.M. 303; 1948-NMSC-047; 197 P.2d 884; 1948 N.M. LEXIS 656



September 21, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 27, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus proceeding by R. F. Deacon Arledge against Thomas J. Mabry, Governor of the State of New Mexico, Charles R. Brice, Chief Justice of the Supreme Court of the State of New Mexico, and Mrs. M. A. Romero, Secretary of State, comprising the State Board of Canvassers of the State of New Mexico, and the State Board of Canvassers, respondents, to command respondents to recanvass returns for Democratic nomination of office of the judge of district court in certain matter.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ of mandamus made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Informant, an unsuccessful candidate in a primary election for the democratic nomination for district court judge, brought mandamus proceedings against respondent individuals, the governor, chief justice of the state supreme court, and the secretary of state, who comprised the State Board of Canvassers of the State of New Mexico; and the Board itself, to command respondents to recanvass the election returns. The court issued an alternative writ.


OVERVIEW: The candidate had originally been declared the winner, but, after a recount, the Board certified his opponent as having the most votes. The candidate sought another recount and claimed that this recount should exclude all return from portions of a certain precinct, which had been acquired by the United States through condemnation proceedings and incorporated what was commonly known as the "Los Alamos Project." He claimed that the area at issue was not "in New Mexico" within the meaning of N.M. Const. art. VII, § 1. The court concluded that part of the land acquired by the federal government for the Los Alamos Project was under exclusive federal jurisdiction and so was not in New Mexico for purposes of elector qualifications, but that part remained within New Mexico for the purpose of determining elector eligibility. However, the polling places within the Project were all outside of New Mexico, and that fact was fatal to the validity of the election. Those residents affected could cast their ballots elsewhere or vote by absentee ballot, but it was up to the county board of commissioners to relocate the polling places. The court made permanent the alternative writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The alternative writ of mandamus was made permanent.

Bd. of County Comm'rs v. McCulloh


No. 5096


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


52 N.M. 210; 1948-NMSC-028; 195 P.2d 1005; 1948 N.M. LEXIS 643



June 21, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 21, 1948


PRIOR HISTORY: Original mandamus action by the Board of County Commissioners of Bernalillo County, relator, against Clyde C. McCulloh, Attorney General of the State of New Mexico, respondent, to compel the respondent to approve bonds of the County of Bernalillo for purpose of constructing a county hospital with isolation ward.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandamus made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Realtor Board of County Commissioners of Bernalillo County brought a mandamus action in order to compel respondent Attorney General of the State of New Mexico to approve bonds of the County of Bernalillo for purpose of constructing a county hospital with isolation ward.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General responded to the court's alternative writ commanding him to approve the bonds by stating that the hospital bond election held and conducted by the Board was in conformity with 1947 N.M. Laws Ch. 48. However, the Attorney General contended that the bonds were void because 1947 N.M. Laws Ch. 48 was unconstitutional insofar as it authorized a county to issue general obligation bonds for the purpose of equipping a county hospital and isolation wards, and for the purchase of necessary land therefor. The court held the phrase "erecting necessary public buildings" as used in N.M. Const. art. 9, § 10 included within its purview the construction of a county hospital with isolation ward, equipping such hospital and isolation ward, and acquiring the land therefor. It was the court's duty to interpret the constitution to carry out the constitution, not giving it an overly technical reading to destroy what was intended. The power to erect a necessary public building included the implied power to purchase the necessary land on which to erect it, and to equip it so that it could be used for the purpose for which it is built.


OUTCOME: The court issued the relief requested and made the writ permanent.

Black Hawk Consol. Mines Co. v. Gallegos


No. 5044


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


52 N.M. 74; 1948-NMSC-007; 191 P.2d 996; 1948 N.M. LEXIS 623



March 5, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 23, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Sante Fe County; William J. Barker, Judge.

Action by Black Hawk Consolidated Mines Company against J. O. Gallegos, as Commissioner of Revenue of the Bureau of Revenue of the State of New Mexico, to recover money paid under protest as a tax for the privilege of doing a mining business within the state. From a decree of dismissal, the plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mining company appealed a decree of the District Court, Sante Fe County (New Mexico), which dismissed its action against defendant commissioner of revenue to recover money paid under protest as a tax. The tax was imposed by the Emergency School Tax Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 76-1404 (1941), for the privilege of doing a mining business within the state.


OVERVIEW: The mining company operated a gold mine. Pursuant to federal law, all of the gold it mined was sold to the United States mint in Colorado. The mining company sought a refund of taxes it paid pursuant to the Emergency School Tax Act, which imposed a tax for the privilege of doing a mining business within the state. The tax was based on the gross receipts of the mine. The trial court dismissed the mining company's action. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) the tax was constitutional because it was not a direct tax on interstate commerce, and it did not unduly burden interstate commerce; (2) the tax did not constitute a burden upon or an interference with the United States' authority to coin money or regulate the value of money: (3) neither the Gold Reserve Act of 1934, 48 Stat. 337, or U.S. Const. art. I, § 8 deprived the state of its power to tax the gold mine; and (4) N.M. Const. art. 4, § 15 was not violated by an amendment to the original bill in the legislature because the amendment did not change the original purpose of the bill.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entered in favor of the commissioner in the mining company's action for a tax refund.

 

424 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Prince


No. 5054


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


52 N.M. 15; 1948-NMSC-003; 189 P.2d 993; 1948 N.M. LEXIS 615



January 7, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 2, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Error to District Court, Bernalillo County; Albert R. Kool, Judge.

Lewis Prince was charged with embezzlement, and to review an order sustaining a motion to quash the information, the State brings error.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of embezzlement, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4519 (1941); the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico) sustained a motion to quash the information; and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Section 41-4519 provided that any person in the possession of the property of another, who converted such property to his own use, was guilty of embezzlement. It expressly repealed a prior statute that provided that a person who fraudulently converted property that had been entrusted to him to his own use was guilty of larceny. The information charged that defendant fraudulently converted money with which he had been entrusted, which did not belong to him. The information was quashed as unconstitutional and void, and defendant was released. On review, the court first concluded that § 41-4519 was unconstitutional because it did not refer to entrustment and fraudulent appropriation, which were essential elements of embezzlement. However, the court then held that because § 41-4519 failed in its purpose to define the crime of embezzlement, its repealing clause failed as well, and the previous statute remained in effect. Furthermore, the information sufficiently advised defendant of the offense charged. Therefore, the court held that the trial court erred in dismissing defendant, reversed the trial court's judgment, and directed the trial court to reinstate the case on its docket.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, with directions to the trial court to reinstate the case on its docket.

Lyman v. Kern


Docket No. 19,771


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


128 N.M. 582; 2000-NMCA-013; 995 P.2d 504; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 149; 39 N.M. St. B. Bull. 8



December 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 15, 2000. Certiorari Denied, No. 26,150, February 11, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY. Alvin F. Jones, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a Chaves County District Court (New Mexico) order compelling the parties to arbitrate based on a stipulation between the parties in plaintiff's negligence action.


OVERVIEW: After entry of a binding arbitration award, defendants appealed the order compelling the arbitration, which was based on the parties' oral stipulation to arbitrate plaintiff's negligence action. Defendants argued that the order to arbitrate was not final because they did not agree to binding arbitration and that the order was unconstitutional because it deprived them of their right to a jury trial. The court dismissed the appeal, which was filed 16 months after entry of the arbitration order. The trial court delegated resolution of the merits to the arbitration process, divesting itself of any further power to address the issues of law or fact presented by the case, rendering the order final and only appealable within 30 days of its entry. Because the order was final, defendants were also obligated to appeal to preserve their right to jury trial.


OUTCOME: Appeal was dismissed. Order compelling arbitration was a final order from which defendants failed to timely appeal within 30 days, postponing their appeal until after an arbitration award was rendered against them. Defendants' failure to timely appeal also resulted in a waiver of their right to jury trial.

In re Christopher K.


Docket No. 20,612


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


128 N.M. 406; 1999-NMCA-157; 993 P.2d 120; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 135; 39 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1



November 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. T. GLENN ELLINGTON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child appealed the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which held that he could not withdraw his request for a jury trial without the concurrence of appellee state in his delinquency action, and scheduled the matter for trial before a jury.


OVERVIEW: In his juvenile delinquency action, appellant, the child, sought to withdraw his request for a jury trial. The trial court denied his request, holding that the concurrence of appellee, the state, was required. Appellant challenged, arguing that the concurrence of appellee was not necessary. Appellee was not entitled to demand a jury trial in a delinquency proceeding, since N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32A-2-16(A) (1993) did not list appellee along with those who may demand a jury trial. Neither § 32A-2-16(A) nor N.M. Child Ct. R. 10-228 (1999) afforded appellee the right to concur or object to appellant's waiver of a jury trial. Nor did N.M. Const. art. II, § 12 require that appellee concur with the waiver, since state courts had consistently held that a juvenile could waive a jury trial without ever suggesting that appellee had a constitutional right to concur.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, because appellant should have been permitted to withdraw his request for a jury trial without the concurrence of appellee, since appellee had no right provided by any state statute, court rule, or the state constitution to require its concurrence to that waiver.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted defendant of bribery or intimidation of a witness, under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-24-3(A)(3) (1997), and misdemeanor criminal sexual contact.


OVERVIEW: At earlier trial, defendant disputed whether he held a knife to the victim's throat, hit her on the head, threw the phone at her, or did other things alleged in indictment against him. The court also held the statute to be constitutional and found sufficient evidence to convict defendant.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed, because the trial court did not submit special verdict forms to the jury, defendant was acquitted of all the felony charges except threatening a witness, and it was impossible to determine whether the jury found each of the essential elements of threatening a witness.

Hughes v. Timberon Water & Sanitation Dist.


Docket No. 19,922


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


128 N.M. 186; 1999-NMCA-136; 991 P.2d 16; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 108; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 48



August 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied, No. 25,956, October 12, 1999.
Released for Publication October 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY. Ralph W. Gallini, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners within water and sanitation district, challenged order of District Court of Otero County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment to appellees, water and sanitation district and its directors, in appellants' action to enforce alleged statutory right to vote in district elections, N. M. Stat. Ann. § 73-21-4(D).


OVERVIEW: Court interpreted N.M. Stat. Ann. § 73-21-4(D) to mean that a "taxpaying elector of a district" must be a resident of the district because this interpretation was consistent with the current election laws, the election laws in effect at the time the statutory provision was adopted, and the election requirements of the Water and Sanitation District Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 73-21-1 to 73-21-54. Court concluded that the most reasonable construction of the statutory language was that only residents of the district were permitted to vote in district elections. Court noted that this interpretation would enable the court to avoid potentially troublesome constitutional issues under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.M. Const. art. VII, § 1, although the court concluded that this consideration was not determinative of the case.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed because interpreting "taxpaying elector of the district" to mean that only residents of district were permitted to vote in district elections was consistent with current elections laws, election laws in effect at time statutory provision enacted, and Water and Sanitation District Act.

 

430 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Rivera v. Trujillo


Docket No. 19,403


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


128 N.M. 106; 1999-NMCA-129; 990 P.2d 219; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 98; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 41



July 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Denied September 13, 1999. Released for Publication October 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF RIO ARRIBA COUNTY. Steve Herrera, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order from the District Court of Rio Arriba County (New Mexico) denying plaintiff's motion for reconsideration of defendants' summary judgment motion in an auto negligence suit. Plaintiffs claimed the trial court erred in finding plaintiff driver caused the accident due to his loss of consciousness prior to impact, and in failing to accept plaintiffs' evidence disputing the blackout.


OVERVIEW: The court held that plaintiffs' auto negligence suit was properly dismissed where plaintiff driver's depositional testimony proved plaintiff driver's blackout prior to impact proximately caused the accident, and where plaintiffs' summary judgment evidence was rejected as untimely and unverified. Plaintiff driver was injured in auto accident involving defendant trucking company's truck. On defendants' motion for summary judgment, plaintiff driver presented his affidavit alleging he did not blackout prior to the accident, but suffered a loss of memory regarding the accident. Plaintiff driver also submitted a police report to this effect. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendants, determining that plaintiff driver's blackout proximately caused the accident. Plaintiffs brought a motion to reconsider, which the trial court denied. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court properly excluded plaintiff driver's affidavit and the police report where they were untimely submitted and the police report was unverified. As admission of the untimely deposition testimony would not change the result, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting defendants' motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of reconsideration of its grant of summary judgment to defendants in an auto negligence action. Where plaintiff driver's deposition testimony proved plaintiff driver blacked-out prior to impact and proximately caused the accident, dismissal was proper. A police report and plaintiff driver's affidavit disputing the blackout was properly rejected, where the evidence was untimely and unverified.

 

431 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Cockrell v. Bd. of Regents


Docket No. 19,417


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 478; 1999-NMCA-073; 983 P.2d 427; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 41; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 24



May 7, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF DONA ANA COUNTY. Robert E. Robles, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order denying Paul summary judgment on the ground of qualified immunity reversed. Remanded for entry of summary judgment to that effect and for further proceedings on Cockrell's other claims.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court of Doda Ana County (New Mexico) denying defendant summary judgment on the ground of qualified immunity in plaintiff's suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 alleging a breach of implied contract and a deprivation of a property interest without due process of law.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff took an emergency position with a state university as a basketball coach. A year later, plaintiff re-applied and was rehired in the same position. Plaintiff did not have an express, written contract of employment, but instead claimed certain rights as an employee under the employment manual. The key dispute was whether plaintiff was still a probationary employee at the time of his termination. A decision denying summary judgment to defendant athletic director on the ground of qualified immunity in plaintiff's suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was reversed and remanded. Plaintiff did not have a clearly established right to continued employment. He was hired under emergency procedures designed to fill an urgent need. There was nothing in the manual providing a probationary period for emergency hires or clearly indicating that the two overlapped. Defendant may reasonably have been entitled to believe that plaintiff's time as an emergency hire did not eliminate the need for a probationary status. Individual provisions within the manual were arguably inconsistent and contradictory. Affidavits did not create a genuine issue of material fact sufficient to defeat summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for entry of summary judgment on defendant's qualified immunity claim because plaintiff's alleged property interest in continued employment under the employment manual was not clearly established at the time of his discharge.

 

432 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Pinnell v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


Docket No. 18,831


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 452; 1999-NMCA-074; 982 P.2d 503; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 44; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 25



May 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 8, 1999. As Corrected June 24, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. Steve Herrera, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Decision of trial court dismissing Plaintiffs' complaint affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of a decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) dismissing plaintiffs' complaint for declaratory and permanent injunctive relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, claiming a violation of their rights to equal protection as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were elected members of a five-member board that had passed a resolution that one board member would be elected the chair and vote only in a tie. Plaintiffs were constituents of the chair when defendants considered a proposal to grant a variance to construct a parking lot. One member did not vote and the vote passed two-to-one without needing the vote of the chair. Had the chair been permitted to vote on the matter, the vote would have been two-to-two and the variances would not have been approved. A decision dismissing plaintiffs' suit alleging that the voting resolution violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV was affirmed. Defendants failed to show that the suit was dismissed for failure to join an indispensable party. The resolution lacked any obvious discriminatory purpose. Plaintiffs demonstrated no severe restriction upon their fundamental rights. There was no evidence that the classification burdened a sensitive but not suspect class. The rule imposed only reasonable, nondiscriminatory restrictions. The resolution allowed the business of county government to be conducted in an organized and efficient manner. This was a legitimate governmental purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiffs' complaint because the claim was not dismissed on joinder grounds and defendants' resolution was reasonably related to a legitimate state interest.
