State v. Dawson


Docket No. 19,409


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 472; 1999-NMCA-072; 983 P.2d 421; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 43; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 24



April 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] June 25, 1999. Released for Publication June 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Albert S. "Pat" Murdoch, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence of district court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) which convicted him of concealing identity in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-3 (1963).


OVERVIEW: After criminal defendant was convicted of concealing identity in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-3 (1963), he appealed. On appeal, the court consolidated defendant's variety of issues into four groups: (1) whether the district court correctly interpreted the requirements of § 30-22-3; (2) whether there was sufficient evidence to convict; (3) whether his constitutional rights were violated; and (4) whether jurisdiction was proper. The court affirmed conviction and sentence because the law required a person to show identification or, if he had reasonable concern as to the validity of the request, to show identification so soon as not to cause substantial inconvenience or expense to the police. The evidence sufficed for the trial court to find that officers were acting in the legal performance of their duties. The court noted that shortcomings in the discovery process did not affect jurisdiction. To the extent that defendant believed that § 30-22-3 was vague in other respects, he failed to elaborate on his challenge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed conviction and sentence because the law required a person to show identification or, if he had reasonable concern as to the validity of the request, to show identification so soon as not to cause substantial inconvenience or expense to the police.

 

434 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dawson


Docket No. 19,409


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 472; 1999-NMCA-072; 983 P.2d 421; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 67



April 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Albert S. "Pat" Murdoch, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) that convicted defendant of concealing identity, under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-3 (1963).


OVERVIEW: University police noticed defendant's camper parked on university property. The officers approached the vehicle, identified themselves, and intended to ask defendant to remove the vehicle from university property. Defendant refused to identify himself. Defendant continued to refuse to identify himself after several requests from several officers. Eventually, defendant provided his full name. Subsequently, defendant was convicted for concealing identity, under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-3, based on defendant's delay in providing his name. The appellate court held that § 30-22-3 required defendant to provide identifying information immediately or so soon after determining the validity of the request so that no substantial inconvenience or expense to the police was caused. In addition, the appellate court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the finding that defendant refused to identify himself, that defendant had the requisite intent, under § 30-22-3, and that the officers were acting within the legal performance of their duties. Furthermore, defendant's constitutional vagueness challenge was not preserved for review. Therefore, defendant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction for concealing identity because there was sufficient evidence that defendant refused to identify himself to officers, that defendant had the requisite intent to violate the statute, and that the officers were acting within the legal performance of their duties.

 

435 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Ramah Navajo Sch. Bd., Inc. v. N.M. Taxation & Revenue Dep't


Docket No. 18,909


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 101; 1999-NMCA-050; 977 P.2d 1021; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 20



March 4, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied, No. 25,667, April 8, 1999, Certiorari Denied, No. 25,671, April 12, 1999. Released for Publication April 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. Steve Herrera, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court's judgment reversed. Remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), denying their request for a refund of gasoline taxes under the Indian Self-Determination and Education Assistance Act of 1975, 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 450-458.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a Native American school board and two private gasoline distributors, sought review of the denial of their request for a refund of state gas taxes. Appellants brought their suit under the Indian Self-Determination and Education Assistance Act of 1975 (Act), 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 450-458, claiming that the statute preempted a state gas tax law. The lower court denied appellants a refund of the gas taxes. The appellate court found that the Act did not specifically preempt the state gas taxes, but that the taxes were preempted by virtue of the fact that the state law would not impose the taxes on a federal agency performing the same services as appellant school board. The court found that the purpose of the Act was to permit Native American tribes to take over the education of tribal children from the federal government. As such, appellant school board was entitled to the same exemption from taxation as the federal government. The court therefore reversed the lower court and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was reversed, and the court remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with its opinion. The court found the appellants were entitled to a refund of the gasoline taxes because preemption could be implied under the circumstances, although the state gas tax law was not specifically preempted by federal law.

Hart v. City of Albuquerque


Docket No. 19,026


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


126 N.M. 753; 1999-NMCA-043; 975 P.2d 366; 1999 N.M. App. LEXIS 9; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 14



January 21, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. W. DANIEL SCHNEIDER, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed the decision of the district court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which ordered appellant to grant appellee's requested zoning change from residential to commercial and found that appellant's decision denying the zoning change was not supported by substantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed a judgment which ordered appellant city to grant appellee's requested zoning change from residential to commercial. The district court found that appellant's decision to deny the requested zoning change was not supported by substantial evidence and thereafter issued a writ of mandamus ordering appellant to determine a new zoning category for the lots at issue. Appellant contended on appeal that the district court exceeded its scope of review for a zoning appeal and that substantial evidence supported its zoning decision. The court agreed, holding that the district court was not authorized to overturn a rejection of a petition for a zoning change and then order appellant to rezone. In particular, a district court could not prescribe what zoning would be applied to a particular property. Further, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-21-9(D) was unconstitutional to the extent that it purported to allow a district court to zone land. Finally, the district court could not issue a writ of mandamus to interfere with appellant's legitimate exercise of its authority to act on the application after the district court reversed appellant's zoning decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment which ordered appellant city to grant appellee's requested zoning change from residential to commercial because the district court exceeded its scope of review in ordering the zoning change and erred in issuing a writ of mandamus. Finally, substantial evidence supported appellant's denial of the zone map amendment.

 

437 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Snyder


Docket No. 18,661


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


126 N.M. 168; 1998-NMCA-166; 967 P.2d 843; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 146; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 49



September 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied No. 25,407, November 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY. Frank K. Wilson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. The District Court of Otero County (New Mexico) denied his motion to suppress evidence seized as a result of a warrantless search of his automobile by agents of the United States Border Patrol at a fixed checkpoint in the state and convicted him of the charge. Defendant sought review of the denial of his motion to suppress and the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the failure to exclude the evidence violated his rights under N.M. Const. art. II, § 10 because the state failed to make a particularized showing of exigent circumstances. The state asserted that there was no state action. The court held that under N.M. Const. art. II, § 10, the requirement of exigent circumstances for a warrantless vehicle search applied to a federal border patrol agent's search at a state checkpoint. The court also held that it would defer to the border patrol agent's judgment if reasonable people might differ about whether exigent circumstances were present. Defendant claimed that there were no exigent circumstances because his person and his vehicle could have been secured while the agents sought a search warrant. The court rejected this argument because physically restraining defendant pending the issuance of a search warrant would not be any less intrusive than conducting an immediate search and because an extended investigatory stop could become a suspect de facto arrest. The court held that there was an objectively reasonable basis for the agents to believe that there were exigent circumstances justifying the warrantless search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the motion to suppress the evidence and the defendant's conviction for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute.

State v. Duran


Docket No. 18,787


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


126 N.M. 60; 1998-NMCA-153; 966 P.2d 768; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 130; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 45



August 18, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied No. 25,353, October 13, 1998. Released for Publication October 23, 1998. As Corrected November 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. ALBERT S. "PAT" MURDOCH, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded in part for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment and sentence of the District Court Of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted defendant of stalking, harassment, and two counts of criminal trespass.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for stalking and a separate charge of harassment; and the same pattern of conduct was used to prove both crimes. The issues on appeal were: (1) whether defendant's convictions for stalking and harassment violated double jeopardy; (2) whether the criminal harassment statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-3A-2 (1993), was unconstitutionally vague; (3) whether the convictions were supported by sufficient evidence; and (4) whether he was denied due process of law because of the trial judge's alleged bias. The court reversed the convictions in part. In so ruling, the court determined that (1) a comparison of the offenses of harassment and stalking had failed to clearly indicate that the legislature intended that the same unitary conduct underlying the charges of harassment and stalking be punished as distinct offenses; and (2) the intent required to be proven for both crimes overlapped in part. The court concluded that the harassment offense was subsumed into the misdemeanor stalking offense. On remand, the court directed the trial court to resentence defendant. The court found that no other reversible error was committed and the convictions were otherwise affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions of stalking, harassment, and two counts of criminal trespass were affirmed in part. However, the cause was remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate the judgment and sentence and to resentence defendant consistent with the matters set forth in the opinion.

Bonito Land & Livestock, Inc. v. Valencia County Bd. of Comm'r


Docket No. 18,723


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 638; 1998-NMCA-127; 964 P.2d 199; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 108; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 41



August 11, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF VALENCIA COUNTY. William A. Sanchez, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of an order from the District Court of Valencia County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant county. After the county denied the property owner's application for a use permit allowing mineral extraction, the property owner had filed a complaint seeking a declaratory judgment that it could use its property free of the county's purported zoning.


OVERVIEW: The county adopted a zoning ordinance at the time the land in question was owned and managed by the United States, prohibiting the land from being used for mineral extraction activities. The land was later conveyed to the property owner, which filed a complaint seeking a declaratory judgment that the land was not zoned. The trial court granted the county's motion for summary judgment, ruling that the ordinance applied to the land. On appeal, the court reversed. The court noted that the county had the power to zone federally-owned land. However, the ordinance in question excluded land owned by the state or federal government. The county conceded that it only intended to zone privately-owned land when it adopted the ordinance. The court rejected the county's argument that when the land passed into private ownership the ordinance took effect. The court held that the land became unzoned when it became private property. In order to zone it, the county had to meet the notice requirements of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-21-6(B). The original notice was not adequate to apprise the average citizen that the county intended the ordinance to apply to federally-owned land that passed into private hands.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the county in the property owner's complaint seeking a declaratory judgment that its land was not subject to a zoning ordinance, and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Jutte


Docket No. 18,572


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


126 N.M. 244; 1998-NMCA-150; 968 P.2d 334; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 129; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 45



August 11, 1998, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY. William P. Lynch, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico) which denied his motion to suppress evidence and convicted him for possession of illegal drugs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was detained at a roadside weigh station for a routine regulatory stop. The truck he was driving had no commercial load, but the inspector detained defendant because he was suspicious that items in the truck may have been stolen and that drugs may have been in the truck. The inspector held defendant until drug dogs arrived, obtained a consent to search from defendant, and found drugs. Defendant's motion to suppress the evidence at trial was denied and he was convicted. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that it was error to deny the motion to dismiss because the regulatory stop constituted a de facto arrest due to the unreasonable delay of one hour while the inspectors were awaiting the drug dogs. The court found that the de facto arrest tainted the consent to search and made the search illegal. The court held that the evidence should have been suppressed under the doctrine of the fruit of the poisonous tree.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction, held that it was error to deny defendant's motion to suppress evidence, and remanded for further proceedings.

Khalsa v. Levinson


Docket No. 18,211


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 680; 1998-NMCA-110; 964 P.2d 844; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 92



July 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 12, 1998. As Corrected November 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. MICHAEL E. VIGIL, Successor District Judge.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which found that appellee mother was entitled to an award of attorney fees and costs and which rejected the father's claims that he had no duty to consult with the mother concerning their children and that the mother was responsible for child support. Both parties alleged that the trial court's custody and support order was final.


OVERVIEW: A final decree between the father and the mother was entered by the trial court incorporating the provisions of a marital settlement agreement, including specific religious lifestyle provisions. One year later, the mother sought a modification of the custody arrangement, sanctions, and attorney fees. Although there were numerous subsequent motions between the parties raising new issues and requesting new relief, the trial court only entered two subsequent orders - the final of which was under appeal. The court dismissed the appeal and ruled that it lacked jurisdiction over the case. The court found that the appealed order, although designated as "final and appealable" and containing findings of facts and conclusions of law, did not contain required decretal language or provisions directing the entry of judgment. Moreover, the order did not address a number of claims raised in the parties' motions. Because the resolved claims were so intertwined with the issues held in abeyance and remaining to be resolved and because the order was not designated as a N.M. R. Civ. P. Dist. Ct. 1-054(C)(1) "no just reason for delay" appeal, appellate review was premature.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the father's appeal for lack of jurisdiction over the trial court's decision that was not yet final. The court remanded the case back to the trial court to adjudicate all unresolved issues. The court suggested appointing a special master and directed the trial court to review the authority for the trial court's appointment of a case manager and an evidence expert.

Hannahs v. Anderson


Docket Nos. 17,898 & 18,908

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied No. 25,358, October 13, 1998. Released of Publication October 23, 1998. As Amended November 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE BERNALILLO COUNTY VALUATION PROTESTS BOARD. FARES MARTINEZ, Chairperson.



DISPOSITION: Decisions of the Board affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of decisions from the Bernalillo County Valuation Protests Board (board) (New Mexico), which denied the taxpayers' protests of the assessed value placed upon their lot by appellee tax assessor. The taxpayers also challenge the board's decisions as to sanctions against the assessor for the denial of their discovery request for information on lot sizes and valuations of other lots within their subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers challenged the assessed value placed upon their lot for two tax years. They claimed that the tax assessor's denial of their discovery request required sanctions. The board ordered that no change be made in the valuation records and sanctioned the tax assessor as to one of the two tax years. The court affirmed the board's decisions against the taxpayers. The court further held that the taxpayers were not prejudiced by the tax assessor's refusal to comply with their discovery request. The court held that there was substantial evidence to support the board's findings that the taxpayers were not entitled to a change in the property valuation. The court also held that the taxpayers did not show that the valuation amounted to an intentional and arbitrary discrimination in violation of N.M. Const. art. VIII, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's decisions with respect to the taxpayers' protests of the assessed value placed upon their lot and their claim for sanctions against the tax assessor.

Christian Child Placement Serv. of the N.M. Christian Children's Home v. Vestal


Docket No. 19,036


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 426; 1998-NMCA-098; 962 P.2d 1261; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 81; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 34



June 9, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF ROOSEVELT COUNTY. ROBERT BRACK, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Roosevelt County (New Mexico) granted summary judgment to petitioner child service's agency in its action against respondent father for termination of his parental rights. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father pleaded guilty to criminal sexual penetration of a child. The victim gave birth to a baby girl and executed a relinquishment and consent to adoption. Subsequently, the agency filed a petition to terminate the father's parental rights. The trial court granted summary judgment to the agency. On appeal, the court found that the father did not acquire a fundamental right to withhold consent to the adoption because he committed criminal sexual penetration of a minor. The court determined that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32A-5-19(C) was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in protecting children and preventing their exploitation. The court held that the father was not entitled to a evidentiary hearing because there was no requirement for obtaining the consent of a biological father of a child conceived as a result of rape. The court also held that the father had no standing to assert that his parents (the paternal grandparents) were not provided with notice of the proceedings to terminate his parental rights. The court concluded that the father failed to demonstrate the existence of any material, disputed factual issues which would preclude an award of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order issuing summary judgment to the agency.

 

444 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Educ. v. Johnson


Docket No. 18,721


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 91; 1998-NMCA-048; 957 P.2d 76; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 20; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 14



February 25, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANDOVAL COUNTY. Kenneth G. Brown, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed and cross-appeal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trustee sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Sandoval County (New Mexico), which awarded the trustee compensation from appellee school district in a condemnation proceeding. The trustee maintained that he was not prejudiced by accepting the amount tendered and was entitled to an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The school district filed a petition in the trial court to condemn certain property. A trust owned a portion of the land sought by the school district. The trustee challenged the adequacy of the condemnation offer, and the trial court awarded the trust an additional amount. Although the trustee accepted a check payable to the trust, the trustee appealed the judgment, and the school district cross-appealed. Upon review, the court denied the trustee's appeal and affirmed the school district's cross-appeal. The court held that none of the exceptions to the general rule that a party waived his right to appeal when he accepted the benefits of a judgment applied to the trustee because, when the trustee accepted the full amount of the judgment and not just the advance deposit made by the school district, the trustee waived his right to appeal under § 42-2-6(B). The court stated that the statute's language regarding "advance deposits" did not apply to the final judgment. The court found that delivery of a cashier's check was for payment in full and that the school district had no cause to move to dismiss the trustee's appeal until the trustee actually filed his notice of appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the trustee's appeal and affirmed the school district's cross-appeal.

Kennedy v. Dexter Consol. Sch.


Docket No. 17,710


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 764; 1998-NMCA-051; 955 P.2d 693; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 23; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 15



February 3, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Granted, No. 24,995, April 2, 1998. Released for Publication April 2, 1998. As Corrected April 14, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY. R. W. GALLINI, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed judgment against Dexter Consolidated Schools. Reversed judgment against Kent Perry for compensatory and punitive damages. Reversed judgment in favor of Randy Ford against James Derrick. Reversed award of punitive damages to Crystal Kennedy against Sue Rodriguez. Reversed judgments against Donald Warren for compensatory and punitive damages, judgment against Sue Rodriguez for compensatory damages, and judgment in favor of Kennedy against Derrick. Remanded for retrial of those claims. Reversed award of attorney's fees and remand for further proceedings in that regard.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, school district and school officials, sought review of the decision of the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), which entered judgment in favor of appellee students in students' action for damages under the federal Civil Rights Act of 1871, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: A student at school within the school district complained that her ring was missing. School officials conducted strip searches of two students, one of which required the student to be partially nude, and the other required the student to strip to his undergarments. Students filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action for damages. The trial court found in favor of the students, and awarded compensatory and punitive damages. School officials appealed, arguing they were precluded from judgment because of qualified immunity. The school district appealed, arguing that insufficient evidence and evidentiary errors warranted reversal of the trial court's judgment. The court held that the judgment entered against the school district was proper because it should have known that its custom of strip searching its students without individualized reasonable suspicion was improper and that it should have trained its employees to conduct searches only after a determination of individualized reasonable suspicion. As for the school officials, the court held that they could be relieved of liability if their conduct did not violate clearly established rights of which a reasonable person would have known.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court in part, reversed the decision of the district court in part, and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

446 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Trambley v. Wyman


Docket No. 18,473


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 13; 1998-NMCA-035; 956 P.2d 144; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 11; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 12



January 26, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 18, 1998. Released for Publication February 25, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. W. Daniel Schneider, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lawyer sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which affirmed the judgment against him by the metropolitan court in favor of plaintiff court reporter. The court reporter brought this action under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 36-2-13.1(A) (1993) to recover court reporter fees incurred by the lawyer's client in a separate proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered judgment against the lawyer in this action in which the court reporter sought recovery under § 36-2-13.1(A) of attorney fees incurred by the lawyer's client in a separate proceeding. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment against the lawyer. The court held that the act of making arrangements to pay a court reporter for deposition services did not involve the rendering of a service that required the use of legal knowledge or skill and therefore the statute did not unconstitutionally regulate the practice of law. The court held that § 36-2-13.1(A) did not conflict with attorney rule of conduct, N.M. R. Prof. Conduct 16-108(E)(1) (1997), which provided that the client was ultimately liable for the costs and expenses of litigation. The court held that there was no conflict of interest involved in the lawyer's subsequent action to recover these fees from the client. Finally, the court held that the client was not an indispensable party in the original action because the lawyer and client were jointly and severally liable for the court reporter fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the lawyer for court reporter costs incurred by the lawyer's client in a separate proceeding.

 

447 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Ortiz v. Taxation & Revenue Dep't., Motor Vehicle Div.


Docket No. 18,127


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 677; 1998-NMCA-027; 954 P.2d 109; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 7; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 12



January 21, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. STEVE HERRERA, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Taxation and Revenue's Motor Vehicle Division (department) sought review of the decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which overturned the department's revocation of appellee client's driver's license.


OVERVIEW: The client retained an attorney to represent him in a driver's license revocation proceeding before the department. Because the attorney was a former department employee, his representation of the client violated N.M. Stat. Ann. § 10-16-8(C). The client proceeded pro se. The department revoked the client's driver's license. The district court overturned the revocation on the ground that § 10-16-8(C) was an unconstitutional usurpation of the judiciary's authority to regulate the conduct of attorneys. On appeal, the court reversed the decision, holding that § 10-16-8(C) did not violate separation of powers principles. Section 10-16-8(C) prohibited a former government employee from representing persons before his former employer for pay for a period of one year. The court found that the statute was rationally related to the state's interest of enhancing public trust by prohibiting any conflicts of interest. Further, the court held that attorneys were not expressly excluded from the definition of public employee. The court also held that N.M. Rules of Prof. Conduct 16-111 was not a bar because attorneys were subject to Rule 16-111 and other statutes concerning conflicts of interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's decision, and directed the district court to affirm the department's revocation of the client's driver's license.

 

448 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Hennessy v. Duryea


Docket No. 17,317


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 754; 1998-NMCA-036; 955 P.2d 683; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 10; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 11



January 14, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 18, 1998. Released for Publication February 25, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Theresa Baca, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) entered an order awarding a share of respondent husband's military retirement pay to petitioner wife. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband served in the military during their marriage and retired therefrom fifteen years subsequent to the parties' divorce. The divorce decree divided property but was silent as to military retirement benefits. After the husband retired, the wife petitioned the trial court to divide what she alleged was her undivided community interest in the military retirement pay that her husband was then receiving. The basis for the wife's action was N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-4-20, which provided a party the right to seek a division and distribution of previously undivided property in a separate proceeding after the divorce. The court reversed. The court found that the Uniform Services Former Spouses' Protection Act barred the application of state law in cases where a divorce decree, entered prior to a particular U. S. Supreme Court decision, did not contain specific language that treated, or reserved jurisdiction to treat, military retirement pay as the property of a service member and his former spouse. Thus, the wife could not utilize § 40-4-20 to obtain a share of the military pension because the parties' final decree of divorce was entered prior to the Supreme Court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's order.

Mark D. v. Mun. Boundary Comm'n


Docket No. 17,823


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 709; 1998-NMCA-025; 954 P.2d 1186; 1998 N.M. App. LEXIS 3; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 10



January 13, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. Steve Herrera, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, Municipal Boundary Commission (commission) and city, appealed an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which directed that the commission hold a new hearing with new notice under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-7-14(B) (1965) regarding the annexation of land sought by the city and challenged by petitioner residents.


OVERVIEW: The residents claimed that the commission's hearing to consider annexation was improper because the commission did not publish notice as set forth in the general definitional section of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-1-2(J) (1987) and did not have the necessary quorum due the recusal of its only attorney commissioner. The court reversed the order for a new hearing after determining that the order was appealable under the doctrine of practical finality, and affirmed the commission's decision to annex. The court found that the commission gave adequate notice because it complied with the specific notice statute of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-7-14(B) (1965). The specific statute was controlling over the general statute and was consistent with the legislative purpose of extending notice to persons who lived outside the municipality's boundaries, but likely had an interest in the proposed annexation. The court also found that the commission acted with a proper quorum because under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-7-12(A), any two members constituted a majority and thus a quorum of the three-member commission.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that directed the commission to hold a new hearing and affirmed the commission's proceedings, which had granted the city's petition for annexation.

Chisholm v. Rueckhaus


Docket No. 17,444


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 255; 1997-NMCA-112; 948 P.2d 707; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 98; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 49



October 10, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. SUSAN M. CONWAY, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, father of minor child who was injured during birth, brought a medical malpractice action pro se on behalf of his child. Defendant, New Mexico Medical Review Commission screening panel, required that he be represented by counsel. The father filed a declaratory judgment action in the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which was denied in a letter-decision. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Medical Malpractice Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-5-1 to 29 (1976, as amended through 1992) (Act), the father submitted a written application to the panel regarding his intention to bring a medical malpractice action, pro se, against certain health care providers. OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the trial court's denial of the father's request for a declaratory judgment.

State v. Crain


Docket No. 16,463


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 84; 1997-NMCA-101; 946 P.2d 1095; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 89; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 45



August 13, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Cert. denied, SC24,654, September 30, 1997. Released for Publication October 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. W. John Brennan, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions entered by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) for kidnapping and two alternative counts of criminal sexual penetration in the second degree (CSP II).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's theory at trial was that the entire act of sexual intercourse was consensual because defendant promptly and voluntarily withdrew from the victim when she began to say "Daddy, Daddy." On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in its jury instructions for the crime of CSP II, that defendant was subjected to double jeopardy when he was sentenced to multiple punishments for the same offense, and that the cumulative errors of defendant's trial counsel deprived defendant of his right to effective assistance of counsel. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence for CSP II that resulted in personal injury, but it reversed the other convictions and remanded the case. In doing so, the court held that it was not persuaded that the legislature intended multiple punishments for the same offense or that the legislature intended to punish every CSP that resulted from force and restraint as a second-degree felony. Accordingly, the case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate defendant's conviction and sentence for kidnapping and CSP II in the commission of a kidnapping.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate defendant's conviction and sentence for kidnapping and CSP II in the commission of a kidnapping. Defendant's remaining conviction and sentence for CSP II resulting in personal injury was affirmed.

Welch v. Sandoval County Valuation Protests Bd.


Docket No. 17,850


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 722; 1997-NMCA-086; 945 P.2d 452; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 77; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 43



July 31, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Denied September 17, 1997. Released for Publication September 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SANDOVAL COUNTY VALUATION PROTESTS BOARD.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision of appellees, Sandoval County Valuation Protests Board (board) and Office of the Sandoval County Assessor, which held that the taxpayers' leasehold interest in the land was not exempt from taxation.


OVERVIEW: An Indian tribe, which was exempt from property tax, leased its land for 99 years to a corporation, which leased two lots to the taxpayers. The taxpayers claimed that they were exempt from property taxes, and the board rejected the taxpayers' claim. The taxpayers appealed, and the court affirmed the decision of the board. The court held that the master lease was not a fractional interest under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-36-4(A)(1) (1978) because the term of the lease was for more than 75 years. The court looked at the original term of the lease and not the time remaining under the lease. The court held that the classification under § 7-36-4 had a rational basis, which satisfied the constitutional requirements. The court ruled that the record established neither a disproportionate effect on Indians nor a discriminatory intent or purpose so there was no equal protection violation. The court held that the N.M. Stat. §§ 1048, 1069 (1905) did not apply because the leasehold interest was the property of the taxpayers. The court ruled that the state had the authority to tax the property of non-Indian lessees of Indian land, even if the property was located on the reservation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the board, which held that the taxpayers were not exempt from paying property taxes on the land, which was subject to a lease and on an Indian reservation.

Lucero v. Pino


Docket No. 17,748


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 28; 1997-NMCA-089; 946 P.2d 232; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 75; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 42

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY. Robert M. Doughty II, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a judgment of the District Court of Otero County (New Mexico) in favor of appellee father, which denied a motion under N.M. R. Civ. P. Dist. Ct. 1-060(B) to reopen an order under the Family Violence Protection Act (Protection Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 40-13-1 to 40-13-8, and an order dismissing her paternity action.


OVERVIEW: The mother was the subject of a Protection Act action brought by the father many months after an alleged minor incident. The district court nevertheless issued an order giving custody to the paternal grandmother. Later, while the mother was in custody as a delinquent, she filed a paternity action, which the district court dismissed as res judicata based on the Protection Act proceedings. The grandmother then sought to adopt the child. The mother filed a motion under N.M. R. Civ. P. Dist. Ct. 1-060(B) and contended that both orders were void. The court found the district court correct in not reopening the paternity order because considering that the district court had both personal and subject matter jurisdiction, the paternity order was not void, but merely erroneous for its res judicata determination.

Johnson v. Weast


Docket No. 17,005


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 470; 1997-NMCA-066; 943 P.2d 117; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 55; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 32



May 20, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied July 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Diane Dal Santo, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pharmacist filed an action against defendant drug inspector under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, the federal Civil Rights Act, alleging in part unlawful arrest, unlawful search and seizure, and violation of procedural due process. A jury verdict was rendered in favor of the pharmacist for violation of his civil rights. The drug inspector appealed.


OVERVIEW: The pharmacist spoke to a drug inspector requesting that he investigate what the pharmacist suspected were forged prescriptions. The drug inspector reviewed the pharmacist's prescription records looking for forgeries. The pharmacist fully cooperated with the inspector. The drug inspector confirmed 150 forged prescriptions. Although under state law the drug inspector had the power to make an arrest, he made no effort to place the pharmacist under arrest. The drug inspector was called to testify before the grand jury that subsequently indicted the pharmacist on a number of drug-related charges. All charges were later dismissed. The pharmacist filed suit against the drug inspector and the assistant district attorney under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The jury awarded the pharmacist damages for violation of his civil rights. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded with instructions to enter judgment for defendant. The court opined that the case, as presented to the jury, fell somewhere in between unconstitutional arrest and unconstitutional malicious prosecution. The court held that the case failed to satisfy either theory or to establish the deprivation of a right secured to the pharmacist.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and the case was remanded with instructions to enter judgment for defendant.

 

455 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arellano


Docket No. 16,758


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 589; 1997-NMCA-074; 943 P.2d 1042; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 61; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 33



May 12, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied, Sc24,410, 7/29/97. Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed June 3, 1997, granted July 28, 1997. Released for Publication August 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MORA COUNTY. Jay G. Harris, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision from the District Court of Mora County (New Mexico), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of criminal damage to property against her.


OVERVIEW: Upon her return home, defendant discovered that her husband had given two people permission to stay in her home. The state alleged that defendant chased the two people away with an ax and then broke the windows, windshield, and headlights and damaged the engine of their employer's pickup. The trial court dismissed the state's charge against defendant on the ground that defendant could only have been charged under a specific statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. §66-3-506 (1994), injuring or tampering with a vehicle, and not under a general statute, § 30-15-1 criminal damage to property. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held that § 30-15-1 did not include the same matter as § 66-3-506. Under § 30-15-1 the state had to prove that the amount of damage exceeded $ 1000. Under § 66-3-506 the state had to prove that the property damaged was a motor vehicle. Thus, each statute included an element that the other did not, and therefore, the general/specific rule was inapplicable. The court held that the state's ability to prosecute under either statute did not violate defendant's equal protection rights where each offense involved different elements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge against him of criminal damage to property.

State v. Kanikaynar


Docket No. 16,327


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 283; 1997-NMCA-036; 939 P.2d 1091; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 26; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 21



March 26, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Granted May 2, 1997. Released for Publication May 8, 1997. As Corrected May 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. JAMES F. BLACKMER, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) imposing an additional 60 days of confinement pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-8-102(F)(2) (1978 & Repl. Pamp. 1994), based on defendant's refusal to submit to a chemical breath alcohol test, following defendant's guilty plea to a charge of aggravated driving while intoxicated (DWI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated DWI. The basis for the aggravation was defendant's refusal to submit to a chemical test that would determine the alcohol concentration of his breath. The district court imposed a sentence that included an additional 60-day minimum mandatory confinement. He appealed the sentence contending that § 66-8-102(F)(2) was unconstitutional. The court disagreed and affirmed the district court's decision. The court held that the provision did not violate defendant's Sixth Amendment right to counsel because the issuance of a citation for DWI did not amount to the initiation of criminal proceedings in which presence of counsel was required. The court ruled that the right to refuse an alcohol test had no constitutional implications. Thus, the statutory penalty arising from a refusal to take the test did not offend notions of fairness and due process. The court concluded that defendant's failure to cooperate or give his assent to a breath test did not create a legal right where one otherwise did not exist.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court to impose an additional term of 60 days in sentencing defendant following his guilty plea to a charge of aggravated DWI.

City of Albuquerque v. Chavez


Docket No. 16,646


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 258; 1997-NMCA-034; 939 P.2d 1066; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 25; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 21



March 13, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ Certiorari Granted May 2, 1997. Released for Publication May 8, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Burt Cosgrove, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an employment matter, plaintiff city appealed an order of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which set aside decision of the city's personnel board that upheld the termination of defendant employee.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the proceedings before the city's hearing officer violated constitutional due process because the employee bore the burden of persuasion and was required to present his evidence first. The court held that due process was not violated by requiring the employee to present his evidence first or to bear the burden of production or persuasion in proceedings before the hearing officer. The court determined that it was not only permissible but necessary for the employee to bear the burden of presenting the facts he claimed mitigated or explained his behavior. Under the particular procedural facts of the case, the court concluded that the employee should bear the burden of producing that evidence and of persuading the hearing officer of its validity. The court further held that there was no violation of constitutional due process when a statute, ordinance, or rule provides that a public agency's decision to terminate or otherwise discipline an employee should be affirmed by a personnel board unless the employee persuaded the board that the agency decision was incorrect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order setting aside the personnel board's decision to terminate the employee and remanded the matter for consideration of the employee's other challenges to the personnel board's decision.

State ex rel. Dep't of Pub. Safety v. One 1986 Peterbilt Tractor


Docket No. 16,829


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 387; 1997-NMCA-050; 940 P.2d 1182; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 40; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 17



March 11, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Denied May 29, 1997. Released for Publication June 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. JAMES A. HALL, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) which found that a truck engine bearing an altered vehicle identification number was contraband and subject to forfeiture by appellee state police.


OVERVIEW: The driver drove his tractor and trailer into the port of entry for New Mexico. The locking pin/slider frame was not engaged on the vehicle. As a result, state personnel conducted a full safety check of the vehicle and determined that the engine number had been altered. The driver presented a bill of sale, title documents, and insurance. The state police impounded the engine as contraband pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-3-507 (1978). The trial court found that a truck engine bearing an altered vehicle identification number (VIN) was contraband and subject to forfeiture by the state police. The driver appealed and the court affirmed. The court held that under New Mexico law, the driver who was in possession of an engine having an altered VIN had the burden to overcome the presumption that the engine was contraband and as such subject to forfeiture to the state. The driver could not produce documents that provided evidence of his title to the engine through its intermediate owners to the manufacturer. The court held that § 66-3-507 constituted a valid exercise of the police power of the State of New Mexico, not directly interfering with or burdening interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that found a truck engine bearing an altered vehicle identification number was contraband and subject to forfeiture by the state police.

Las Cruces Prof'l Fire Fighters v. City of Las Cruces


Docket No. 17,415


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 239; 1997-NMCA-031; 938 P.2d 1384; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 20; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 18



February 19, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF DONA ANA COUNTY. JERALD A. VALENTINE, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee union complained that a directive constituted a practice prohibited by the Public Employee Bargaining Act (PEBA), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 10-7D-1 to -26 and the Las Cruces, N.M., Ordinance ch. 16.5 (1993) (ordinance). The local board of labor management relations (board) ruled in favor of the union. Appellant city sought review to the District Court of Dona Ana County (New Mexico), which affirmed the board's decision. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: A fire chief issued a directive forbidding union organizational activities in any fire department facility. The union complained that the directive was unconstitutional, and judgment was rendered in its favor. The city appealed and contended that the union's complaint to the board was untimely, the board's decision was incorrect, and the city did not receive a fair hearing before the board due to the bias of the board's chairperson. The court affirmed the decision of the district court. The court found that the filing of the complaint was timely and also agreed that "duty hours" was the time during which fire fighters were required to be performing job duties. If the city were to enforce the no-solicitation mandate of the ordinance as it interpreted the language, it would have been engaging in an employer practice ordinarily prohibited by the PEBA and by other provisions of the ordinance. Thus, the no-solicitation directive was not authorized by the ordinance and was a prohibited employer practice. The court found no impropriety in the chairman's questioning. The questions were intelligent, respectful, phrased in a fair manner, and pertinent to issues to be decided at the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that was in favor of the union.

 

461 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Andrews


Docket No. 16,528


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 95; 1997-NMCA-017; 934 P.2d 289; 1997 N.M. App. LEXIS 6; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 22



January 14, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Denied February 20, 1997. Released for Publication March 4, 1997. As Corrected June 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CURRY COUNTY. David W. Bonem, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which convicted him of concealing his identity in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-3 (1978, Repl. Pamp. 1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding and refused to produce a driver's license. The officer asked for his address, date of birth, and social security number, but defendant would only give his name. On appeal, defendant argued that this did not constitute concealing his identity under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-3 (1978, Repl. Pamp. 1994), that the evidence was insufficient, and that the statute was vague. The court affirmed the conviction. Because the statute made it an offense to conceal one's name or identity and because all drivers in New Mexico were required to carry driver's licenses, the court concluded that the officer could seek more than just defendant's name and could request the information contained on a driver's license. The court found substantial evidence that defendant was concealing his identity because a jury could have reasonably inferred from defendant's conduct that he intended to hinder the officer. Considering that the statute was sufficiently definite in the context of a motor vehicle stop and required proof of specific intent and that the statute limited the officer's inquiry, the court determined that the statute was not impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for concealing his identity.

 

462 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Carrillo v. Compusys, Inc.


Docket No. 17,101


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 720; 1997-NMCA-003; 930 P.2d 1172; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 101; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 5



November 21, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Denied January 10, 1997. Released for Publication January 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. R.E. Richards, Workers' Compensation Judge, Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the decision of the WCJ pro tem.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a worker who was claiming workers' compensation benefits, challenged the decision of the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Administration (WCA), which denied her benefits in a workers' compensation claim against appellee employer. The worker based her appeal on the argument that the Workers' Compensation Judge pro tempore (WCJ pro tem) did not have the authority to hear her case.


OVERVIEW: The worker was injured while working for the employer. After she was injured, but before she filed her workers' compensation claim, she began working for the WCA. Because she worked for the WCA, her case was reassigned to a mediator pro tem. The worker and the employer rejected a series of pro tem judges until finally one was appointed to which neither party objected. That pro tem judge issued a ruling dismissing the worker's claim. The worker argued that the WCA had neither the statutory nor constitutional authority to appoint a WCJ pro tem to hear her case. The court noted that, although the issue was not raised below, an argument regarding the lack of authority of a judge to hear a case was jurisdictional and could be raised at any time, even where the parties had stipulated to the appointment. The court held that where a WCA employee filed a complaint with the WCA, the Director had to appoint a pro tem judge to adjudicate the complaint. The court rejected the worker's argument that, under N.M. Const. art. VI, § 3, only the Supreme Court could appoint judges pro tem.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

463 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rosaire


Docket No. 16,474


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 250; 1996-NMCA-115; 939 P.2d 597; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 96



September 27, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Centiorari Granted December 23, 1996. Released for Publication December 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LINCOLN COUNTY. RICHARD A. PARSONS, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the District Court of Lincoln County (New Mexico) for escape from the state penitentiary inmate-release program, contrary to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 33-2-46 (1990).


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a conviction for escape from the state penitentiary inmate-release program, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial, holding that a uniform jury instruction, N.M. R. Ann. 14-2228, failed to instruct the jury on all the essential elements of the crime of escape from the inmate-release program. Defendant was in the custody of the New Mexico Department of Corrections pursuant to a judgment and sentence in a prior unrelated case. Defendant was furloughed, and failed to return on time due to car problems. Defendant was charged with escape, and at trial objected to the jury instruction on escape from the inmate-release program because it failed to contain the statutory element of "willfulness," and requested an alternate instruction, which was refused by the trial court. On appeal, the court held that "willfully" was an essential element of the crime of escape that differed from the N.M. R. Ann. 14-2228 requirement that defendant have the "intent not to return." The court interpreted "willfully," as used in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 33-2-46, to mean a conscious, purposeful failure to return within the time fixed as distinguished from an involuntary failure to return.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction as the trial court failed to instruct the jury on the essential element of "willfulness" for the crime of escape from the inmate-release program, and remanded for a new trial.

 

464 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Montano v. Los Alamos County


Docket No. 16,982


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 454; 1996-NMCA-108; 926 P.2d 307; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 89; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 46



September 12, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed September 30, 1996, denied October 23, 1996. Released for Publication October 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LOS ALAMOS COUNTY. STEVE HERRERA, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens challenged a decision of the District Court of Los Alamos County (New Mexico), which dismissed their declaratory judgment action seeking declaration that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-12-1.1 required that the governing body of appellee county be elected from single member districts.


OVERVIEW: The citizens argued that the county was in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-12-1.1. The trial court dismissed the action for failure to state a claim upon which relief could have been granted. The court dealt with the issue of whether the proviso in § 3-12-1.1 negated the mandate that municipalities with a population of over 10,000 elect their governing body from single-member districts. The court found that the language in § 3-12-1.1, which stated that H class counties "may" provide for single-member districts, unambiguously exempted the county from the mandate. The court held that the phrase "having a population of 10,000 or less" applied to municipalities and not to H class counties; therefore, the county was not required to provide for single-member districts. The court rejected the citizens' argument that the trial court's judgment violated their equal protection rights under N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 because the citizens failed to meet their burden of showing that the classification served no valid governmental interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

465 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hosteen


Docket No. 16,526


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 228; 1996-NMCA-084; 923 P.2d 595; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 64; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 36



May 22, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied August 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SAN JUAN COUNTY. BYRON CATON, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered by the District Court of San Juan County (New Mexico), which convicted him of the offense of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor (DWI). The trial also found that defendant was guilty of his fourth DWI, which made his conviction a felony under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-8-102(A) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to DWI, a misdemeanor offense. The State sought to enhance that conviction to a felony by submitting proof of three prior DWI convictions. Defense counsel conceded two of those convictions. He contested the use of the third because his client had not been represented by counsel. The trial court overruled his objection and enhanced his conviction to a felony in accordance with § 66-8-102(A). On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction and sentence. It found that defendant had not established that the concession made by his attorney constituted the ineffective assistance of counsel. Moreover, those claims were usually resolved through a petition for habeas relief. While the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments specified that a defendant could be sentenced to prison only if he had been afforded the assistance of counsel, the lack of counsel did not prohibit the subsequent use of a conviction for enhancement purposes. Therefore, the trial court was allowed to consider the uncounseled conviction. The court found that defendant had waived the issue of whether the New Mexico Constitution afforded him greater protection in that regard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

466 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanchez


Docket No. 16,076


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 280; 1996-NMCA-089; 923 P.2d 1165; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 68; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 38



May 16, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for. Released for Publication September 9, 1996. As Corrected October 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF DONA ANA COUNTY. Graden W. Beal, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction and sentence of the District Court of Dona Ana County (New Mexico), which was entered following his guilty plea to charges of second degree criminal sexual penetration (CSP II), aggravated burglary, kidnapping, and aggravated battery. Defendant argued that the sentences for CSP II, kidnapping, and burglary constituted multiple punishments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to charges of CSP II, aggravated burglary, kidnapping, and aggravated battery. At the plea hearing, he did not challenge the factual basis for the charges and did not offer any facts of his own. At the sentencing hearing, defense counsel for the first time raised the issue of whether CSP II merged with either aggravated burglary or kidnapping. The trial court denied a motion based on defense counsel's argument and sentenced defendant to 56 years in the penitentiary. Defendant appealed the sentence, contending that the CSP II conviction merged with either the kidnapping or the aggravated burglary conviction. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence. The court ruled that it was obvious to the trial court that defendant intended to appeal on grounds of a double jeopardy violation, that the guilty plea was a constructively conditional plea, and that appellate review of that issue was not waived. On the merits, the court found that defendant failed to establish a sufficient factual record below, and concluded that it could not ascertain whether defendant's conduct was unitary, the first part of its double jeopardy analysis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence that was imposed following defendant's guilty plea to CSP II, aggravated burglary, kidnapping, and aggravated battery.

 

467 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lake


Docket No. 17,075


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 794; 1996-NMCA-055; 918 P.2d 380; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 31; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 26



April 4, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed April 24, 1996, denied May 22, 1996. Released for Publication June 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANDOVAL COUNTY. KENNETH G. BROWN, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the order from the District Court of Sandoval County (New Mexico), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the information against defendant that charged him with the unlawful carrying of a firearm in an establishment licensed to dispense alcoholic beverages.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a convenience store to purchase coffee. The store was licensed to sell alcoholic beverages, but at the time defendant entered the premises, such sales were prohibited by statute. Defendant had an unconcealed, loaded handgun in his pocket. A police officer noticed the gun, and he placed defendant under arrest for violating N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-7-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1994), the unlawful carrying of a firearm in an establishment licensed to dispense alcoholic beverages. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the charge on the grounds that § 30-7-3 was vague and overbroad. The trial court granted defendant's motion because it found that a small fraction of the licensed premises was devoted to package liquor sales and that a reasonable person would not know that there was liquor on the premises or that carrying a firearm therein was illegal. The trial court also found that the statute did not serve a valid purpose during the hours when liquor sales were restricted. The court reversed and found that § 30-7-3 did not require proof that defendant knew that his act was unlawful. The court also found that the term "licensed premises" included the contiguous areas of a structure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and reinstated the information against defendant that charged him with unlawful carrying of a firearm in an establishment licensed to dispense alcoholic beverages. The court held that the statute was reasonably related to the public health, safety, and welfare and was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

468 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. House


Docket No. 16,638


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 784; 1996-NMCA-052; 918 P.2d 370; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 29; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 24



March 28, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed May 9, 1996, denied May 29, 1996. Released for Publication May 29, 1996. As Corrected June 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. JAMES F. BLACKMER, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of bail pending appeal of the DWI conviction and sentence, affirmed. Denial of bail pending appeal as to the remaining convictions and sentences, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated (DWI), reckless driving, great bodily injury by vehicle, and four counts of vehicular homicide. Defendant sought review of his convictions and requested bail pending appeal under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-11-1(C)(1995). The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) denied the request for bail pending appeal and defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that § 31-11-1(C)(2) unconstitutionally intruded upon the judiciary's power to prescribe rules of judicial procedure. The court rejected this claim, held that the statute was properly applied to the DWI conviction, but improperly applied to the other convictions, and affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's order. The court held that § 31-11-1(C)(2) was valid and did not impinge upon the separation of powers. The court also held that defendant's challenge to the DWI conviction did not present a substantial question that was likely to result in reversal. The court found that defendant's prior conviction, which was based on a guilty plea, was properly used to enhance the sentence on his current conviction because there was no error in failing to inform him of all the collateral consequences of his plea. However, the court held that defendant's appeal on the remaining convictions presented a substantial question that was likely to result in reversal because it appeared that the trial court improperly ruled on the motion to change venue. Accordingly, the court reversed the denial of bail pending appeal on these remaining convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of bail pending appeal of defendant's DWI conviction and sentence. The court reversed the trial court's denial of bail pending appeal as to his remaining convictions and sentences.
