Wilson Corp. v. State ex rel. Udall


NO. 16,484


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 677; 1996-NMCA-049; 916 P.2d 1344; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 26; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 23; 1996-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P71,389



March 19, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed April 4, 1996, denied May 2, 1996. Released for Publication May 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COLFAX COUNTY. PEGGY J. NELSON, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the district court order enforcing the CIDs against the Marketers.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from an order by the District Court of Colfax County (New Mexico) for appellants to comply with civil investigative demands (CIDs), in an action where the attorney general issued CIDs to appellants for information regarding pricing and marketing of gasoline.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the New Mexico Antitrust Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 57-1-1 to -15 (Michie 1995), the attorney general issued civil investigative demands (CIDs) directed to appellants for information regarding pricing and marketing of gasoline. After service of the CIDs, recipients raised challenges. After these were consolidated, the district court ordered appellants to comply with the CIDs. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that there was no support for a constitutional requirement that a CID could issue only if the attorney general established a likelihood that the Act had been or was being violated and that the evidence was not so compelling that every rational person would have determined the only purposes of the attorney general were improper ones. The court also rejected appellants' contentions regarding the denial of discovery, where appellants failed to set forth what discovery they sought or how it would be relevant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that appellants comply with civil investigative demands (CIDs), where the court held CIDs could be issued without a showing antitrust laws had been or were being violated and affirmed denial of discovery where appellants failed to show what was sought or its relevance.

 

470 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ernesto M. (In re Ernesto M.)


No. 16,203


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 562; 1996-NMCA-039; 915 P.2d 318; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 16; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 15



February 1, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed February 19, 1996, denied March 21, 1996. Released for Publication April 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CHILDREN'S COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. JAMES L. SHULER, Children's Court Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant child appealed the judgment of the Children's Court Of Eddy County (New Mexico), which, under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32A-2-20 (1978, Repl. Pamp. 1993), sentenced the child as an adult for the robbing, beating, kidnapping, and rape of a convenience store clerk.


OVERVIEW: The child beat, kidnapped, and repeatedly raped a convenience store clerk and admitted that he was guilty of four crimes. The children's court found that the child was a youthful offender under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32A-2-3(I) (1978, Repl. Pamp. 1993) and sentenced him to 30 years in prison as an adult. Two experts believed that the child was amenable to treatment, and one expert was not sure. The court affirmed the children's court's sentence, holding that even though § 32A-2-20 did not specify the standard of proof by which the children's court was to determine whether the child should be sentenced as an adult, § 32A-2-20 provided the child with elemental due process and was not arbitrary or capricious. Even though no expert stated that the child could not be treated, the court held that the children's court was entitled to disbelieve the experts and to determine the credibility of the testimony. The court ruled that the 30-year sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment because the child essentially tortured the clerk, and there was evidence that the child was the instigator of the crimes against the clerk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the children's court's decision to sentence the child as an adult for the crimes that he committed.

 

471 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duarte


No. 15,581


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 553; 1996-NMCA-038; 915 P.2d 309; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 15; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 15



January 25, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 26, 1996. Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed February 14, 1996, denied March 21, 1996. Released for Publication April 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. Fred A. Watson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which convicted him of voluntary manslaughter and conspiracy to tamper with evidence, and sentenced him under the enhancement provision of the habitual-offender statute.


OVERVIEW: After defendant stabbed an acquaintance during an altercation involving his girlfriend, he was convicted of voluntary manslaughter and conspiracy to tamper with evidence, and his sentence was enhanced due to his status as a habitual offender. Defendant appealed the denial of his requested instruction on deadly force and defense of others, the determination that he was competent to stand trial, and the use of his prior convictions to enhance his sentence. The court affirmed the convictions and the sentence, holding that defendant was not entitled to the requested instruction on deadly force. Although defendant failed to testify, the jury could infer that his attack on the victim was motivated by an intent to protect his girlfriend. However, there was no evidence to show that the use of force was reasonable in light of the victim's statements, actions, and unarmed status. Although there was some conflicting testimony regarding defendant's competency, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding him competent. Further, no showing was made that the sentence enhancement was improper despite the claim that defendant had been unable to understand the prior guilty pleas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of voluntary manslaughter and conspiracy to tamper with evidence, and it confirmed the enhancement of defendant's sentence under the habitual offender statute.

 

472 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Lane v. Lane


No. 16,262


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 414; 1996-NMCA-023; 912 P.2d 290; 1996 N.M. App. LEXIS 1; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 11



January 12, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed February 1, 1996, denied February 22, 1996. Released for Publication February 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF VALENCIA COUNTY. WILLIAM A. SANCHEZ, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of an order of the District Court of Valencia County (New Mexico), which held that appellee husband was the natural father of a child born by artificial insemination during the parties' marriage, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-11-6-(A).


OVERVIEW: A husband was awarded joint custody of a child in a divorce decree, and the wife appealed, asserting that the child was conceived during the marriage by artificial insemination from an anonymous donor. The court affirmed and held that the parties substantially complied with the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-11-6. The court explained that a husband was entitled to custody of a child only if he was the child's "natural" father, according to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-4-9.1(K). N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-11-6 provided that a husband was to be treated as the natural father of a child conceived by artificial insemination so long as the husband's consent was in a writing signed by him and his wife. There was no written consent signed by the husband and wife prior to the child's birth; however, the court held that the purposes of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-11-6(A) were best effectuated by treating the husband as the child's natural father. Section 40-11-6(A) did not prescribe the form of the writing nor require that the writing be created at a certain time. The court found that the pleadings in the divorce action demonstrated a knowing consent by the parties to treat the husband as the natural father.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court awarding joint custody of the child to the husband.

 

473 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Old Abe Co. v. N.M. Mining Comm'n


No. 15,750


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 83; 1995-NMCA-134; 908 P.2d 776; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 141; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 6



October 24, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed November 13, 1995, denied December 11, 1995. Released for Publication December 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ADOPTION OF REGULATIONS by the NEW MEXICO MINING COMMISSION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee New Mexico Mining Commission adopted regulations that implemented the New Mexico Mining Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 69-36-1 to -20 (1978). Appellant miners challenged the regulations as arbitrary and capricious, an abuse of discretion, and also alleged that the regulations and Act were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court held that because the Commission had taken no action against the miners under the regulations, it did not have jurisdiction to review the constitutionality of the Act. However, pursuant to the authority granted in the Act, the court did have jurisdiction to review a pre-enforcement facial challenge to the regulations. The court found that the Commission failed to comply with the statuary requirements to produce a schedule of fees. Therefore, the court invalidated those provisions of the regulations that did not set a determinate fee but merely set maximum fees. Other than those regulations, the court held that the remaining regulations (1) did not conflict with the Act; (2) were not impermissibly vague (3) did not improperly delegate unguided discretion or violate N.M. Const. art III, § 1 by improperly delegating legislative authority; (4) did not violation N.M. Cont. arts. VIII, § 9, or IV, § 30, and (5) did not violate equal protection principles.


OUTCOME: The court held that it did not have jurisdiction to review the validity of the Act. The court invalidated the fee structure regulations but held that the remaining regulations were not arbitrary, capricious, or an abuse of discretion, and were in accordance with law.

 

474 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Bell v. N.M. Interstate Stream Comm'n


No. 16,321


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 328; 1996-NMCA-010; 911 P.2d 222; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 160; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 8



October 20, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for. Released for Publication January 29, 1996. As Corrected February 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. GERALD R. COLE, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents of an injured child sought review of an order entered after a remand in the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which granted a renewed motion for summary judgment filed by defendants, New Mexico Interstate Stream Commission and associated governmental entities of the State of New Mexico, in the parents' action under the Tort Claims Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-6, -8, and 11 (Supp. 1995).


OVERVIEW: The child was injured when hit his head on a submerged object in a state park lake. Defendants claimed that they were immune from liability under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-6 (Supp. 1995). In a prior appeal, the court concluded that the trial court erred in granting defendants' motion for summary judgment because the only evidence of record was that the lake was used solely for recreational purposes and defendants failed to show a right to immunity. On remand, defendants filed a renewed summary judgment motion adding an engineer's affidavit stating that the lake served multiple purposes, including the storage and diversion of water. On appeal of the second summary judgment order, the court ruled that the new evidence provided by defendants established that they were entitled to immunity under the second sentence of § 41-4-6.The court noted that the legislative intent in enacting § 41-4-6 was to preserve sovereign immunity for water diversion and storage works. The court further ruled that the law of the case doctrine did not preclude defendants from adducing new evidence to support their renewed motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting defendants' renewed motion for summary judgment.

 

475 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Tull v. City of Albuquerque


No. 16,193


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 829; 1995-NMCA-123; 907 P.2d 1010; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 133; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 2



September 21, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As corrected June 13, 2001. Certiorari not Applied for. Released for Publication December 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Gerard W. Thomson, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees appealed from a judgment of the District Court for Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which dismissed the employees' breach of employment contract claim against defendant city on the ground that the statute of limitations on the claim had run.


OVERVIEW: In 1994, almost seven years after a change in the employees' job responsibilities, the employees brought a breach of an employment contract action against the city, alleging that they were entitled to a retroactive raise in salary commensurate with their increased job responsibilities. The trial court dismissed the claim, holding that the three-year statute of limitations applicable to contract claims against a city began to run when the employees' duties were changed in November 1987. On appeal the employees contended that a new breach of contract occurred with each paycheck that did not include the raise to which they were entitled. The court affirmed, holding that the continuing-wrong theory was inapplicable because the only actionable wrong alleged by the employees was the city's initial refusal to increase the employees' salaries and, although that wrong had continuing consequences in the form of lower paychecks, the continuing effects did not extend the life of the breach of contract cause of action, which was based solely on the initial refusal. Because the breach of contract occurred in November 1987, the employees had only until November 1990 to file their complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the employees' breach of employment contract complaint against the city.

 

476 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Daugherty v. City of Carlsbad


No. 15,923


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 716; 1995-NMCA-108; 905 P.2d 1120; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 118; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 10



August 25, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed October 10, 1995, denied November 1, 1995. Released for Publication November 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. ALVIN F. JONES, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners challenged the decision of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which granted the motion for summary judgment of defendant city, through its councilmen and mayor, and that concluded that the annexed tract was contiguous as a matter of law pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-7-17 (1978 and Repl. Pamp. 1987) after intervenors had filed a petition seeking the adoption of an ordinance to annex their land into the city.


OVERVIEW: Intervenors filed a petition with the city council seeking annexation of a tract of land that they owned to the city limits by a 23 acre irregular-shaped strip of land owned by the landowners. The landowners filed an appeal in the district court, challenging the annexation, claiming the property that intervenors really sought to be annexed, their own property, was just connected by a "shoestring" parcel of the landowners' property to satisfy the technical statutory requirement of contiguity. The city and the landowners filed cross motions for summary judgment. The district court concluded that the annexed tract was contiguous as a matter of law pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-7-17 (1978 and Repl. Pamp. 1987), and that there was no issue of material fact. On appeal, the court affirmed the district court. The court held that the appropriate judicial response was deference to the legislative decision of the city council. The court determined that the district court had found that the annexed tract was contiguous to the city, and it had properly refused the landowners' invitation to analyze the economic or political benefits or burdens upon their land by the annexation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court granting the city's motion for summary judgment and concluding that the annexed tract was contiguous as a matter of law.

 

477 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Cottrell v. Santillanes


No. 16,242


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 367; 1995-NMCA-090; 901 P.2d 785; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 87; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 41



July 19, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed August 7, 1995, Rehearing Denied August 24, 1995. Released for Publication August 29, 1995. As Corrected September 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. ROBERT H. SCOTT, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, current and former city councilors, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which granted judgment in favor of appellees, a city, a city clerk, two citizens groups, a voter, and two current city councilors that supported an amendment. Appellants filed a complaint for declaratory judgment challenging the constitutionality of a charter amendment to limit the term of its city councilors.


OVERVIEW: The amendment in question, Albuquerque, N.M. Charter § 13, limited the term of its city councilors to no more than two elected terms. The trial court stated that passage and enforcement of the amendment was a constitutional exercise of the city's powers under the Home Rule Amendment, N.M. Const. art. X, § 6. The court reversed, holding that the Qualifications Clause, N.M. Const. art. VII, § 2, preempted a home rule municipality's power to adopt additional qualifications for elected office within the State of New Mexico beyond those set forth in its constitution. The court stated that reading N.M. Const. art. VII, § 2 and N.M. Const. art. V, § 13 together, the law was that any citizen who was a qualified voter could have held any municipal elected office subject only to the residency requirement. Thus, the amendment to the city charter was inconsistent with the Qualifications Clause. The Municipal Charter Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 3-15-1 to -16 (Supp. 1994), did not expand the city's power to adopt additional qualifications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Albuquerque Police Dep't v. Martinez (In re Forfeiture of Fourteen Thousand Six Hundred Thirty Nine Dollars ($ 14,639) in United States Currency


No. 15,525


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. GERARD W. THOMSON, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police department (department) sought review of an order by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) that set aside a default judgment in favor of the department and thereby dismissed the department's forfeiture case against appellee arrestee.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee's property was seized upon arrest. The arrestee did not respond to publication of the forfeiture proceeding, and a default judgment was entered in favor of the department. In his criminal trial, the arrestee filed a motion to suppress the evidence (some of which included the forfeited items), and the motion was granted with an order that all property was to be returned to the arrestee. The court found that collateral estoppel applied to the civil forfeiture proceeding based on the judgment in the criminal trial even though the actions were brought by separate entities because the entities were arms of the same larger entity. The court affirmed the effective dismissal of the forfeiture action and remanded for further findings..


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the prior order that in essence dismissed the department's forfeiture action, and remanded for additional findings as to residual evidence to support the forfeiture action.

 

479 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Luckie


No. 15,889, No. 15,972


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 274; 1995-NMCA-075; 901 P.2d 205; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 70; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 36



June 19, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed July 10, 1995, denied August 8, 1995. Released for Publication August 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. FRANK H. ALLEN, JR. and ROSS C. SANCHEZ, District Judges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of orders entered in the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) in two separate cases dismissing indictments against defendants for unlawful custodial interference, a violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-4-4 (1994). The court granted the State's motion to consolidate the appeals.


OVERVIEW: The trial courts found that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-4-4(B) (1994), which defined custodial interference as the taking of a child without good cause and with the intent to deprive another person of his right to custody for a protracted time, was unconstitutionally vague and violated the Due Process Clauses of the United States and New Mexico Constitutions. On appeal, the court determined that the State failed to preserve its argument that defendants were precluded from asserting a facial challenge to § 30-4-4(B). The court reversed the dismissals on the ground that the statute was not impermissibly vague because the phrases used in the statute had such general and well-recognized meanings that individuals were placed on notice of the conduct sought to be proscribed, and that it was not necessary that phrases such as "without good cause" and "for a protracted time" be defined by statute. The court further determined that the indictments brought against defendants, which followed the exact language of § 30-4-4(B), sufficiently apprised defendants of the essential facts of the unlawful conduct they allegedly engaged in so they could properly defend against the charges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's orders dismissing the indictments and remanded for further proceedings.

Ridenour v. Ridenour


No. 15,622


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 352; 1995-NMCA-072; 901 P.2d 770; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 75; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 35



June 2, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed June 22, 1995, denied July 12, 1995. Released for Publication August 14, 1995. As Corrected August 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF VALENCIA COUNTY. WILLIAM A. SANCHEZ, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed from an order of the District Court of Valencia County (New Mexico), which granted petitioner grandparents request for visitation rights with the granddaughter.


OVERVIEW: After the relationship between a mother and grandmother deteriorated, the mother terminated all contact between her child and the grandparents. The grandparents subsequently filed a petition for grandparental visitation. The trial court granted the petition. The mother appealed from the order, arguing that the Grandparent's Visitation Privileges Act (GVA), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 40-9-1 to 4 (1994), was unconstitutional and that the amount of visitation granted was unreasonable and not supported by substantial evidence. The court affirmed, holding that the GVA was constitutional because although the state's enforcement of it did impact the mother's right to raise her child, the intrusion was not a substantial interference and was thus an appropriate mechanism by which the state may balance the parties' competing interests. The court noted that an act authorizing the trial court to permit grandparent child visitation withstood state and federal constitutional challenges if allowance of such visitation was shown to be in the best interest of the child. The court also held that the trial court's grant of visitation was reasonable and not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the grandparents visitation rights with their granddaughter, against the mother's challenge to those rights.

 

481 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Mott v. Sun Country Garden Prods.


No. 15,548


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 261; 1995-NMCA-066; 901 P.2d 192; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 71; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 34



May 26, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed June 22, 1995, denied July 12, 1995. Released for Publication: August 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANDOVAL COUNTY. KENNETH G. BROWN, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed a decision of the District Court of Sandoval County (New Mexico), which entered a verdict in favor of plaintiff, executor of the estate of a deceased motor vehicle driver. The corporation argued that the district court committed error in excluding evidence that neither the driver nor his passenger was wearing seat belts at the time of the accident, refusing jury instructions, and refusing to admit relevant evidence.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that the seat belt defense was not prohibited by statute when the executor brought her action, and the district court therefore violated N.M. Const. art. IV, § 34 by prohibiting the introduction of seat belt evidence. The court held that because the corporation did not possess the right to limit the executor's recovery for seat belt non-use at common law, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-7-373 did not limit the corporation's rights and the statute was within the legitimate ambit of legislative authority. The corporation also argued that the prohibition of a seat belt defense arbitrarily and unreasonably interfered with the adjudication of rights in a comparative negligence system and denied substantive due process. The court held that evidence of the failure to use seat belts did not limit or apportion damages. The court also held that because the theory of strict liability was not raised, the failure to instruct the jury on strict liability was not error, and the district court did not abuse its discretion in determining that expert testimony would not assist the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the verdict in favor of the executor.

 

482 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arrington


No. 15,345


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 54; 1995-NMCA-057; 897 P.2d 241; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 56; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 29



May 5, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed May 24, 1995, denied June 15, 1995. Released for Publication June 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY. RALPH W. GALLINI, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment and sentence of the district court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which, after defendant pleaded no contest to a distribution of marijuana charge, sentenced her to incarceration in a correctional facility, despite an earlier ruling on an unrelated charge that sentencing defendant under the habitual-offender statute to the correctional facility would be cruel and unusual punishment due to her significant asthma problems.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded no contest to a marijuana charge and was sentenced under the habitual-offender statute to over five years in prison. On appeal, defendant argued that her incarceration was unconstitutional in view of the court's earlier ruling, on unrelated charges, that imposing a prison term upon her, a person with significant asthma problems, was cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII and N.M. Const. art. II, § 13. The court disagreed, explaining that the basis of its earlier ruling was that the evidence showed that the prison was unable to provide defendant with necessary medical care. Incarceration, in such circumstances, would be life-threatening because defendant's medical needs could not be handled adequately. Testimony in the instant case indicated, however, that a contract physician was available 24 hours a day to provide treatment and that he could arrive within 10 minutes of an emergency call. Moreover, other physicians were available and at least one nurse was always on duty, and defendant could retain possession of her medication. Thus, custodial treatment at the prison would not amount to deliberate indifference to defendant's condition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and five and one-half year sentence as a habitual offender in the correctional facility.

Conoco, Inc. v. State Taxation & Revenue Dep't


Docket No. 15,372


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 745; 1997-NMCA-004; 931 P.2d 739; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 170; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 6



May 1, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Granted. As Corrected February 11, 1997.



DISPOSITION: ADMINISTRATIVE APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO TAXATION AND REVENUE DEPARTMENT. GERALD B. RICHARDSON, Hearing Officer. Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision by appellee New Mexico Taxation and Revenue Department (department), which denied the taxpayer's claims for refunds and reduced the department's assessment against the taxpayer consistent with modifications to the standard apportionment formula allowed for previous years.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed suit against the department and sought a refund of corporate income taxes paid to the State of New Mexico for certain years based on what its tax liability would have been had foreign dividends and income been excluded from its apportionable tax base. The department denied the taxpayer's claim for refunds and the taxpayer appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the department's decision and held that the denial of a refund to the taxpayer was proper because where the dividends from subsidiaries of a parent company reflected profits derived from an integrated enterprise, those dividends, including foreign subsidiary dividends, were income earned. The court held that as long as the intra-state and extra-state activities formed part of a single, unitary business, the fact that a tax was apportioned in part upon the taxpayer's foreign income sources did not constitute a bar to state taxation. Lastly, the court held that New Mexico did not allow a foreign tax credit for corporations using the separate-entity reporting method and having foreign subsidiary dividend income, and that it was proper to look at the entire tax scheme in evaluating a claim of discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the department.

Bustamante v. De Baca


No. 15,369


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 739; 1995-NMCA-036; 895 P.2d 261; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 25; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 25



April 4, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. STEVE HERRERA, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant New Mexico Department of Public Safety sought review of an order from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) in favor of appellee police officer, which held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-8-134(A) (Repl. Pamp. 1994), was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous.


OVERVIEW: The Department initiated successful proceedings to terminate the police officer for violating § 66-8-134(A) by using his position of authority to suggest or imply to a motorist that he could reduce or alter the DWI citation issued to her. The police officer appealed the discipline to the district court, which concluded that the statute was unconstitutional, and remanded for a redetermination. The court held that the Department was entitled to appeal the order based on an exception to the final order requirement. The court further held that § 66-8-134(A) was not unconstitutional. The court explained that the provision precisely defined, in unequivocal terms, the type of behavior prohibited, that no one could cancel or solicit the cancellation of any uniform traffic citation other than as provided in the Motor Vehicle Code. The court determined that none of the statute's terms defied common understanding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the police officer and remanded for a redetermination of the original appeal.

Marez v. Taxation & Revenue Dep't, Motor Vehicle Div.


No. 15,733


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 598; 1995-NMCA-030; 893 P.2d 494; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 19; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 24



March 17, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for. Released for Publication April 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. JAMES F. BLACKMER, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment entered by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which upheld the revocation of his driver's license by appellee, the Motor Vehicle Division (MVD), under the New Mexico Implied Consent Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 66-8-105 to 66-8-112 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The driver refused to take a breath test in order to determine his blood-alcohol level after his arrest. His driver's license was revoked by the MVD after a hearing. The district court upheld that revocation. The driver appealed from the district court's judgment, which was affirmed. The Act authorized the revocation of a driver's license solely on the basis of a driver's refusal to submit to a breath test. The court rejected the driver's argument that the Act was unconstitutional because his refusal to take a breath test could be used to establish the criminal offense of aggravated driving while intoxicated under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-8-102(D)(3) (1994). Rather, the privilege against self-incrimination and right to counsel secured by the Fifth and Sixth Amendments to the United States Constitution were applicable to only criminal proceedings. Furthermore, the United States Supreme Court had found that implied consent acts were a valid exercise of a state's police power. The court also stated that the driver did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 66-8-102(D)(3) because he had not been charged under that statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment, which had upheld the MVD's revocation of the driver's operator's license.

 

486 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guebara


No. 15,219


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 662; 1995-NMCA-031; 894 P.2d 1018; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 30; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 25



March 17, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed March 22, 1995, GRANT April 27, 1995. Released for Publication May 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. JAMES L. SHULER, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), for receiving or transferring a stolen motor vehicle, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-3-305 (1978, Repl. 1994 ). Defendant pled no contest to the charge, reserving his right to appeal based upon the trial court's ruling that the vehicle identification number (VIN), which police obtained in a warrantless search of the subject vehicle, was admissible.


OVERVIEW: Defendant requested permission from a friend to park a vehicle at her residence. After the vehicle had remained parked on the property for three weeks, the friend's husband telephoned police stating that he feared the vehicle was stolen. Because the keys were unavailable, police put a coat hanger through the vehicle's window in order to move an envelope that covered the VIN and discovered that the VIN matched that of a vehicle that was reported stolen. The trial court admitted the VIN into evidence, finding that the police had acted reasonably under the circumstances, their actions were lawful, and a warrant had been unnecessary. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case, finding that the search had violated defendant's Fourth Amendment rights. The court reasoned that defendant had not abandoned the vehicle and that it was reasonable to expect that police would not break into a car to reveal its VIN. The court found that the police could have impounded the vehicle under the VIN Statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 66-3-508 and -507(b) (1978, Repl. 1994), and obtained a warrant to search it. Since the search was unlawful, the court held that the VIN should have been excluded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of receiving or transferring a stolen motor vehicle and remanded the case to the trial court.

State v. Rowell


No. 15,365


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 710; 1995-NMCA-029; 895 P.2d 232; 1995 N.M. App. LEXIS 32; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 25

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CURRY COUNTY. STEPHEN QUINN, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his jury conviction in the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico) on one count of computer access with intent to commit fraud over $ 250, a fourth degree felony in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-45-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1989), and one count of attempt to commit fraud over $ 250, a misdemeanor under N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 30-16-6, 30-28-1 (Repl. Pamp. 1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on one count of computer access with intent to commit fraud over $ 250 in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-45-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1989), and one count of attempt to commit fraud over $ 250 in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 30-16-6, 30-28-1 (Repl. Pamp. 1994). The court affirmed his conviction on the intent charge, but reversed and vacated his conviction on the attempt charge. The court found that he allowed the state's expert testimony that the switching involved in a long distance call constituted accessing a computer network, to go unrebutted and, therefore, there was substantial evidence to support his conviction for computer access with intent to defraud under N.M. The court held that the applicable statutes were not vague and that the jury instructions made it clear that the applicable law was contained entirely in those instructions. The court ruled that the state failed to rebut his contention that he could not be convicted of attempt under the general fraud statute if he also was convicted, on the same facts, of the completed offense under the specific provisions of the § 30-45-3 computer fraud statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated defendant's conviction for attempt to commit fraud over $ 250 because the state did not contradict his argument that he could not be convicted, based on the same facts, of both a completed offense under the specific provisions of the computer fraud statute and an attempted offense under the general fraud statute. The court affirmed the remainder of his conviction because it was supported by substantial evidence.

Bolton v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 15,635


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 355; 1994-NMCA-167; 890 P.2d 808; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 175; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 19



December 15, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF VALENCIA COUNTY. LESLIE C. SMITH, Designated District Judge.

Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed January 23, 1995, denied February 16, 1995. Released for Publication February 28, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals and cross-appellant financial corporations challenged a judgment of the District Court of Valencia County (New Mexico), which, in the individuals' suit against the financial corporations and appellee county commissioners, invalidated a portion of a county bond issue.


OVERVIEW: In response to the adoption of a county bond issue, the individuals filed a suit claiming that the issuance of the bond violated constitutional provisions requiring voter approval of bond issues. Subsequent to a trial court's ruling invalidating only a portion of the bond issue, the court held that limitations on the individuals' discovery did not deny them their due process rights. The court then noted that, by limiting repayment of the bonds to receipts from gross receipts and gasoline tax revenues, the bonds were solely repayable out of special funds and thus were not considered general obligation bonds because they did not pledge the full faith and credit of the county. As a result, the court held that the bond issue did not violate N.M. Const. art. IX, § 10, which required voter approval only prior to the issuance of general obligation bonds. However, the court held that the trial court erred in invalidating the portion of the bond issue that allowed for the refinancing of road building equipment. In so holding, the court reasoned that the power to purchase equipment to construct roads was a part of the express power a county was granted to build and maintain such roads.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment invalidating a portion of the bond issue that allowed for refinancing for road building equipment and affirmed the judgment upholding the remainder of the bond issue.

 

491 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Corn v. N.M. Educators Fed. Credit Union


No. 14,553


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 199; 1994-NMCA-161; 889 P.2d 234; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 150; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 17



December 2, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petitions for Writ of Certiorari filed December 22, 1994, denied January 17, 1995. Released for Publication January 23, 1995. As Corrected May 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. MaryAnn Lunderman, Workers' Compensation Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker challenged that portion of a decision of the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Administration, which, in her claim against appellees, employer and carrier, limited her award of attorneys' fees to the cap required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-54(G) (Repl. Pamp. 1991).


OVERVIEW: The worker brought a claim against the employer and the carrier concerning a head injury sustained in a work-related car accident. The administration determined that her attorney had reasonably expended almost $ 20,000 in fees because of the complexity of the case, but found that it had to limit the award to $ 12,500, as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-54(G). The worker raised an equal protection challenge to this statute because the attorney's fees of the employer were not similarly limited. The court ruled that § 52-1-54(G) was unconstitutional and remanded for a reconsideration of the fee award. The court found that a heightened rational-basis review applied to the classification and interests represented in the statute and that the statute had to have a factual foundation and a legal rationale. Although limits on attorney's fees were originally justified as a protection for workers, the court determined that the imposition of a cap on fees in the absence of the employer's bad faith was not justifiable as serving any rationale purpose and, in fact, placed the worker at a disadvantage to the employer.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the cap on attorney's fees for a worker in a worker's compensation claim was unconstitutional. The court vacated the limited award of attorney's fees for the worker in her claim against the employer and the carrier and remanded for a reconsideration of the fee award.

 

492 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guzman


Nos. 14,802 & 14,803 (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 190; 1994-NMCA-149; 889 P.2d 225; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 164; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 12



November 17, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed December 5, 1994, denied January 5, 1995. Released for Publication January 27, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. H. Richard Blackhurst, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: For the above reasons, a new trial is required. This case is therefore reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed convictions from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, conspiracy to commit distribution of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, conspiracy to commit distribution of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Defendants argued that the State's use of five out of five peremptory challenges against Hispanic prospective jurors was racially motivated and violated defendants' constitutional rights. The State argued that defendants failed to establish a prima facie case that the State purposefully discriminated against Hispanic prospective jurors, and, even if defendants had established a prima facie case of purposeful discrimination, the prosecutor satisfied his burden of providing race-neutral explanations for his peremptory challenges. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial, holding that Hispanics were a cognizable group for purposes of Batson inquiry. Because of the presence of Anglo jurors whose characteristics were comparable to those relied upon to exclude Hispanic jurors, the State failed to satisfy its burden of providing a racially neutral explanation. Also, the Batson rationale not only protected a defendant's right to an impartial jury, but also protected prospective jurors from discriminatory exclusion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, conspiracy to commit distribution of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia and remanded for a new trial.

 

493 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Armijo


No. 15,172


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 802; 1994-NMCA-136; 887 P.2d 1269; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 139; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 8



October 20, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed November 7, 1994, denied December 7, 1994. Released for Publication January 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. STEVE HERRERA, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the district court's order dismissing the indictment and disqualifying the attorney general's office. We remand for trial on the indictment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state sought review of an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which dismissed the state's indictment of defendant public official on charges of fraud and bribery and which disqualified the state attorney general from prosecuting the action.


OVERVIEW: The public official was indicted by a grand jury on charges of bribery and fraud. The district court entered an order granting the public official's motion to dismiss the indictment and to disqualify the attorney general's office from continued prosecution of the action. The district court determined that the indictment was based on perjured testimony, that the state failed to present exculpatory evidence to the grand jury, and that the state engaged in outrageous misconduct. On appeal, the court reversed the order. The court held that: (1) the order dismissing the indictment was appealable under N. M. Stat. Ann. § 39-3-3(B) (1978), and the state had a constitutional right to appeal the attorney general's disqualification; (2) the rule requiring dismissal of an indictment for withholding directly exculpatory evidence in violation of N. M. Stat. Ann. § 31-6-11(B) (1978) did not apply because there was no evidence that the state's intentionally failed to provide the grand jury material that was directly exculpatory; and (3) the order disqualifying the attorney general was improper there was no evidence that the prosecution engaged in improper or bad faith conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the indictment of defendant public official on charges of fraud and bribery and disqualifying the state attorney general from prosecuting the action. The court remanded the action to the district court for trial on the indictment.

 

494 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Lally


No. 14,960


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 795; 1994-NMCA-135; 887 P.2d 1262; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 140; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 6



October 12, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed November 1, 1994, denied November 29, 1994. Released for Publication January 9, 1995. As Corrected February 20, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. ROBERT H. SCOTT, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pharmacist sought review of a decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which entered judgment against the pharmacist in his action against defendant assistant district attorney (attorney). The pharmacist sought a declaratory judgment declaring that the pharmacist's civil rights were violated by the attorney's conduct of initiating criminal proceedings against him maliciously and without cause.


OVERVIEW: The pharmacist reported to the board of pharmacy that patrons were soliciting forged prescriptions. An investigator for the board instituted an investigation and several suspects were apprehended. The same investigator filed a criminal complaint against the pharmacist accusing him of unlawfully filling forged prescriptions. Ultimately, the action against the pharmacist was dismissed. The pharmacist sought a declaratory judgment against the attorney declaring that his civil rights were violated by the attorney's past conduct. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the attorney. On appeal, the court affirmed. Past wrongs, even unconstitutional wrongs, did not create a foundation for declaratory relief without either continuing illegal actions or continuing consequences to the pharmacist. The absence of any "useful purpose" or "practical effect" was the essence of why declaratory judgment was inappropriate for the pharmacist. The pharmacist sought moral vindication and his action for money damages was frustrated by immunity. Vindication alone was not the kind of constructive "useful purpose" for which declaratory judgment was created.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which entered judgment against the pharmacist, in his action against the assistant district attorney, seeking a declaratory judgment declaring that the pharmacist's civil rights were violated by the attorney's conduct of initiating criminal proceedings against him maliciously and without cause.

 

495 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Alvarez v. Chavez


No. 14,975


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 732; 1994-NMCA-133; 886 P.2d 461; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 131



October 5, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for. Released for Publication November 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. STEVE HERRERA, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant superintendent appealed a decision by the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which concluded that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 59A-51-4 (Repl. Pamp. 1992) and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 59A-51-13(C) (Repl. Pamp. 1992) violated equal protection guarantees because the two statutes infringed plaintiff bail bondsman's fundamental right to hold public office and because they were not rationally related to a legitimate state end.


OVERVIEW: The bail bondsman filed an action for declaratory judgment, challenging the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 59A-51-4, 59A-51-13(C). The superintendent contended that the statutes were rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest and were therefore constitutional. The court stated that the statutes, which required the bail bondsman to give up his livelihood if he was to remain in elected office, were substantial barriers to his candidacy. The statutes were subject to at least the heightened rational-basis standard of review under the New Mexico Constitution. The superintendent proffered as a basis for the statute the need to protect the integrity of the bail-bonding process. The court agreed that protecting the integrity of the bail-bonding process was a legitimate state goal. However, the statutes were both under inclusive and over inclusive, and the presence of state and county officials in the statutes' prohibitions did not appear to be rationally based. Also, the statutes contained a number of classifications, and those were required to be rationally related to the purported purpose of the statutes. Thus, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which concluded that the two statutes, which precluded county officers from being licensed as bail bondsmen or from receiving benefits from the bail-bonding business, violated equal protection guarantees in the bail bondsman's declaratory judgment action.

 

496 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Aldridge v. Mims


No. 14,794


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 661; 1994-NMCA-114; 884 P.2d 817; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 127; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1490



August 22, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed September 12, 1994, Denied September 30, 1994. Released for Publication November 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SIERRA COUNTY. Edmund H. Kase, III, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child challenged the judgment of the District Court of Sierra County (New Mexico), which granted appellee estate's motion to dismiss the child's claim of heirship and his paternity action.


OVERVIEW: The child was by his maternal grandparents without the consent of his natural father. The child argued that he should have been able to prove the decedent's paternity so that he could inherit from both his natural parents as well as his adoptive parents. The court found that at the time of the alleged father's death, it was already established that, under the Uniform Probate Code, an adopted child inherited through the adoptive, not the natural, parents. Therefore, the court affirmed the dismissal of the child's actions because the adoption was final and its validity could not be attacked. The district court properly considered the adoption decree and correctly concluded that the child was legally precluded from challenging his adoption at such a late date.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the child's claims of heirship against his alleged father's estate and his paternity action were affirmed.

 

497 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Udall v. Public Employees Ret. Bd.


No. 14,954


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 507; 1994-NMCA-094; 882 P.2d 548; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 109



July 12, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed September, 1, 1994, Granted September 28, 1994. Released for Publication September 29, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. JOE CRUZ CASTELLANO, JR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State of New Mexico appealed an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which ruled that a pension plan for legislators was constitutional. In the action against defendants, the Public Employees Retirement Board and various plan participants, the attorney general had contended that the plan violated N.M. Const. art. IV, § 10, and that a portion of the benefits already received should be repaid.


OVERVIEW: The case was assigned to a district judge who issued an order finding the plan unconstitutional. On appeal by defendants, the court dismissed the appeal on the ground that the order was not a final, appealable order because it did not resolve the attorney general's claim for refunds. On remand, the district judge vacated the order. On appeal, the court rejected the attorney general's contentions that under the law of the case doctrine, the second district judge should not have revisited and reversed the first decision regarding constitutionality. The district court had the authority to reconsider the earlier non-final ruling; thus, it was not inappropriate for the second district judge to overrule the prior interlocutory order. In reversing the order, the court held that the legislative pension plan violated the Constitution. It was "clearly satisfied" that state-funded pensions were barred by N.M. Const. art. IV, § 10 because the words "compensation, perquisite or allowance" included pension plan benefits. Irrespective of whether the framers contemplated pensions, they clearly stated that legislators were to receive nothing other than the sums specified in the Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's order and remanded the action for further proceedings regarding the attorney general's claim for repayment of pension plan benefits already received.

 

498 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Duke City Pizza, Inc.


No. 14,431


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 346; 1994-NMCA-085; 881 P.2d 706; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 94; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1118



June 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed August 9, 1994, Denied September 1, 1994. Released for Publication September 6, 1994. As Corrected November 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. MaryAnn Lunderman, Workers' Compensation Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker sought review from a decision of the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Administration (New Mexico), which granted her disability claim but denied her certain parts of her motion requesting attorney fees against appellee employer.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court rejected the worker's claim that it was error for the administration judge to deny her claim of bad faith attorney fees, since it was within the administration judge's discretion, and it was not clearly irrational. The court found that the worker and the expert's testimony led them to conclude that there was substantial evidence on the record to support a finding of temporary total disability. Since post-injury employment did not preclude a finding of temporary total disability, it was not error for the administration judge to refuse to award a credit for overpayment of benefits to the employer. The court agreed with the employer that it was error to find that the worker suffered a scheduled injury to her left arm versus her left hand, since the record did not reveal any evidence to support the medical expert's opinion that the worker's left arm was useless. Since the worker failed to show that she could not perform her pre-injury job, the court erred in awarding her expenses for college education as vocational rehabilitation benefits. Since the expert witness did not testify under subpoena, the expert witness fee awarded to the worker was in error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administration judge's denial of bad faith attorney fees to the worker and affirmed the denial of a credit for overpayment of benefits to the worker by the employer. The court reversed the administration judge's compensation order of vocational rehabilitation benefits to the worker.

 

499 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rickard


Nos. 14,566, 14,591, 14,503, 14,458, 14,866


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 312; 1994-NMCA-083; 881 P.2d 57; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 89; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1052



June 24, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed July 14, 1994, Granted August 15, 1994. Cert was not granted for Woods, only for the other four defendants. Released for Publication August 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 14,566. APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CURRY COUNTY. FRED T. HENSLEY, District Judge.

No. 14,591. APPEAL PROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF ROOSEVELT COUNTY. DAVID W. BONEM, District Judge.

No. 14,503. APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY. PATRICK J. FRANCOEUR, District Judge.

No. 14,458. APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CURRY COUNTY. FRED T. HENSLEY, District Judge.

No. 14,866. APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY. LARRY JOHNSON, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, five defendants were subjected to random urinalysis testing as a condition of probation and tested positive for the presence of cocaine. Subsequently, each defendant was convicted in a district court (New Mexico) for possession of cocaine. Defendants challenged whether their urine test results were privileged information improperly disclosed to law enforcement officials under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-21-6 (Repl. Pamp. 1990).


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that their drug test results should not have been used to prosecute them for possession of cocaine because disclosure of the drug test results violated the privilege against disclosure found in the specific types of social records listed in § 31-21-6. The court held that the drug test results at issue were more akin to investigative reports than social records. Thus, the privilege set forth in § 31-21-6 was inapplicable. The court also held that defendants' guilty pleas precluded them from raising challenges to the sufficiency of the evidence.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions for possession of cocaine were affirmed.

 

500 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Alarid v. Sec'y of the N.M. Dep't of Taxation & Revenue


No. 13,887


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 23; 1994-NMCA-075; 878 P.2d 341; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 71; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 939



June 7, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed June 23, 1994, Denied July 19, 1994. Released for Publication July 19, 1994. As Corrected August 31, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. JOE CRUZ CASTELLANO, JR., District Judge



DISPOSITION: We reverse the trial court's summary judgment granted in favor of Plaintiffs as well as the trial court's award of costs to Plaintiffs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Secretary of the New Mexico Department of Taxation and Revenue sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff taxpayers, ordered the secretary to refund state income taxes that the taxpayers paid on their retirement incomes on the grounds that the tax violated the intergovernmental tax immunity doctrine, and awarded court costs to the taxpayers.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers were New Mexico residents and retired employees (or their spouses) of Los Alamos National Laboratory (LANL), which was operated by the University of California (UC) through a contract with the federal government. They paid income taxes on their California retirement income under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-2-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1988). The taxpayers filed a complaint seeking a refund of the taxes, claiming that the tax violated the intergovernmental tax immunity (ITI) doctrine. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the taxpayers on the basis that taxation of their retirement income operated to discriminate against those who dealt with the federal government and the State of California. On appeal, the court reversed the grant of summary judgment. The court held that the tax did not violate the ITI doctrine because the tax fell directly on the taxpayers based on their status as New Mexico residents. They were not so closely connected with the federal government that they could not be viewed as separate entities. The fact that UC operated LANL through federal funding did not make UC into a party with whom the federal government dealt for ITI purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of the taxpayers that directed the secretary to refund state income taxes, and reversed the trial court's award of court costs to the taxpayers.

 

501 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wood


No. 14,949


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


117 N.M. 682; 1994-NMCA-060; 875 P.2d 1113; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 58; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 791



April 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed May 9, 1994, Denied May 27, 1994. Released for Publication June 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY. RALPH W. GALLINI, District Judge



DISPOSITION: The judgment and sentence are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which convicted him of possession of cocaine, contrary to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-31-23(D)(Cum. Supp. 1993).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on suspicion of driving while intoxicated. During the booking procedure, he removed syringes from his pocket, which tested positive for cocaine. On appeal, defendant argued that the trace amount of cocaine he was alleged to have possessed was insufficient to support his conviction, that the possession statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him, and that his conviction violated constitutional protections against double jeopardy. Affirming, the court held that "any amount" as used in § 30-31-23(D) clearly meant that the legislature intended to prohibit possession of any identifiable amount of a controlled substance. Therefore, the clearly identifiable trace amount was sufficient to support the conviction. From the evidence, the court found that the jury could have properly inferred defendant's knowledge of possession. The court found no factual basis in he record to support the double jeopardy claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

502 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Luevano v. Maestas


No. 14,310


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


117 N.M. 580; 1994-NMCA-051; 874 P.2d 788; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 48; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 847



April 6, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for. Released for Publication May 20, 1994. The Docket Number of this Case has been Corrected by the Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Susan M. Conway, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners challenged an order from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which granted defendant neighbors' motion for summary judgment and denied the landowners' motion for declaratory judgment, holding that the neighbors were entitled to use a road that lay between property owned by the landowners and property owned by the neighbors.


OVERVIEW: The landowners acquired a portion of land to which an easement appurtenant in the road had been granted to the neighbors. The landowners filed an action and sought to bar the use of the road to the neighbors, a declaration that the road was a private easement, and permission to extend their fence the length of the road. The district court granted the neighbors' motion for summary judgment and held that the public had a prescriptive easement to use the road. On appeal, the court affirmed. The public acquired rights by implied dedication. There was evidence of the road's reputation as public that supported the general proposition that the road was open to the public. The neighbors produced enough evidence of implied dedication to make a prima facie showing of entitlement to summary judgment, and the landowners were unable to rebut the presumption. The evidence that the road was regarded in the community as a public road, that the county maintained the road, and that the city made significant improvements to it indicated the landowner's intent to make a dedication, the public's reliance, and public benefit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the neighbors on the grounds that the public acquired rights to the road by implied dedication.

 

503 of 795 DOCUMENTS


TBCH, Inc. v. City of Albuquerque


No. 14,522


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


117 N.M. 569; 1994-NMCA-048; 874 P.2d 30; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 42; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 677



March 25, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 11, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. GERARD W. THOMSON, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nightclub sought reversal of an order of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), dismissing its appeal from a declaratory ruling adopted by appellee city. The declaratory ruling purported to explain the meaning of "completely and opaquely covered" female breasts as that term was used in the city's comprehensive zoning code.


OVERVIEW: The nightclub featured female dancers who applied heavy flesh-colored theatrical makeup to their breasts and areolae and affixed flesh-colored plastic circles to their nipples. The city zoning manager notified the nightclub that its dancers' breasts were not "completely and opaquely covered" as required by Albuquerque, N.M., Rev. Ordinances ch. 7, art. XIV, § 5(B)(114)(a). The zoning manager ordered the nightclub to comply with the ordinance. The city planning commission and the city council both approved the zoning manager's ruling, The nightclub then appealed the decision to the district court by writ of certiorari. The district court found against the nightclub. On appeal, the court held that theatrical makeup, which was spread completely over the required surfaces of the dancers' breasts, and the plastic circles, which were placed on the dancers' nipples, satisfied the plain and unambiguous language of the ordinance. The court found that the definition of "cover" did not mean that only some sort of clothing could act as a cover. The court held that the nightclub complied with the zoning code as written, and reversed the district court's order of dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's order of dismissal.

 

504 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Gallegos v. Southwest Cmty. Health Servs.


No. 13,919


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


117 N.M. 481; 1994-NMCA-037; 872 P.2d 899; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 38; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 570



March 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed March 28, 1994, Denied April 14, 1994. Released for Publication April 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. PHILIP R. ASHBY, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient challenged the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) in favor of defendant doctors and hospitals in a medical malpractice suit. The patient claimed that it was error to grant defendants additional peremptory challenges, deny her additional peremptory challenges, and deny her a new trial based on juror misconduct. The doctors appealed the requirement that each party to bear its own costs.


OVERVIEW: The patient brought suit against the hospital and doctors that provided medical care to her mother during pregnancy and the patient's delivery. The trial court granted defendants additional peremptory challenges, but denied additional challenges to the patient. The jury returned a verdict in favor of defendants and the patient's motion for a new trial was denied. All parties were ordered to bear their own costs. The court affirmed the decisions. It found that the trial court properly awarded defendants additional challenges as the evidence demonstrated their conflicting interests. Further, the rule did not authorize equalization of peremptory challenges and did not violate the patient's rights to equal protection. The court also found that a statement made by a juror to an alternate juror that there would be a verdict that day did not constitute jury misconduct as the communication concerned only the chronological progress of the trial and not the merits of the case. Finally, the court affirmed the order requiring each party to bear their own costs based on the patient's indigency as she did not engage in bad faith or abusive litigation tactics and her claims were not frivolous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of defendants in the patient's medical malpractice suit and the trial court's order requiring that the parties bear their own costs.

 

505 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Powell v. N.M. State Highway & Transp. Dep't


No. 14,395


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


117 N.M. 415; 1994-NMCA-035; 872 P.2d 388; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 30; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 581



March 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed March 23, 1994, Denied April 6, 1994. Released for Publication April 11, 1994. As Corrected May 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. STEVE HERRERA, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured passenger challenged an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted the motion of defendant State Highway and Transportation Department for summary judgment, and upheld the constitutionality of the notice provision under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-16(B) (1989).


OVERVIEW: The injured passenger's left leg was severed in a car accident when the car in which he was riding left the road and struck a blunt-edge guardrail installed and maintained by the department. The passenger notified the department that he intended to file a claim. The department filed a motion for summary judgment, claiming that the injured passenger failed to provide timely notice under § 41-4-16. The injured passenger responded by claiming that the 90-day provision under § 41-4-16(A), (B) was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the department's motion. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court ruled that there was no evidence in the police report that any of the passengers' injuries were caused by the guardrail; therefore, the police report was insufficient as a matter of law to provide actual notice of the injured passenger's potential claim. The department did not have notice that the accident would have resulted in litigation. Finally, the court held that the injured passenger failed to present evidence to show that he was under any legal disability or otherwise unable to comply with the statutory notice provisions; therefore, his constitutional challenge was denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the department.
