Hoffman v. Taxation & Revenue Dep't, Property Tax Div.


No. 14,415


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


117 N.M. 263; 1994-NMCA-032; 871 P.2d 27; 1994 N.M. App. LEXIS 16; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 585



February 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for. Released for Publication March 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. SUSAN CONWAY, District Judge



DISPOSITION: For the reasons stated above, we reverse and remand to the trial court with instructions to void the tax sale. Costs on appeal are awarded to Hoffman.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which determined that the taxpayer's complaint to avoid conveyance after a tax sale by defendant state was barred by the two-year statute of limitations. The trial court later stayed its judgment pending appeal and enjoined defendant buyer from selling or encumbering the property at issue.


OVERVIEW: The delinquent taxpayer contended that the tax sale was invalid as the state failed to comply with either statutory or constitutional due process requirements prior to the tax sale in which her real property was sold for delinquent taxes by the state. She contended that the state violated her constitutional right to minimum due process by failing to provide notice of the impending tax sale that adversely affected her property interest. The state contended that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-38-70 barred the taxpayer from contesting the tax sale even if the state failed to comply with statutory and constitutional due process notice requirements. The court held that the trial court's imposition of the statute of limitations was error because, based on the record, it held that the state failed to give the taxpayer minimum due process notice of the impending tax sale. It further held that the tax sale was invalid as a result of that due process violation under both U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and N.M. Const. art. II, § 18.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that determined the taxpayer's complaint to avoid conveyance after a tax sale by the state was barred and remanded to the trial court with instructions to void the tax sale.

 

507 of 795 DOCUMENTS


New Mex. Taxation & Revenue Dep't v. Whitener


No. 13,092


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


117 N.M. 130; 1993-NMCA-161; 869 P.2d 829; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 170; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 391



December 21, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed January 10, 1994, Granted February 9, 1994. Released for Publication March 1, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM AN ADMINISTRATIVE HEARING OF THE TAXATION AND REVENUE DEPARTMENT. GERALD B. RICHARDSON, Hearing Officer


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff New Mexico Taxation and Revenue Department sought review of a decision and order of a hearing officer of the New Mexico Taxation and Revenue Department, which granted defendant's protest to taxes imposed on him under the Controlled Substance Tax Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 7-18A-1 to 18A-7 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to distribute. Thereafter, the Department levied an assessment representing the tax, penalty, and interest under the Controlled Substance Tax Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 7-18A-1 to 7-18A-7 (1993). Following a hearing held on defendant's protest, the hearing officer found and concluded that the tax violated defendant's right against double jeopardy. Affirming the decision, the court determined that the controlled-substance tax was unconstitutional as applied to defendant. Noting that the fact that the assessment was labeled a "tax" was not dispositive of the double jeopardy issue, the court ruled that defendant rebutted the presumption that the tax assessment was correct by showing how he had previously been convicted of a drug offense involving the same controlled substances that formed the basis of the assessment, that the burden then shifted to the Department to show the correctness of the assessed tax, and that the Department did not present evidence showing that the assessment was proportionate to the claimed remedial goals and was therefore not a prohibited second penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the hearing officer's decision and order.

 

508 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Vest v. State ex rel. N.M. Human Servs. Dep't (In re Francisco A.)


No. 13,358


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 708; 1993-NMCA-144; 866 P.2d 1175; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 148; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 96



November 29, 1993, Decided  
November 29, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Not Applied For. Released for Publication January 4, 1994. As Corrected February 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CHILDREN'S COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. STEVE HERRERA, Children's Court Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foster parent filed a petition to adopt three minor children. Plaintiffs, husband and wife, also filed a petition to adopt the children. By stipulation, the cases were consolidated. The Children's Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) granted the petition filed by the husband and wife and awarded the foster parent visitation rights. Intervenor, the New Mexico Human Services Department (HSD), and the foster parent appealed.


OVERVIEW: The foster parent had custody of the children for three years. HSD removed the children from the foster parent's home and placed them with the husband and wife. The parties then filed competing adoption petitions. On appeal, HSD argued that the children's court lacked jurisdiction to consider the foster parent's petition or to award her visitation rights. The foster parent cross-appealed, claiming that the children's court did not have jurisdiction to grant the opposing petition prior to the termination of her foster parent rights. The court held (1) N.M. Stat. § 40-7-34(A) limited the children's court's power to grant an adoption petition but did not place any limitations on its jurisdiction, (2) the children's court had authority to award visitation to the foster parent but it erred is so doing because it based the visitation decision solely on the children's wishes, (3) HSD was not required to terminate the foster parent's parental rights prior to placing the children with the husband and wife, and (4) HSD's failure to hold a timely hearing regarding the removal of the children not deprive the children's court of the authority to grant the petition filed by the husband and wife.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

509 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hernandez


No. 14,897


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 562; 1993-NMCA-132; 865 P.2d 1206; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 129; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 19



October 19, 1993, Decided  
October 19, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied November 29, 1993. Released for Publication December 14, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. ROSS C. SANCHEZ, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) after he was found guilty of the offenses of auto burglary and possession of burglary tools.


OVERVIEW: The victim parked his car in a store's parking lot. He found the passenger door ajar when he returned. The ignition switch was also damaged. A security guard informed him that he had seen defendant getting out of the car. The security guard apprehended defendant. He admitted to the security guard that he had been the car. Defendant was found guilty of auto burglary and possession of burglary tools. He appealed from those convictions, which were affirmed. The burglary statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-16-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1984), required an unauthorized entry. By comparison, unauthorized entry was not an element of the offenses of unlawful taking of a vehicle, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-3-504 (Repl. Pamp. 1989), or tampering with a vehicle, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-3-506 (Repl. Pamp. 1989). Therefore, the court rejected defendant reliance on the specific-statute doctrine. Furthermore, the evidence was sufficient to support a burglary conviction because the theft of a vehicle could be an offense committed therein. The trial court did not error when it refused to suppress defendant's statements to the security guard because that individual was not acting as a government agent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for the offenses of auto burglary and possession of burglary tools.

Padilla v. Montano


No. 13,768


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 398; 1993-NMCA-127; 862 P.2d 1257; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 111; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1133



September 29, 1993, Decided  
September 29, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Not Applied For. Released for Publication November 8, 1993. As Corrected December 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GRANT COUNTY. V. LEE VESELY, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, mother and child, sought review of the decision of the District Court of Grant County (New Mexico) barring their actions for past child support against respondent father pursuant to the Uniform Parentage Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-11-1 to -23 (Repl. Pamp. 1989).


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a complaint to establish paternity in the father and for past and future child support. Later, an amended complaint was filed, which added the child as a party to the action. The trial court found that the actions of the mother and child for past support were barred or limited pursuant to the general "catch-all" statute of limitations and not the statute of limitations under the Act. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the general "catch-all" statute of limitations did not apply to actions to collect past child support and the applicable statute of limitations for support proceedings was provided by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-11-23. The court also concluded that the trial court erred when calculating past child support for not considering other sources of revenue other than the father's gross monthly income. Finally, the court ruled that the mother was not entitled to prejudgment interest on the past support because the amount was unliquidated until the action was brought and a figure set by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in part and reversed in part. The court remanded the matter to the trial court for determination of the appropriate amount and apportionment of past child support between the mother and the child.

Dick v. City of Portales


No. 14,236


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 472; 1993-NMCA-125; 863 P.2d 1093; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 115; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1145



September 22, 1993, Decided  
September 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Granted December 16, 1993. Released for Publication November 16, 1993. As Amended April 4, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. STEVE HERRERA, DISTRICT JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner business owners sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which affirmed a decision by respondent alcohol and gaming division to deny that a liquor license be transferred to the business owners after a public hearing was held. The alcohol and gaming division had previously granted preliminary approval for the transfer of the license.


OVERVIEW: The alcohol and gaming division granted preliminary approval for the transfer and then respondent city held a public hearing in which local citizens testified against the transfer. Subsequent to the hearing, the alcohol and gaming division denied the transfer and this decision was affirmed by the district court. On appeal, the court affirmed holding that the decision to deny the transfer was supported by substantial evidence and was not arbitrary, capricious, or an abuse of discretion. The court found that the objection that the decision was not supported by substantial evidence had not been raised below and that the business owners failed to introduce any evidence. The court held that as to the argument that the decision denied them due process under the law, the state had broad police powers to grant or deny a liquor license and the ownership of a liquor license was a privilege and not a right. The court held that the delegation of the legislative authority to transfer a license on moral as well as public health and safety grounds were within the traditional definition of the state's police power and therefore the denial had to stand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court denying the transfer of the liquor license to the business owners.

Neff v. State ex rel. Taxation & Revenue Dep't


No. 13,531


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 240; 1993-NMCA-116; 861 P.2d 281; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 103; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 988; 17 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1709



September 8, 1993, Decided  
September 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for. Released for Publication October 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Steve Herrera, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Sante Fe County (New Mexico) that dismissed the taxpayer's complaint as not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: Where the trial court dismissed the taxpayer's suit, the court held that the trial court erred in proceeding with a motions hearing without giving notice to first taxpayers and, therefore, the case was reversed as to them only. The district court's failure to give notice to the first taxpayer's new attorney of the hearing on the motion to dismiss and motion for summary judgment resulted in a denial of due process. With respect to the second taxpayers, the court found that the trial court correctly determined that it lacked jurisdiction because of the failure to timely appeal, as required by the Tax Administration Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-1-26 (1978). It was undisputed that the second taxpayers failed to follow the Act as to the time constraints or as to the manner in which they asserted their claim, which was mandatory before questioning in court the constitutionality of a tax. As there was a complete remedy otherwise provided by statute, and obviously intended to be exclusive, the issue was not subject to disposition by declaratory judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the judgment dismissing the first taxpayer's complaint, where he was not given notice of the hearing on the motion to dismiss. The court affirmed that part of the judgment dismissing the second taxpayer's complaint.

State v. Ramos


No. 13,734


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 123; 1993-NMCA-089; 860 P.2d 765; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 82; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 924

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied September 3, 1993. Released for Publication September 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SIERRA COUNTY. EDMUND H. KASE, III, District Judge



DISPOSITION: For the reasons discussed herein, we affirm Defendant's convictions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged the decision of the District Court of Sierra County (New Mexico) that convicted her on eight counts of fraudulent practices contrary to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 58-13B-30 of the New Mexico Securities Act of 1986.


OVERVIEW: Criminal appellant was convicted on eight counts of securities fraud. On appeal, appellant first contended that the portions of the Securities Act she was convicted of violating were unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Specifically, appellant asserted that N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 58-13B-30 and 58-13B-2V were vague and that section 58-13B-30 was overbroad because of the statutes' definitions of securities. Appellant's next contention was a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. The appellate court found that appellant failed to demonstrate that he trial counsel's performance fell below the required standard. The court concluded that the evidence presented was substantial to support the trial court's conviction.


OUTCOME: Appellate court affirmed criminal appellant's convictions when the court found that the portions of the Securities Act were not unconstitutional, she was not deprived of ineffective assistance of counsel, her convictions were supported by substantial evidence, and the trial court did not err in rejecting a proffered jury instruction.

Beavers v. Johnson Controls World Servs.


No. 13,610


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 29; 1993-NMCA-088; 859 P.2d 497; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 87; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 922



July 26, 1993, Decided  
July 26, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Granted September 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF RIO ARRIBA COUNTY. Steve Herrera, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employer and supervisor, challenged a decision of the District Court of Rio Arriba County (New Mexico), which awarded judgment to appellee employee for mental and emotional damages proximately resulting from treatment by the supervisor under the theory of prima facie tort.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that she suffered mental and emotional damages as a result of the supervisor's harassment. Almost three years after the events giving rise to the cause of action, a decision was rendered in New Mexico which recognized a cause of action for prima facie tort as a specific tort cause of action and it was under this theory that the employee's cause went to trial. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the employee. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the decision recognizing a prima facie tort should not be applied retroactively. It found that the recognition of a prima facie tort as a cause of action imposed significant new duties and conditions and took away previously existing rights. Further, the prima facie tort punished conduct that was lawful until the case recognizing the tort was decided. Finally, retrospective application would not further all purposes of the prima facie tort, as the goals of compensation and punishment arguably would be advanced by retroactive application, the goal of deterrence would not be advanced.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment entered in the employee's favor in her suit against appellees under a prima facie tort theory and remanded the matter with directions to dismiss the employee's complaint against appellees.

Citizens for Incorporation v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 13061


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 710; 1993-NMCA-069; 858 P.2d 86; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 59; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 666



June 2, 1993, Decided  
June 2, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied July 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. PHILIP R. ASHBY, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, citizen corporation and resident, sought review of the decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which affirmed the decision of respondent, Bernalillo County Board of Commissioners (board), denying petitioners' request for an incorporation election and dismissing petitioners' census reimbursement claim.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed a petition and map for incorporation with the board. Petitioners paid for a census in order to comply with the board's census request. The board voted not to allow an incorporation election because the petition did not meet the requisite statutory requirements. The district court consolidated petitioners' summary judgment motion and petition for review, dismissed petitioners' complaint, and upheld the board's action. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that petition offered by petitioners did not comply with the statutory "swear or affirm" requirement of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-2-1(A)(4)(a)(1) because nothing in the petition subjected petitioners to the penalty of perjury. Further, the accompanying map was not an accurate map or plat as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-2-1(B)(1) because people could not determine whether their property was within the proposed incorporation area. Moreover, regardless of whether the legislative or administrative standard of review was applied, the district court's compliance findings were supported by substantial evidence. Finally, petitioners were required to provide census funds under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-2-1(B)(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court that affirmed the board's decision denying petitioners' request for an incorporation election and dismissing petitioners' census reimbursement claim.

State ex rel. Dep't of Pub. Safety, State Police Div. v. One 1990 Chevrolet Pickup


Nos. 13,728, 13,731, 14,242


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 644; 1993-NMCA-068; 857 P.2d 44; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 60; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 680



June 1, 1993, Decided  
June 1, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied July 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. PATRICIO M. SERNA, District Judge; APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LUNA COUNTY. MANUEL D.V. SAUCEDO, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) and the District Court of Luna County (New Mexico), the court considered whether NMSA 1978, § 30-31-34(D) (Repl. Pamp. 1989) (New Mexico) allowed for the forfeiture of vehicles when a small amount of a controlled substance was discovered in the possession of the owners.


OVERVIEW: Each case raised the issue of whether § 30-31-34(D) (Repl. Pamp. 1989) (New Mexico), provided for forfeiture of vehicles and other property when the owner of the property was in possession of a small amount of controlled substances designed solely for personal use. The trial courts came to opposite conclusions. The court found that, in order for property to be forfeited under the statute, possession of a controlled substance had to be for the purpose of sale. In reaching its determination, the court found that the 1981 amendment to the statute, as well as the comments to § 505(a)(4) of the Uniform Controlled Substance Act (USCA), 9 U.L.A., Part II, 834 (1988), after which the state statute was modeled, mandated that forfeiture should be enforced only where the controlled substance possessed was meant for sale. Prior caselaw had not been based on the amended statute, and so was not controlling. The contention that the USCA could not be relied upon in interpreting New Mexico law was rejected. The claim of unconstitutional vagueness was not reached as it was mooted by the decision of the court. Likewise, a motion to transfer possession of the vehicle pending appeal was moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying forfeiture in one case, and did not reach the issues concerning that trial court's order granting the motion to transfer possession of the vehicle pending appeal. In the other appeal, the court reversed the trial court's order of forfeiture.

No. 13620

NCR Corp. v. Taxation & Revenue Dep't


No. 13035


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 612; 1993-NMCA-060; 856 P.2d 982; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 54; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 596

May 6, 1993, Filed, Decided

The corporation contended that the Foreign Commerce Clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3 prohibited the imposition of a corporate income tax on the corporation's foreign source income.


OVERVIEW: The Taxation and Revenue Department (Department) issued corporate income tax assessments against the corporation for taxes due in 1981 through 1987, plus interest and penalties. Ann. §§ 7-4-10, -11, -14, and -16 (1990) and the statutory formula specified by the Uniform Division of Income for Tax Purposes Act, there was a clear legislative intent to impose the tax on property, payroll, and sales of the corporation's unitary business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Taxation and Revenue Department's decision and order that denied the corporation's challenge to four separate deficiency assessments of corporate income tax, penalty, and interest. The court remanded, however for determination by the hearing officer of the amount of the allowable adjustment from the additional taxes imposed, because of the corporation's previous payment of taxes for certain of the years in question.

 

520 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Ramirez v. City of Santa Fe


No. 13312


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 417; 1993-NMCA-049; 852 P.2d 690; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 40; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 457



April 7, 1993, Decided  
April 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Not Applied For. Released For Publication May 18, 1993. As Corrected July 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. JOE CRUZ CASTELLANO, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners challenged the dismissal by the District Court Of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) of their petition for writ of certiorari seeking judicial review of defendant city council's reclassification of a tract from residential to industrial and commercial due to lack of standing to bring the action against defendants, city, city council members, and urban policy committee members, and intervenor developer, and untimely filing.


OVERVIEW: The city council granted an amendment to the general plan that reclassified a tract of land from residential to industrial and commercial. When the landowners filed a petition for writ of certiorari seeking judicial review of the city council's decision, the district court dismissed the petition due to two jurisdictional defects: lack of standing and the untimely filing of the petition for writ of certiorari. On appeal, the court reversed the district court's order. The landowners alleged the following injuries: fear of increased noise, crime, and pollution; detrimental effect on aesthetics; declining property values; traffic hazards; and increased drainage and flooding. The court held that the threat of aesthetic, quality of life, and property harm alleged by the landowners, whose residential properties were located near the land included in the amendment, conferred standing on them. The court held that the date from which the city council's decision triggered the 30-day period for filing a petition for writ of certiorari pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-21-9(A) was the date the city council made its final decision. Therefore, the petition for writ of certiorari was timely filed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's order that the landowners lacked standing and that the petition for writ of certiorari was not timely filed. The court remanded the case to the district court with instructions to determine certain issues.

Hammonds v. Freymiller Trucking, Inc.


No. 13,639


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 364; 1993-NMCA-030; 851 P.2d 486; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 21; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 420

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. JOHN W. POPE, Workers' Compensation Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker challenged a judgment of the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Administration, which granted summary judgment to appellee employer and dismissed the workers' claims under the Workers' Compensation Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-1 to -70 (1991) for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The worker, a New Mexico resident, sustained a work-related injury in New Mexico while employed as an interstate truck driver. The worker received workers' compensation benefits under Indiana law and then filed a claim in New Mexico. The trial court granted the employers' motion for summary judgment on the ground that New Mexico lacked jurisdiction over the claim under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-66. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case. The employer was subject to the Workers' Compensation Act because it employed more than three workers in total, including workers employed outside New Mexico. Moreover, the statutory exemption for employers involved in interstate commerce did not apply in this case. The legislature had intended for out-of-state employers employing fewer than three workers in the State of New Mexico to be exempt only from the administrative burden of obtaining and filing proof of workers' compensation insurance complying with New Mexico's statutory requirements but not from liability for payment of benefits under the Act if they were otherwise subject to New Mexico's workers' compensation law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the Workers' Compensation Administration for further proceedings.

State v. Powell


No. 13756


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 188; 1993-NMCA-021; 848 P.2d 1115; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 17; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 310



February 15, 1993, Decided  
February 15, 1993, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 17, 1993. Certiorari not Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY. R. W. GALLINI, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which convicted defendant of unlawful carrying of a firearm in an establishment licensed to dispense alcoholic beverages in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-7-3(A) (1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to a bar after he was released from jail on charges arising from a stabbing at a bar. Defendant arrived at the bar and laid a knife on the bar, telling the bartender that he was checking his weapon so that there would not be any problems. A couple of hours later he handed her a loaded pistol, again saying that he wanted to avoid problems. The police were called and defendant was charged with unlawful carrying of a firearm in an establishment licensed to dispense alcoholic beverages. Defendant was convicted as charged. Defendant sought review, contending that the State was required, but failed, to prove his conscious wrongdoing. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that proof of an evil intent was not necessary to convict for a violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-7-3(A). The intent element in firearm-possession offenses was typically no more than knowledge of possession.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful carrying of a firearm in an establishment licensed to dispense alcoholic beverages.

 

523 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Castleman


Nos. 13,673/13,317 (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 467; 1993-NMCA-019; 863 P.2d 1088; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 118; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1130



February 11, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari Filed March 2, 1993, Granted April 12, 1993, Quashed September 16, 1993. Released for Publication November 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: 13,673: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY. R. W. GALLINI, DISTRICT JUDGE. 13,317: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. W.C. WOODY SMITH, DISTRICT JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment from the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which convicted them of distribution of an imitation controlled substance in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-31A-4 (1989), a provision of the Imitation Controlled Substances Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 30-31A-1 to -15 (1989).


OVERVIEW: A police officer met with one defendant and told her that he wanted to buy cocaine. She produced a packet, which was given to the officer in exchange for $ 50. The second defendant was asked by an undercover police officer if he had a "rock," a street name for a measure of cocaine. Defendant gave the officer a small foil packet in exchange for $ 20. Both defendants challenged the Act as being unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. One defendant also contended that the Act deprived him of equal protection. The other defendant further raised issues concerning the jury instructions in her case and the sufficiency of the evidence to convict her. The court concluded that the Act was not unconstitutionally vague. A person of ordinary intelligence could have determined that defendants' conduct fell within the class of acts prohibited by the statute. Furthermore, the Act was not unconstitutionally overbroad in violation of the First Amendment because its prohibitions were addressed to conduct, not speech. The Act did not violate equal protection, and the challenges to the jury instruction and the sufficiency of the evidence were rejected. Defendants' convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Rivera


No. 13540


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. Fred A. Watson, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which convicted defendant of unlawful carrying of a firearm in a licensed liquor establishment and negligent use of a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed a car in which defendant was a passenger strike another car in the parking lot of a lounge. When the officer approached the car to investigate, he saw defendant holding a small caliber handgun, pointed toward the driver of the car. Defendant was convicted of unlawful carrying of a firearm in a licensed liquor establishment and negligent use of a deadly weapon. On appeal, he alleged that the negligent use of a deadly weapon statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-7-4 (Repl. Pamp. 1984), violated his right to bear arms under the New Mexico Constitution; that § 30-7-4 was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague; and that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions. Upon review, the court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that: (1) § 30-7-4 did not infringe on defendant's right to bear arms because the right to bear arms under the state constitution was not absolute, and defendant's right to bear arms was circumscribed by the conditions under which he sought to assert the right; (2) § 30-7-4 was not unconstitutionally overbroad and vague; and (3) the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for unlawful carrying of a firearm in a licensed liquor establishment and negligent use of a deadly weapon.

Labalbo v. Hymes


No. 11094


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 314; 1993-NMCA-010; 850 P.2d 1017; 1993 N.M. App. LEXIS 26; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 385



January 15, 1993, Decided  
January 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 2, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. ALBERT S. MURDOCH, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, guardians of their daughter, appealed from the order of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) that denied their request for damages and a preliminary injunction in a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action that sought to enjoin defendants, a group home for retarded citizens and associated persons, from discharging their daughter from a private home for the developmentally disabled.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, guardians of their daughter, filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim in district court against defendants, a group home for retarded citizens and associated persons, that sought damages and a preliminary injunction that would enjoin defendants from discharging their daughter from a private home for the developmentally disabled. Plaintiffs alleged that defendants' discharge decision denied their daughter pre-deprivation procedural due process. The district court denied plaintiffs' requested relief. The court vacated the order denying injunctive relief, holding that a private entity that was under state contract to provide services to mentally disabled persons was a state actor when it made decisions regarding the discharge of those persons under its care. The court held that the district court's mistaken conclusion that defendants were not state actors foreclosed the possibility of it finding that plaintiffs suffered irreparable injury, and that they had a substantial likelihood of success on the merits. The court reinstated plaintiffs' § 1983 action and ordered a stay of the discharge procedures pending review of the merits of the § 1983 claim.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the district court's order that denied injunctive relief to plaintiffs', guardians of their daughter, and reinstated a claim which alleged that defendants', a group home for retarded citizens and associated persons, decision to discharge plaintiffs' daughter from a private group home was a denial of pre-deprivation procedural due process because defendants acted under color of state law in making the discharge decision.

State v. Cherryhomes


No. 13479


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


114 N.M. 495; 1992-NMCA-111; 840 P.2d 1261; 1992 N.M. App. LEXIS 79; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1104



October 6, 1992, Decided  
October 6, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied November 18, 1992. Released for Publication November 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. James L. Shuler, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico),which held him in criminal contempt for failure to comply with a court order and imposed a fine against him.


OVERVIEW: The district court held defendant in contempt for failure to comply with a court order. The order, issued on the basis of a local rule outlining appropriate dress in district court, required defendant, an attorney, to wear a conventional tie when he appeared in the district judge's courtroom. Defendant, contrary to the district judge's instructions had worn a bandanna. On appeal, defendant argued that his dress caused no disruption, that the judge required him to comply with a unique and personal interpretation of the local rule, and that the judge's ruling infringed defendant's First Amendment right of free expression. Because the evidence indicated that defendant violated a court order, the district court had the discretion to exercise its inherent power to issue a contempt sanction to preserve its authority and maintain respect for the courts and the court concluded that no abuse of discretion occurred. The court noted that defendant was required to obey the order, even if it was subject to reversal on constitutional grounds. Moreover, the district court judge's refusal to recuse himself was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the contempt citation entered against defendant and the fine imposed by the district court.

State v. Powell


No. 13398


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


114 N.M. 395; 1992-NMCA-086; 839 P.2d 139; 1992 N.M. App. LEXIS 78; 20 Media L. Rep. 1841



July 27, 1992, Decided  
July 27, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GRANT COUNTY. V. LEE VESELY, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the District Court of Grant County (New Mexico), which dismissed the complaint charging defendant with criminal libel in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-11-1 (1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a university teacher, was convicted of criminal libel in magistrate court based on accusations he had made against the university's acting vice-president for academic affairs. On appeal, the trial court dismissed the complaint, holding that § 30-11-1 was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to libel of public officials or public figures. On further appeal, the court affirmed on other grounds, holding that the criminal libel statute was unconstitutional insofar as it applied to a public statement involving a matter of public concern. The court held that the Constitution prohibited a conviction for criminal libel for public defamation made without actual malice on a matter of public concern. The court rejected the state's argument that any constitutional defect in the statute could be cured by requiring the trial court to instruct the jury on "actual malice." Because the charge against defendant was predicated on public statements relating to the performance of the administration of a public institution of higher learning and thus was a matter of public concern, defendant could not constitutionally be prosecuted under § 30-11-1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the complaint against defendant for criminal libel.

Chevron Res. by Blatnik v. N.M. Superintendent of Ins.


No. 13499


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


114 N.M. 371; 1992-NMCA-081; 838 P.2d 988; 1992 N.M. App. LEXIS 76



July 9, 1992, Decided  
July 9, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied August 26, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. JOHN W. POPE, Workers' Compensation Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer company (company), by and through its assignee employee worker (worker), filed an action against appellees, the New Mexico Subsequent Injury Fund (fund) and state insurance superintendent, challenging a decision of the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Administration denying the worker's claim for benefits under the Subsequent Injury Act (SIA), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 52-2-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The worker, a miner, filed a claim to receive workers' compensation benefits from the fund pursuant to the SIA, based on alleged disability resulting from aggravation of pre-existing lung disease, due to his employment with the company. He also filed an alternative claim for benefits under the New Mexico Occupation Disease Disablement Law (ODDL), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 52-3-1 et seq. The fund denied the claim. After a hearing, during which evidence was taken both supporting and refuting the worker's claim that his disability was caused by his employment, a workers' compensation judge (WCJ) ruled that the worker did not suffer a compensable injury under the Workers' Compensation Act (WCA) and that the SIA did not apply to benefits payable under the ODDL. On appeal, the court affirmed the WCJ's decision. The court held that the WCJ's finding that the worker's disability was not caused by his employment was not in error because it was rationally based upon the evidence, and thus the worker was not eligible for SIA benefits arising under the WCA. Benefits payable under the ODDL were not compensable under the SIA because the SIA made no reference to the ODDL, but only to the WCA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision administration denying the worker's claim for benefits under the SIA.

Southard v. Fox


No. 12117


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 774; 1992-NMCA-045; 833 P.2d 251; 1992 N.M. App. LEXIS 97; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 557



April 21, 1992  
April 21, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended. Second Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. REBECCA SITTERLY, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant car driver sought review of a decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which entered an award of prejudgment interest in connection with a jury verdict stemming from a personal injury action brought by plaintiff injured person.


OVERVIEW: The driver and the injured person were involved in an automobile collision. The injured person filed a personal injury action against the driver for damages. The driver admitted liability and the jury returned a verdict of $ 130,000. The trial court awarded the injured person prejudgment interest at the rate of eight percent per year. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 56-8-4(B) was not ambiguous and applied to all actions and was not limited to certain or specific actions, such as those only based on contract or in which damages were ascertainable before trial. The statute gave the trial court discretion to award prejudgment interest after considering whether the plaintiff was the cause of unreasonable delay or whether defendant made a reasonable and timely offer of settlement. The trial court properly considered the factors required by the statute in making its award of prejudgment interest and did not abuse its discretion. The trial court found that the injured person did not cause unreasonable delay in adjudicating her claims and the driver did not dispute those findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which entered an award of prejudgment interest in connection with a jury verdict stemming from a personal injury action brought by the injured person against the driver.

City of Albuquerque v. Sanchez


No. 13350


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 721; 1992-NMCA-038; 832 P.2d 412; 1992 N.M. App. LEXIS 30; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 518



April 1, 1992  
April 1, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiori not applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. GREGORY D. GRIEGO, Workers' Compensation Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the decision of the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Administration, which the health care provider selected by appellee worker as the worker's health care provider.


OVERVIEW: The worker was injured while working for the employer. The employer designated a doctor as the worker's health care provider. The worker notified the employer that he was designating the physician as his treating physician. The employer objected to this designation and filed a motion to strike the worker's notification. The court affirmed the trial court's decision granting judgment for the worker. Under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-49, because the employer designated the worker's health care provider, the worker was entitled to change his health care provider after the expiration of the initial 60 day period. The worker substantially complied with the statutory provisions requiring him to give the employer 10 days notice of the change along with the name and address of his physician. The employer failed to meet its burden of proof and demonstrate that the physician would not provide reasonable care to the worker. The trial court properly treated the employer's objection to the worker's selection of a health care provider as a request for change of health care provider. The worker had unfettered discretion to choose his own physician after the expiration of the 60 day period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

GTE Southwest, Inc. v. Taxation & Revenue Dep't


No. 12419


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 610; 1992-NMCA-024; 830 P.2d 162; 1992 N.M. App. LEXIS 19; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 411



February 27, 1992  
February 27, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 8, 1992. As Amended. Second Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TAXATION AND REVENUE DEPARTMENT. GERALD B. RICHARDSON, Hearing Officer


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff telephone company taxpayer sought review of an order entered by defendant Taxation and Revenue Department (New Mexico) that denied its protest of an assessment for gross receipts tax on access and ancillary service charges paid by interstate carriers and pass-throughs of municipal franchise fees paid by customers. The taxpayer also challenged the penalty assessed against it for its delay in paying the protested tax.


OVERVIEW: The period for which the protested taxes were assessed began on the date of the AT&T divestiture and concluded on the effective of a statutory amendment that clearly deducted access charges from gross receipts. The court held that the gross receipts tax was properly assessed on receipts for ancillary services and for pass-throughs of franchise fees, but that receipts for access services were not taxable. The provisions of the New Mexico Gross Receipts and Compensating Tax Act (act), specifically N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-9-55, in effect during the relevant time were construed to encompass tax deductions for all "interstate messages" regardless of whether the receipt related only to an intrastate component of the interstate transmission. Receipts from access charges were "receipts from transmitting messages" and not taxable. Receipts from charges for ancillary billing services related to the provision of interstate phone service but were not "receipts from transmitting messages or conversations by telephone" and were not taxable. Franchise fee pass throughs were taxable because they were included in the total amount received by the taxpayer for selling its telephone services.


OUTCOME: The denial of the taxpayer's protest of the gross receipts tax imposed upon access charges and the penalty imposed for the delayed payment of the protested tax was reversed. The denial of the taxpayer's protest of taxes imposed upon ancillary service fees and municipal franchise fee pass-throughs was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. PATRICIO SERNA, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality challenged the decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which reversed the municipality's rejection of appellee land developers' petition to annex land.


OVERVIEW: The municipality contended that the lower court erred in granting the land developers a writ of certiorari to consider the municipality's denial of a land petition, and the lower court's subsequent decision on examination of the merits of the petition to reverse the municipality's denial of annexation. Serrano v. Dep't of Alcoholic Beverage Control


No. 11729


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 444; 1992-NMCA-015; 827 P.2d 159; 1992 N.M. App. LEXIS 9; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 272



February 4, 1992  
February 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari not Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. W. JOHN BRENNAN, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer, a state agency, sought review of an order from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which had reversed and remanded a decision of a state personnel board. Appellee employee, a state alcohol beverage control agent, was terminated by the employer after he failed to meet the law enforcement certification requirements of NMSA 1978, § 29-7-8 (Cum.Supp.1981), and the board had upheld the termination.


OVERVIEW: When the employee was hired , his position as an agent did not fall within the definition of a police officer. Several years later, the definition of a police officer was expanded in NMSA 1978, § 29-7-7(F) (Cum.Supp.1981) to include persons working in a law enforcement agency. The law enforcement certification requirement for police officers in NMSA 1978, § 29-7-8(B) required police officers to obtain certification within 12 months of their employment, which the employee failed to do. The employee claimed that he was exempted or grandfathered from the certification requirement, but the court disagreed and held that his termination was lawful. The court ruled that the employer was a law enforcement agency under NMSA 1978, § 29-7-7(F) (Cum.Supp.1981) and that when NMSA 1978, § 29-7-8 was amended, it required certification for both the permanent appointment and the continued employment of police officers. The change of the heading of § 29-7-8 when it was amended was evidence of legislative intent. In addition, there was no written contract that was impaired, under article II, Section 19, of the New Mexico Constitution, by requiring the employee to meet the certification requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the district court and affirmed the decision of the board.

N.M. State Racing Comm'n v. Yoakum


No. 12556


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 561; 1991-NMCA-153; 829 P.2d 7; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 265; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 377



December 31, 1991  
December 31, 1991, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LINCOLN COUNTY. Robert M. Doughty, II, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant New Mexico State Racing Commission sought review of a decision of the District Court of Lincoln County (New Mexico), which entered judgment finding void the commission's suspension of appellee trainer's license to participate in horse racing in the state for five years pursuant to N.M. St. Rac. Com'n R. 43.53.


OVERVIEW: The suspension had been based on test results indicating that three of the trainer's horses had tested positive for illegal drugs. The trainer contended on appeal that he had been denied procedural due process. The court reversed the judgment in part and remanded the case. As to the first horse, the court noted that N.M. St. Rac. Com'n R. 43.53 (rule) required a hearing as soon as was practicable. The court determined that the commission's delay in granting a hearing was unreasonable given the interest involved, and that because the rule had not been followed, the trainer's suspension based on the positive laboratory tests for the first horse was void. As to the other two horses, the court held that with a full hearing having been held within eight days after notification setting forth the charges, the requirements of the rule had been satisfied, that the hearing and the formal action taken by the commission within 30 days afterward satisfied the requirements of due process, and that the rule was not unconstitutional as applied. The court held that the rule on its face assured a sufficiently timely hearing to satisfy due process safeguards.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment finding void the commission's suspension of the trainer and remanded the case for entry of a new judgment consistent with the court's opinion, with a direction that the trial court should then remand the matter to the commission for further proceedings consistent with the trial court's revised judgment.

State ex rel. Vaughn v. Bernalillo County Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 11710


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO

December 27, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. ALBERT S. "PAT" MURDOCH, District Judge. Cert. not applied for


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which affirmed the order of appellee Bernalillo County Board of County Commissioners' decision to revoke a special-use permit issued to the property owner.


OVERVIEW: The property owner's parcel had been used continuously as a contractor's yard by him and then by his lessee since the late 1960s. In 1976, an amended special use permit was issued to the property owner to allow him to add a warehouse to the site. The permit was expressly granted "for the life of the use." Based on complaints from neighbors, the Bernalillo County Planning Commission voted to cancel the property owner's permit in 1987. The Bernalillo Board of County Commissioners (the Board) affirmed the decision. On appeal, the property owner also challenged the district court's order on rehearing that reaffirmed its prior ruling. The court held that the order should be reversed because the Board had no authority to revoke the permit, which was granted "for the life of the use." The court noted that the Board had other options in pursuing relief, such as seeking an injunction, filing an abatement action, or seeking penalties pursuant to the ordinance in quasi-criminal proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that affirmed the order of the Bernalillo County Board of County Commissioners' decision to revoke a special-use permit issued to the property owner. Feese v. U.S. West Serv. Link, Inc.


No. 12546


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 92; 1991-NMCA-121; 823 P.2d 334; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 229; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 31



October 28, 1991  
October 28, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. JOSEPH N. WILTGEN, Workers' Compensation Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a decision from the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Administration, which awarded temporary total disability benefits and attorney fees to appellee, a workers' compensation claimant. The claimant filed a cross-appeal attacking the constitutionality of the cap on attorney fees awards in workers' compensation cases as limited by NMSA 1978, § 52-1-54(G) (Repl.Pamp.1987).


OVERVIEW: The claimant injured her knees in a fall at her work. She decided to retire, but before her official retirement date, her right knee gave out and she fell at home. She then retired and was awarded total disability benefits for several months after her retirement, as well as attorney fees. The employer asserted that she was not eligible for the benefits because she had voluntarily removed herself from the workforce by retiring. The court affirmed, holding that the issue was not whether the claimant lost wages, but whether she was prevented from engaging in an occupation for remuneration or profit, which was the definition of disability in NMSA 1978, § 52-1-25(A) (Repl.Pamp.1987). The fact that the claimant had retired did not establish that she had voluntarily removed herself from the labor market. The employer claimed that there was insufficient evidence to prove a casual connection between the disability and the earlier injury at work, but there was sufficient medical testimony to support the casual connection. The award of attorney fees was not excessive, and the claimant could not attack the constitutionality of the cap on such fees because her award was below the cap.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the workers' compensation administration.

539 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Gambrel v. Marriott Hotel


No. 12,619


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 668; 1991-NMCA-100; 818 P.2d 869; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 269; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 951



August 15, 1991, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. GREGORY D. GRIEGO, Hearing Officer


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employer and employer's insurer, sought review of a portion of a compensation award by the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Administration, which granted appellee worker's widow death benefits. Appellee State of New Mexico Superintendent of Insurance and the Subsequent Injury Fund (fund) also challenged the employer's actions under the Subsequent Injury Act (SIA).


OVERVIEW: The widow was granted death benefits and the employer and employer's insurer appealed claiming that the widow's claim was barred by the two-year statute of limitations under N.M. Stat. § 52-1-46 (Cum. Supp. 1986). The superintendent and the fund also requested a review arguing that the employer failed to substantially comply with the SIA, the apportioned liability between the employer and the fund was not supported by substantial evidence, and the purpose and the policy of the SIA was violated by assessing liability against the fund in this case. The court affirmed the judgment of the worker's compensation judge (WCJ), but reversed the compensation order insofar as it held the fund liable because the employer did fail to substantially comply with the SIA by failing to seek the worker's signature as to the worker's preexisting condition for a substantial amount of time after the accident. Pursuant to N.M. Stat. § 52-2-6, the employer was required to obtain the signature, and the court found that the employer failed to obtain the signature during the 20 months between when the worker was injured and when he died. The court found no explanation by the employer for the delay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that was entered by the worker's compensation judge in favor of the widow, but reversed the compensation order insofar as it held the fund liable.

 

540 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Trevino


No. 12375


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 804; 1991-NMCA-085; 833 P.2d 1170; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 268; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 212



July 2, 1991  
July 2, 1991, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Affirmed in part by 113 N.M. 780, 833 P.2d 1146.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the trial court (New Mexico), which convicted him of criminal sexual contact of a minor and contributing to the delinquency of a minor. Defendant claimed there was insufficient evidence of use of authority and a merger of the contributing counts and the criminal sexual contact counts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a go-cart track where he employed a 14 and 12-year-old boy in exchange for free rides. Defendant was accused of fondling the genitals of both boys during their tenure at the track. He was convicted of criminal sexual contact of a minor and contributing to the delinquency of a minor (contributing). The court certified the case to the state supreme court for resolution. The court held that: (1) where defendant had ability to place the minor in a confined workstation and the minor testified that he was scared, the jury could infer that defendant used his position to coerce the minor; (2) the court rejected defendant's merger argument stating that contributing required the proof of the additional element that the conduct tended to cause or encourage the delinquency and that defendant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence establishing that element; but (3) where "unlawfulness" was set forth in jury instructions as a required element of the crime of criminal sexual contact of a minor, the court certified the matter for determination of whether the element's absence was meaningful given that the lawfulness of the manner of touching was not in dispute.


OUTCOME: The court would affirm defendant's convictions of criminal contact by a person in position of authority and contributing to the delinquency of a minor. However, because of its uncertainty as to the effect of the omission of the element of "unlawfulness" from the jury instruction regarding criminal sexual contact of a minor, the court certified the matter to the state supreme court.

State v. Scott


No. 12097


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 525; 1991-NMCA-081; 828 P.2d 958; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 263; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 236



June 27, 1991  
June 27, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Granted August 9, 1991. Certiorari Quashed as Improvidently Granted, February 18, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TAOS COUNTY. JOSEPH E. CALDWELL, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions from the District Court of Taos County (New Mexico) for one count of criminal sexual contact of a minor in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-13(B)(Repl. Pamp. 1984), and one count of criminal sexual penetration with great mental anguish in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-11(A)(2)(Repl. Pamp. 1984).


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that defendant, her grandfather, molested her repeatedly from age 6 for over 10 years. Defendant argued that evidence of his past sexual misconduct against the victim was too remote for its probative value to outweigh its prejudicial impact but the court disagreed. Even though the misconduct dated back 10 years, time was only 1 factor to consider. The similarity of the past incidents and the number of incidents weighed in favor of admissibility in that his past sexual misconduct was indicative of a lewd disposition toward the victim. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. Defendant never requested a separate ruling on each incident of molestation and could not raise the issue for the first time on appeal. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in restricting impeachment of the victim's testimony by disallowing extrinsic evidence in the form of witness testimony. Defendant was afforded effective assistance of counsel. Counsel's decision not to call a witness was trial strategy and the result would not have been different if the witness was called. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-13(B)(Repl. Pamp. 1984) was not unconstitutionally vague nor overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for criminal sexual contact of a minor and criminal sexual penetration with great mental anguish.

Health Servs. Div., Health & Env't Dep't v. Temple Baptist Church


No. 10536


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 262; 1991-NMCA-055; 814 P.2d 130; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 162; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 620

May 7, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Santa Fe County; Bruce L. Kaufman, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, church, pastor, principal, and church school, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted judgment in favor of appellee, Health Services Division (division), and enjoined appellants from operating a childcare center without a license.


OVERVIEW: The division initiated a case against appellants based on their operation of a childcare center without a license in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 24-1-5(A). The lower court entered judgment in favor of the division and enjoined appellants from operating its child care center without a license. On appeal, appellants argued that the statutory requirement of obtaining a child care center license violated their right to freely exercise religion. The court affirmed the lower court judgment because § 24-1-5(A) was generally applicable and religion neutral. The court concluded that appellants were not entitled to the relief sought because § 24-1-5(A) required all childcare centers to have a license for operation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment entered in favor of the division that enjoined appellants from operating a childcare center without a license.

State v. Cochran


No. 12226


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 190; 1991-NMCA-051; 812 P.2d 1338; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 157; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 591



April 30, 1991, Decided  
April 30, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 12, 1991. As Amended


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Curry County; Fred T. Hensley, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which convicted him of false voting in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 1-20-8.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of false voting in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 1-20-8. Defendant argued on appeal that he had been selectively prosecuted as a result of the exercise of his right to free speech. Defendant claimed that he had been singled out for prosecution due to his criticism of the police chief, the police department, and other agencies of the city and county. Defendant claimed that he was selected from a number of similarly situated individuals who were not prosecuted. The court found that defendant had failed to establish the requisite elements of a prima facie case of selective prosecution. Assuming that defendant proved the first element of selective prosecution, the court found that the record did not support a showing of discriminatory purpose based on defendant's vocal criticism of local officials. The court also found that defendant did not show that local officials who were the target of his criticism took part in the decision to prosecute. Accordingly, defendant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Apodaca


No. 12,274


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 302; 1991-NMCA-048; 814 P.2d 1030; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 168; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 653



April 25, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied July 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Socorro County; Leslie C. Smith, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the District Court of Socorro County (New Mexico), which denied defendant's motion to suppress and then convicted defendant of possession with intent to distribute marijuana.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant for an alleged violation of the New Mexico safety-belt law. After inquiry regarding the ownership and destination of the vehicle, the officer obtained permission to look in the trunk. There he found a suitcase from which he claimed he detected the odor of marijuana. The suitcase contained the marijuana that formed the basis of defendant's conviction. On appeal, defendant argued, among other things, that the officer did not have reasonable suspicion to justify the initial stop of the vehicle, that the stop was pretextual, that any consent to search was withdrawn before the suitcase was opened, and that the warrantless search of the suitcase was unlawful. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) it was reasonable for the officer to believe a driver or passenger who permitted the shoulder harness to dangle free was not wearing his lap belt either; (2) the evidence at the suppression hearing was sufficient for the trial court to have concluded that the stop was not pretextual; and (3) where the officer smelled the odor of marijuana and thought he saw marijuana on the handle of the suitcase, he had probable cause to search the suitcase and the entire vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of possession with intent to distribute marijuana.

 

545 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Leiding


No. 11775


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 143; 1991-NMCA-043; 812 P.2d 797; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 154; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 559



April 23, 1991, Decided  
April 23, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Bernalillo County; Frank H. Allen, Jr., District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) for second- and third-degree criminal sexual penetration (CSP).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of having sex with his patients. On appeal he contended that consensual sex between a therapist and his adult patient was not a crime in New Mexico because the state legislature had not enacted a criminal statute concerning sexual relations specifically between a therapist and a patient. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-11 required the state to prove that the offense of CSP was committed through the use of force or coercion. Defendant's argument focused on the state's use the theory of "transference" to prove that the victim suffered from a mental condition rendering him incapable of understanding the nature and consequences of the sexual acts with defendant, and thus constituted coercion. The court concluded that in the absence of more precise statutory language, the legislature did not intend "transference" to be sufficient to bring defendant's conduct under the grasp of the CSP statute and that the state in prosecuting defendant under the CSP statute based on the theory of the transference phenomenon exceeded the limits of the statute's application. The court held that defendant's conduct did not constitute the crimes of second- and third-degree CSP.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the convictions of second- and third-degree CSP and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions that the criminal charges be dismissed and defendant discharged.

State v. Riddall


No. 11,928


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 78; 1991-NMCA-033; 811 P.2d 576; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 144; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 454



March 26, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: March 26, 1991, Filed
 [*1] Certiorari Denied May 8, 1991. As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Chaves County; Alvin F. Jones, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), which convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a switchblade under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-7-8 (1978) and unlawful carrying of a deadly weapon under N. M. Stat. Ann. § 30-7-2 (1978).


OVERVIEW: Defendant showed his butterfly knife while working at a store. The police were called. The trial court convicted defendant for unlawful possession of a switchblade and unlawful carrying a deadly weapon. The court affirmed the conviction for unlawful possession but reversed the conviction for unlawful carrying. The court concluded that a butterfly knife was within the definition of "switchblade" in N. M. Stat. Ann. § 30-7-8 (1978). The court held that the definition was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found no error in the admission of a demonstration of how such knives were commonly opened. The court found no error in the joinder of the misdemeanor charges with the felony charge. Even if there were error, the court did not see any prejudice to defendant. Having concluded that the knife was a switchblade and that ample evidence that it was a switchblade was presented, the court concluded that there was sufficient evidence that the knife was a deadly weapon within the meaning of N.M. Stat. § 30-7-2 (1978). However, the court held that the two convictions merged and, consequently, defendant should not have been sentenced for both.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for unlawful possession of a switchblade but reversed the conviction for unlawful carrying of a deadly weapon. The court remanded.

Wing Pawn Shop v. Taxation & Revenue Dep't


No. 10,555


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 735; 1991-NMCA-024; 809 P.2d 649; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 137; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 403; 15 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 1395



March 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Department of Taxation and Revenue; Gerald B. Richardson, Hearing Officer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer, a pawn shop, challenged an order of appellee, the Department of Taxation and Revenue (New Mexico) (department), which denied the taxpayer's protest of a gross receipts tax assessment.


OVERVIEW: The department held that the taxpayer's disposal of a pawnor's chattel was subject to taxation under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-9-4 (1978). In pawn transactions, the taxpayer loaned cash to the pawnor and either gave the item back if the cash was repaid within 120 days or disposed of the item in satisfaction of the loan. The taxpayer argued that the pawn sales fell within the statutory exemption to the gross receipts tax under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-9-25 and within the statutory deduction under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-9-61.1. The court affirmed, holding that the taxpayer failed to comply with the notice required under the Uniform Commercial Code, N.M. Stat. § 55-9-505(2). The court held that there was substantial evidence that the taxpayer intended to retain the collateral in satisfaction of the debt and not account to the pawnors after the sale. The taxpayer did not meet his burden that he kept an accounting of the portion the proceeds that constituted interest on money loaned for an exemption under § 7-9-25 or receipts from charges for a deduction under § 7-9-61.1. The department was not estopped from denying the taxpayer's protest and the taxpayer was afforded a fair hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the department that denied the taxpayer's protest for gross tax receipts assessments for its pawn sales.

State v. Stephens


No. 12,328


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 543; 1991-NMCA-019; 807 P.2d 241; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 120; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 299



February 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Lea County; Alvin F. Jones, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which convicted her of using a telephone to terrify, intimidate, harass, annoy, or offend in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-20-12 (1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of using a telephone to terrify, intimidate, harass, annoy, or offend. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the calls made by defendant were neither threatening nor maliciously annoying. The court found that because defendant was calling the victim to seek her assistance in terminating what she felt was an unhealthy relationship between her granddaughter and the victim's son, the calls were not maliciously annoying. Because the victim's son was over 20 and was having a sexual relationship with defendant's 16-year-old granddaughter, he was committing a fourth degree felony. The court found the basis for the calls to be legitimate. The court determined that defendant did not threaten the victim by telling her that she was going to call the attorney general. The court found that because the statement did not include a threat of criminal or tortious misconduct, it was not a threat.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for using a telephone to terrify, intimidate, harass, annoy, or offend.
