State v. Watchman


No. 12212


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 727; 1991-NMCA-010; 809 P.2d 641; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 133; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 408



January 22, 1991, Decided  
January 22, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of McKinley County; Joseph L. Rich, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the sentences imposed by the District Court of McKinley County (New Mexico) following his pleas of guilty to one count of felony vehicular homicide and one count of misdemeanor vehicular homicide. The trial court had considered evidence of defendant's prior uncounseled tribal and municipal court convictions for driving while intoxicated when it imposed an aggravated sentence of an extra year for the felony offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been hospitalized after the motor vehicle accident in which he killed two individuals. The trial court had limited his presentence commitment credit to the time he was confined in jail after being released from the hospital. Defendant contended he was in custody while hospitalized. On appeal, the court vacated the sentences and remanded for resentencing and for a determination of the proper amount of presentence commitment credit. The court held that it was error to consider the uncounseled convictions because defendant had not waived assistance of counsel and because he had offered evidence of indigency. Although tribal law did not require appointment of counsel to indigent defendants, the court found that it was required by the N.M. Const. art. II, §14, and the Sixth Amendment to the U.S. Const. The court also held that the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for determination of indigency was not prejudicial and its refusal to order a presentencing diagnostic commitment was not an abuse of discretion. The court found that any questions regarding the trial court's intention that the sentences be concurrent was resolved by the written order.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentences imposed by the trial court for defendant's two vehicular homicide convictions; the court remanded for determination of the proper award of presentence confinement credit and for resentencing.

Pineda v. Grande Drilling Corp.


No. 11379


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 536; 1991-NMCA-004; 807 P.2d 234; 1991 N.M. App. LEXIS 108



January 8, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the New Mexico Department of Labor Workers' Compensation Division; Gregory D. Griego, Workers' Compensation Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, an employer and its insurer, appealed the order of the New Mexico Department of Labor Workers' Compensation Division, which awarded attorneys' fees to claimant, an employee's widow, pursuant to its payment and benefit rule. The widow cross-appealed, contending that she should have received fees pursuant to The Interim Act regardless of the payment and benefit rule.


OVERVIEW: The widow and her children were awarded benefits under the Workers' Compensation Act based on the husband's death during the course of his employment with the employer. The widow was awarded attorneys' fees pursuant to the payment and benefit rule, but not pursuant to The Interim Act. The court reversed the award under the rule and affirmed the denial of an award under the Act. The court held that N.M. Const. art. IV, § 34 barred the application of the payment and benefit rule to the widow's claim because the case was pending when the rule was enacted. Even though the issue of whether the rule applied was not raised before the Division, the widow did not suffer any unfair prejudice from the consideration of the issue for the first time on appeal, and the public interest and jurisdictional nature of the error argued in favor of consideration. Further, the widow was not entitled to an award of attorneys' fees under the Act because while there was evidence of bad faith, there was no evidence of any economic injury suffered as a result of respondents' delay in paying benefits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award of attorneys' fees to the widow under the payment and benefit rule and affirmed the denial of an award off attorneys' fees under the Act.

State v. James M.


No. 12011


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 473; 1990-NMCA-135; 806 P.2d 1063; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 150



December 13, 1990, Decided  
December 13, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Children's Court of Grant County; V. Lee Vesely, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed from a judgment and disposition of the Children's Court of Grant County (New Mexico), which found him guilty of disorderly conduct, as defined by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-20-1 (1978, Repl. Pamp. 1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant got into an argument with another person, who accused him of burglarizing his van. Defendant waived his arms at, pointed at, and used derogatory language toward the other person, even though a police officer told him to stop. Defendant contended that there was insufficient evidence to find him guilty of disorderly conduct and that the offense of disorderly conduct was void for vagueness. The court affirmed the judgment. The court noted that the lower court's reliance on defendant's language to support the disorderly conduct did not violate defendant's right to free speech because defendant's language involved "fighting words," which were not protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. Because defendant's language and actions were likely to incite an immediate breach of the peace, the court concluded that there was sufficient evidence of a violation of disorderly conduct under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-20-1 (1978, Repl. Pamp. 1984). Considering that the statute was limited to conduct disturbing the peace, was understandable by the average person, and was based on what was offensive to the average person, the court determined that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant for disorderly conduct.

 

552 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baca


No. 11514


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 270; 1990-NMCA-123; 804 P.2d 1089; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 134



November 20, 1990, Decided  
November 20, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied January 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Bernalillo County; H. Richard Blackhurst, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for conspiracy to commit armed robbery, armed robbery, and aggravated burglary, all with use of a firearm, which was entered by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico).


OVERVIEW: During the trial court's voir dire, a prospective juror stated that she was the victim of a robbery. She stated she was inclined to sympathize with the state. However, during voir dire by the state and defendant, the juror stated she had thought the matter over and she felt confident she could make a decision based on the evidence. The trial court refused to excuse the juror for cause. Defendant contended that because the juror equivocated about her impartiality until pressured into it by being the object of the scrutiny of the open court, she should have been excused. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that if a juror rehabilitated his or her own bias, the trial court may properly deny challenges for cause to that juror absent undue prompting from the court or counsel. The court found that the juror admitted a bias but was left to think about the matter while the court and counsel examined other jurors on voir dire. On further examination, the first thing she said was that she on further reflection came to the conclusion that she could set aside her bias and decide the case on its own facts. The juror was not pressured by the trial court or counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for conspiracy to commit armed robbery, armed robbery, and aggravated burglary, all with use of a firearm.

 

553 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bolton


No. 11194


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 28; 1990-NMCA-107; 801 P.2d 98; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 114; 29 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1019



September 20, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied November 14, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Guadalupe County; Benny E. Flores, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the District Court of Guadalupe County (New Mexico), which convicted defendants of trafficking a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendants sought a motion for rehearing after they were convicted of trafficking a controlled substance. The sole issue on appeal was the legality of the search that uncovered cocaine in a false gas tank on their truck. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that the roadblock itself was proper because there was no evidence that state police officers questioned motorists about their citizenship in the absence of reasonable suspicion. Thus, the checkpoint was not in actuality an immigration checkpoint. The court further held that the patrol agent acquired sufficient evidence to establish probable cause to search the tank and that he acquired the evidence lawfully. When asked how many gas tanks they had, one defendant replied three while the other replied two. The patrol agent also crawled under the truck and pointed out that the gas tank could not be used for gasoline because the strapping seemed hand-cut and that the tank was not intended for that area of the truck. The court concluded that the underside of defendants' truck was sufficiently exposed to public view that the patrol agent's observations did not constitute a search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's denial of defendants' motion to suppress and affirmed their convictions and sentences for trafficking a controlled substance.

 

554 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gallegos


No. 11857


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 110; 1990-NMCA-104; 802 P.2d 15; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 123



September 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied November 26, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Curry County; Fred T. Hensley, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which found that he had committed the crimes of child abuse and aggravated battery and that he was dangerous, and ordered his detention by the New Mexico Health and Environment Department (HED) in a mental health facility pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-9-1.5(D)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with child abuse and aggravated battery. He pleaded guilty to the crimes. The trial court sentenced defendant to prison. Defendant filed a motion to withdraw his plea on the ground that he was mentally incompetent. Based upon the testimony of prison officials, the trial court allowed defendant to withdraw his plea. After a competency hearing pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-9-1.5(A), the trial court found that defendant had committed the crimes and that he was dangerous. The court ordered defendant's detention by the HED in a mental health facility. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court determined that the evidence supported the trial court's finding that defendant had committed the crimes and that he was dangerous. The court held that pursuant to § 31-9-1.5(A) the trial court was not required to find that defendant was dangerous in two separate hearings, and that the statute did not require an evaluation by the HED before a finding of dangerousness and an order for initial detention could be entered. The court ruled that the incompetency statutes did not deprive defendant of due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order finding that defendant had committed child abuse and aggravated assault and that he was dangerous, and ordering his detention in a mental health facility.

 

555 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cruz


No. 12250


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 780; 1990-NMCA-103; 800 P.2d 214; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 110



September 6, 1990, Decided  
September 6, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 17, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Colfax County; Peggy J. Nelson, District Court Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court of Colfax County (New Mexico), which convicted her of battery upon a police officer in a rude, insolent, or angry manner, a violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-24 (Repl. Pamp. 1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, when she visited her mother in jail, called a police officer a name that he found offensive and, during a scuffle with him, kicked him. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that "rude, insolent, or angry" was sufficient to reasonably define defendant's conduct as criminally culpable. Further, because defendant failed to demonstrate prejudice that arose from the trial counsel's representation of her, the court denied her motion to amend. Moreover, because § 30-22-24 required the conjunctive facts of rudeness, insolence, or anger, possibly evinced or accompanied by speech, without touch or applying force, the court held that the State punished defendant for the inseparable combination of what might have been a protected activity and what was clearly not a protected activity. The court held that where defendant coupled her rude, insolent, or angry remarks with force upon a police officer, the jury could have found defendant guilty of battery upon a police officer. Under the record before it, the court found that the statute was not vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

556 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Giant Indus. Ariz., Inc. v. Taxation & Revenue Dep't


No. 11787


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 442; 1990-NMCA-074; 796 P.2d 1138; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 57



June 26, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the New Mexico Taxation and Revenue Department; Gerald B. Richardson, Hearing Officer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer disputed a decision of the New Mexico Taxation and Revenue Department, which denied its protest of gasoline excise tax assessments and found the taxpayer liable for the assessments. One issue was whether the limitation of the deduction from the tax in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-13-4.1 (Repl. Pamp. 1988) to denatured ethanol alcohol made exclusively in New Mexico was a constitutionally impermissible burden on interstate commerce.


OVERVIEW: The Department assessed the taxpayer for nonpayment of taxes on ethanol-blended gasoline that was not manufactured exclusively in New Mexico. On appeal, the Department conceded that the deduction was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. art. I, § 8. The court held that the discrimination between the tax treatment of ethanol-blended fuel manufactured in New Mexico and such fuel manufactured elsewhere violated the commerce clause. In considering whether the offending provisions in § 7-13-4.1 were severable such that the rest of the statute could be preserved, the court noted that the first two criteria of a three-part test were met. The court considered the purpose of § 7-13-4.1 as stated in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-13-4.3 (Repl. Pamp. 1988). The court concluded that economic protectionism for New Mexico agricultural products was the primary purpose of the deduction. Concluding that the legislature would not have enacted the deduction had it known that the provision was invalid, the provision could not be severed. The entire deduction was invalid. The severability issue was not moot and the court refused to consider whether the Department had the power to declare a statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

State ex rel. Angel Fire Home & Land Owners Ass'n v. S. Cent. Colfax County Special Hosp. Dist.


No. 10945


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 496; 1990-NMCA-072; 797 P.2d 285; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 81



June 21, 1990, Decided  
June 21, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied August 8, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From the District Court of Colfax County; William W. Deaton, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, hospital and others, challenged the decision of the District Court of Colfax County (New Mexico), which entered judgment for appellees, corporation and landowners, finding that the New Mexico Special Hospital District Act (SHDA), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 4-48A-1 through 4-48A-18 (1989) was unconstitutional. The trial court found that the SHDA unconstitutionally delegated legislative powers to private persons.


OVERVIEW: Appellees contended that the SHDA allowed private persons arbitrarily to include property in a special hospital district even though the property and inhabitants would not have been benefited by inclusion. The court rejected this contention, holding that there was not any constitutional prohibition against including property within a special hospital district even though the property and its inhabitants would not benefit from inclusion. Further, the court held that it could not see how appellees could establish a total absence of benefit from inclusion in a special hospital district of relatively limited boundaries. The court reversed the judgment, holding that the SHDA was not unconstitutional on its face solely because the tax to benefit ratio for certain property owners may have differed from that for others within a special hospital district. The court held that because the potential for abuse under the SHDA was sufficiently small, there was no reason to strike the legislation itself. The court concluded that whether a particular district was created or acted in violation of the SHDA could have been resolved through specific litigation without bringing down the entire house.


OUTCOME: In appellees' action challenging the constitutionality of the SHDA, the court reversed the judgment, which was against appellants, and which had found that the SHDA was unconstitutional.

State v. Benny E.


Nos. 11613, 11573


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 237; 1990-NMCA-052; 794 P.2d 380; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 40



April 26, 1990, Decided  
April 26, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY; ALVIN F. JONES, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant child appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Chaves County, children's court (New Mexico), which adjudicated him a delinquent after a bench trial conviction for committing criminal sexual contact of a minor victim pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-13 (Supp. 1989). The trial court had found that the child had touched his private parts to those of his eight-year-old sister, causing her to contract gonorrhea.


OVERVIEW: The charging document alleged that the crime took place sometime during a two-month period. The victim testified by video. She had trouble remembering and refused to answer some cross-examination questions due to embarrassment. The state was permitted to show the victim a stick figure drawing of a person. On appeal, the court held that the charging document gave the child adequate notice to permit him to prepare a defense. However, the court held that the case should be remanded for a determination of whether the victim had needed special protection warranting the video testimony, which would otherwise have violated the child's right to confrontation. The court found that the drawing was not improperly leading since it was necessary to develop the victim's testimony. The court rejected the child's arguments that § 30-9-13 was unconstitutionally vague because it did not define the terms "groin" and "unlawful." Further, the court rejected the child's contention that he had been denied his right to confrontation because the victim failed to answer certain questions. The court noted that he had had a full and fair opportunity to expose any infirmities in the victim's testimony.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally affirmed the trial court's adjudication of the child as delinquent but remanded for findings as to whether the victim had been in need of special protection that had warranted admission of her testimony on a video monitor rather than in person. The court indicated that if the trial court found that the victim had not been in need of such protection, the child should be afforded a new trial.

State v. Crislip


No. 11411


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 412; 1990-NMCA-054; 796 P.2d 1108; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 60



April 26, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 19, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Chaves County; William J. Schnedar, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), which had convicted defendant of child abuse resulting in death, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-6-1 (1978).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his wife were charged with child abuse resulting in death of their stepson, who suffered from multiple injuries, and they were tried separately. Defendant was convicted as charged and alleged error in the upholding of his wife's assertion of the Fifth Amendment self-incrimination privilege while she was appealing her conviction, in the state's refusal to grant use immunity to the wife, and in the admission of a recording of the wife's trial testimony at defendant's trial. On appeal, the court held that: (1) although the wife had testified in her defense at her trial, she did not thereby waive her right to claim the self-incrimination privilege, which could be raised while her direct appeal was pending, at defendant's trial; (2) the trial court had no authority to grant the wife use immunity, which was within the sole control of the prosecution, whose refusal to grant her the immunity was not for improper reasons; and (3) defense counsel made a tactical decision to present the tapes of the wife's prior recorded testimony in the event that she chose to invoke her self-incrimination privilege at defendant's trial, thereby waiving error to the admission thereof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for child abuse resulting in death.

 

560 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Calvillo


No. 11616


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 114; 1990-NMCA-046; 792 P.2d 1157; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 35



April 17, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied May 23, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY; R. W. Gallini, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the District Court of Lea County, defendant was convicted of possession of a firearm by a felon. Appealing the conviction, he alleged that (1) the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress; (2) the prosecutor made improper comments during his closing argument about defendant's failure to testify; and (3) the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on defense of property and defense of others.


OVERVIEW: On the evening of defendant's arrest, his neighbor reported to police that defendant had fired a shot at him. The officers in the area, who heard shots near the time of the neighbor's call, went to defendant's home, and from on a common driveway he shared with a neighbor shone a flashlight into defendant's window, where they saw him lying on a bed with a gun. When defendant did not answer their knock, the police removed a screen window, entered and arrested him. On appeal, the court ruled that because the officers viewed defendant from a common driveway, their action was not a Fourth Amendment search. Given that the officers had heard shots and the neighbor's report of being shot at, the trial court correctly found that exigent circumstances justified seizure of the gun. The prosecutor's closing argument criticized defense witnesses for not telling police when interviewed that, as they claimed at trial, the neighbor was the aggressor. Because it was based on the evidence and unrelated to defendant's failure to testify, it was proper. Because there was no evidence that defendant's acts were taken in defense of property or others, the refusal to give instructions thereon was correct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Henry L.

Pamp. 1989), was sufficiently expansive to contemplate the imposition of limited detention as a condition of probation.

562 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Whitaker


No. 11254


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 486; 1990-NMCA-014; 797 P.2d 275; 1990 N.M. App. LEXIS 76



February 6, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 19, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Curry County; Fred T. Hensley, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which imposed sentence upon him after his nolo contendere plea to fraud and making false public vouchers. The district court found aggravating circumstances on the fraud counts, ordered defendant to turn over any money in a bank account to the county, and conditioned a reduction of defendant's prison sentence on his payment of restitution within 30 days.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the county manager for Curry County, was convicted of fraud and making false public vouchers. On appeal, the court held that (1) defendant could be prosecuted and sentenced for making a false public voucher, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-23-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1984) and fraud, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-16-6 (Cum. Supp. 1989); (2) the continuing nature of defendant's crimes, the betrayal of his high fiduciary duty, and his blaming of other persons were appropriate aggravating circumstances for enhancement of his sentence; (3) ordering defendant to turn over ill-gotten money in a bank account was an appropriate method of compelling partial restitution; and (4) the district court properly included the expense of an audit as "actual damages" to be considered in ordering restitution. However, the court concluded that the district court did not follow the mandate of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-17-1 (Repl. Pamp. 1987) by failing to determine whether defendant had the ability to pay restitution within 30 days. Thus, the district court erred when it conditioned a reduction of defendant's prison sentence on his payment of restitution within 30 days of his original sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded for a new sentence. The court required the district court to consider defendant's ability to pay restitution within 30 days before conditioning a portion of his term of imprisonment on payment of restitution within that time frame. Unless spelled out, the district court should not have considered the absence of the money acquired by defendant as an aggravating circumstance.

State v. Altgilbers


No. 10071


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


109 N.M. 453; 1989-NMCA-106; 786 P.2d 680; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 105



December 7, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended February 20, 1990. Certiorari Denied January 22, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, JOSEPH F. BACA, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which entered convictions for 83 counts of criminal sexual penetration and criminal sexual contact perpetrated on children under 13 years of age.


OVERVIEW: Two of defendant's daughters were the victims of the crimes. Defendant argued that the district court erred by admitting prior statements by his children that identified him as their abuser. The court disagreed and affirmed the convictions. In doing so, the court held that the trial court properly admitted the statements to the therapist pursuant to N.M. R. Ann. 11-801(D)(1)(b) as pretrial consistent statements that rebutted charges of improper influence or motive. The statements to the pediatrician and psychologist were properly admitted pursuant to N.M. R. Ann. 11-803(D) as statements made for purposes of diagnosis or treatment. The court also held that the use of the children's depositions at trial satisfied the Confrontation Clause because defendant had opportunity for cross-examination at the children's depositions. Further, the trial court made individualized findings that the children needed protection from testifying at trial face-to-face with defendant. Defendant was not denied due process by the State's delayed disclosure of a child's recantation because such evidence was disclosed during the trial and defense counsel was as much at fault as the State.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Garcia v. Mt. Taylor Millwork, Inc.


No. 10996


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 17; 1989-NMCA-100; 801 P.2d 87; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 122



November 16, 1989, Decided  
November 16, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Quashed July 24, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the New Mexico Department of Labor Worker's Compensation Division; Joseph N. Wiltgen, Hearing Officer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the order of the New Mexico Department of Labor Worker's Compensation Division, which awarded appellee widow death benefits under the Workers' Compensation Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The only access to the employer's plant was over railroad tracks. A train struck an employee's vehicle while he was proceeding to work. His widow sought death benefits under the Act, and the compensation division awarded her benefits. The court affirmed and held that the Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-5-1 (1987), was a prospective statement of legislative intent that left the going and coming rule in tact. The railroad crossing constituted a part of the employer's premises for purposes of recovery of benefits under the premises exception to the going and coming rule. The railroad crossing was adjacent to the employer's plant, and the employer had negotiated a right of passage over the crossing. The crossing was the sole means of ingress and egress to the plant. Under these circumstances, the crossing was sufficiently connected to the employer's business as to be an integral part of it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that awarded the widow death benefits under the Act.

 

565 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crews


No. 10894


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 723; 1989-NMCA-088; 799 P.2d 592; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 120



October 26, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied December 6, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Dona Ana County; Benny Flores, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of judgments from the District Court of Dona Ana County (New Mexico) convicting them of conspiracy to commit fraud, fraud, and racketeering.


OVERVIEW: Defendants entered into a contract to provide school bus service to a local school district. Defendants were required to submit expense reports that itemized the amount spent on fuel, maintenance, and driver salaries. After an audit, it was determined that many of the figures had been fraudulently increased, and defendants had been pocketing the additional money. Criminal charges were brought against defendants for conspiracy to commit fraud, fraud, and racketeering. After a jury trial, defendants were convicted on all charges. Defendants appealed the convictions raising numerous points of alleged error. Of primary importance, the court discussed the challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence. The court noted that such a challenge required it to review the evidence in a light most favorable to support the verdict, resolving all conflicts and indulging all permissible inferences in favor of the verdict. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions of all defendants, except for the corporation. The court held that the corporation was improperly convicted of racketeering because it was not specifically charged in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The judgments and sentences were affirmed as to all defendants, except the corporation's conviction for racketeering was reversed, and the matter was remanded for entry of a judgment dismissing the count against the corporation.

 

566 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Montez v. J & B Radiator, Inc.


No. 10774


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


108 N.M. 752; 1989-NMCA-060; 779 P.2d 129; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 56



July 20, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied September 5, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant employee sought review of the disposition order of the Workers' Compensation Division (New Mexico) awarding her five- percent permanent partial disability. The employee claimed that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-25 (Supp. 1986) violated her right to equal protection and that N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 52-1-25, 52-1-42 (Supp. 1986) did not limit permanent partial disability to the American Medical Association (AMA) guidelines for permanent impairment.


OVERVIEW: The previous and subsequent codification of the workers' compensation laws provided that partial disability benefits were determined by the inability to perform work, while benefits under the Interim Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-42 (Supp. 1986) were determined by the AMA guidelines on percentage impairment. The court rejected the employee's contention that the Interim Act violated her equal protection rights, finding that the act did not create two classes of workers. All injured workers during the effective dates of the Interim Act were treated the same. The mere fact that a previous and subsequent codification of workers' compensation laws treated workers differently did not raise an equal protection claim. The court also found that the plain language of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-42 (Supp. 1986) provided that partial disability would be determined by the AMA guidelines for permanent impairment. Where the act's language was clear and unambiguous, the court would not resort to any other means of interpretation, and it declined to disturb the hearing officer's findings. The court affirmed the disposition order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the hearing officer's disposition order.

State v. Mirabal


No. 11272


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


108 N.M. 749; 1989-NMCA-057; 779 P.2d 126; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 53



July 13, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied August 18, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the trial court (New Mexico), which entered judgment convicting him of attempting to obtain a controlled substance, a violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-31-25(A)(3) (1987).


OVERVIEW: After defendant attempted to have an invalid prescription filled, he was arrested and charged with violating § 30-31-25(A)(3). The trial court denied defendant's motion for a directed verdict and entered judgment convicting him. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 30-31-25(A)(3) was unconstitutionally vague, holding that it proscribed the intentional acquisition or attempted acquisition of a controlled substance by false means and that it was specific enough to provide a person with notice and fair warning of the nature of the proscribed act. The court specifically found that the terms "deception" and "subertfuge" in the statute were not too general or overly sweeping and that § 30-31-25(A)(3) did not conflict with the general attempt statute, since § 30-31-25(A)(3) was the more specific statute and thus controlled. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the trial court lacked jurisdiction, finding that jurisdiction was shown because the trier of fact reasonably inferred that the mall where defendant attempted to have the prescription filled was located in New Mexico.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State ex rel. Battershell v. City of Albuquerque


No. 10317


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


108 N.M. 658; 1989-NMCA-045; 777 P.2d 386; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 43



May 30, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: May 30, 1989


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, who sought a conditional use permit to operate an adult book store, challenged a judgment from the trial court (New Mexico), which had affirmed the respondent city's denial of such a permit.


OVERVIEW: The owners had operated an adult bookstore until the city enacted an ordinance requiring adult bookstores to relocate from certain areas, and established restrictive criteria for the location and operation of such businesses. The owners purchased an unimproved lot and filed an application with the city for issuance of a conditional use permit to operate another adult bookstore. The site was zoned M-2, and designated as a heavy manufacturing zone. A hearing was held by a zoning hearing examiner, who approved the application for the conditional use permit. The city overruled the examiner and denied the use permit. The owners sought certiorari to the trial court, which affirmed the decision from the city. The court reversed and held that the city failed to comply with the provisions of its zoning code, which required that applicants for a conditional use permit were due notice and a public hearing to present evidence and argument and to question witnesses on all relevant issues. It was error for the city to have refused the owners reasonable cross-examination of witnesses opposing their application, and to refuse that such witnesses be sworn.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the trial court, which had affirmed the decision from the city to deny the owners a conditional use permit to operate an adult bookstore.

 

569 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Jacobs v. Meister


No. 9093


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


108 N.M. 488; 1989-NMCA-033; 775 P.2d 254; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 28



April 21, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 2, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff professor brought a civil rights action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against defendant administrators and others for violation of his constitutional rights in failing to renew his university teaching contract. The trial court (New Mexico) entered judgment for the professor. The administrators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The professor had frequently criticized the university's administration. The university decided not to rehire him. The administrators argued that three of the trial court's findings supported their contention that the professor's First Amendment rights were not violated because his criticism undermined close working relationships and disrupted the proper functioning of the university. The court concluded that despite the three findings, the record and the trial court's other findings amply supported its conclusion that the professor's criticism of the university was protected and was a substantial or motivating factor in the administrators' decision to terminate his employment. Further, the administrators were liable for the violation of the professor's first amendment rights, as they set in motion the events that led to his termination. The professor's own testimony was substantial evidence of emotional injury sufficient to support the award of damages, and he did not have to produce a medical expert or other evidence to support the award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the professor.

 

570 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Elam


No. 10051


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


108 N.M. 268; 1989-NMCA-006; 771 P.2d 597; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 68



February 9, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 27, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the trial court (New Mexico), which convicted him of nine counts of fraud and one count of tax evasion. He argued on appeal that the trial court erred by failing to suppress evidence or grant a new trial; that the search was invalid due to errors in obtaining and executing the warrant; that the jury was improperly instructed; that several counts should have been merged; and that his trial counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his convictions for fraud and tax evasion, defendant raised five issues. The court affirmed, rejecting each of defendant's arguments. Specifically, the court held that the trial court did not err by failing to suppress evidence or grant a new trial on the grounds that the search warrant was not specific and resulted in an unconstitutional general search. Nor was the search invalid due to errors in the manner the search warrant was obtained and executed. The court held that the jury was properly instructed on fraud and tax evasion. Even assuming the trial court erred in refusing to merge several of the counts with which defendant was charged, he received concurrent sentences for the alleged lesser included offenses, which protected him from double jeopardy. Further, the court held that principles of double jeopardy were not offended by the collateral consequences of the separate convictions. Finally, the court rejected defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of trial counsel. Defendant, having raised this issue for the first time on appeal, failed to meet his burden of showing that his attorney was incompetent and that he was prejudiced by counsel's errors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for nine counts of fraud and one count of tax evasion.

 

571 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Inc. County of Los Alamos v. Montoya


No. 10556


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


108 N.M. 361; 1989-NMCA-004; 772 P.2d 891; 1989 N.M. App. LEXIS 10



February 7, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 21, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The County of Los Alamos (county) sought review of the judgment of the district court (New Mexico), which declared that the Los Alamos County Municipal Court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to try first offenders for driving while intoxicated (DWI), contrary to local ordinance, and that the local ordinance under which defendants were charged was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with DWI and either pled no contest or were found guilty in municipal court pursuant to Los Alamos County Municipal Ordinance, N.M. Code § 10.24.140(C) (1986). They appealed to the district court, which ruled that the ordinance was unconstitutional and that the municipal court did not have jurisdiction over defendants who were first-time offenders. The county appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The court found that the jurisdictional statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-8-102F (1978), stated that it did not affect the authority of a municipality to prescribe penalties under a proper ordinance. The court held that under N.M. Const. art. X, § 5, an incorporated county had all the powers granted to a municipality and could enact an ordinance of the type at issue. Defendants argued that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it prescribed a mandatory jail term for first time offenders, whereas the state statute provided that the sentence for such offender could be suspended or deferred. The court found that the ordinance was not inconsistent with the statute because the penalty imposed under the ordinance did not exceed the penalty prescribed by statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the district court judgment that had held that the county's ordinance relating to DWI was unconstitutional and that the municipal court did not have jurisdiction to try first time offenders charged with DWI.

State v. Jim


No. 10425


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


107 N.M. 779; 1988-NMCA-092; 765 P.2d 195; 1988 N.M. App. LEXIS 105



October 18, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied November 18, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SAN JUAN COUNTY, BENJAMIN S. EASTBURN, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the District Court of San Juan County (New Mexico) for great bodily injury by a motor vehicle in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-8-101 (Repl. Pamp.1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a Navajo Indian. The state used one of its peremptory challenges to strike a Navajo Indian. Defendant was convicted of great bodily injury by a motor vehicle. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) defendant failed to establish a prima facie case of discriminatory use of the state's peremptory challenges because there was no showing that Navajo Indians were substantially underrepresented on the jury, and both defendant and the victim were Navajo Indians; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excusing a potential juror for cause who was a personal friend of defense counsel and whose sister worked for defense counsel; and (3) N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-1-12 (978) was not unconstitutionally vague because the term "protracted impairment" was capable of reasonable application by a jury of common intelligence after consideration of the circumstances involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for great bodily injury by a motor vehicle.

 

573 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. Vill. of Tijeras


No. 9424


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


108 N.M. 116; 1988-NMCA-090; 767 P.2d 355; 1988 N.M. App. LEXIS 99



October 11, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: October 11, 1988
 [*116] Certiorari Denied December 6, 1988.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pit bull owners sought review of the decision of the New Mexico trial court, which entered judgment in favor of defendant village in the pit bull owners' action seeking to declare a village ordinance banning pit bull terriers unconstitutional. The pit bull owners contended that the ordinance was vague, violated their procedural and substantive due process rights, and was an unconstitutional taking of their private property.


OVERVIEW: The village enacted the ordinance banning pit bull terriers in response to a series of attacks by pit bulls on persons and animals. The court held that the pit bull owners did not have standing to challenge the ordinance on vagueness grounds because the ordinance clearly applied to them. The court held that the village was entitled to combat the special threat it faced from pit bulls, and that the village's action was clearly rationally related to efforts to combat that threat. The court found no equal protection violation in the ordinance's singling out of only the pit bull terrier breed of dog. The ordinance did not violate the pit bull owners' procedural due process rights because it clearly contemplated that a hearing would take place before a dog was destroyed. The court held that the ordinance was not an unconstitutional taking because it was a legitimate exercise of the police power, reasonably necessary to preserve and protect the public health, safety, and welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment upholding the constitutionality of the village ordinance.

 

574 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Proficient Food Co. v. N.M. Taxation & Revenue Dep't


No. 10028


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


107 N.M. 392; 1988-NMCA-042; 758 P.2d 806; 1988 N.M. App. LEXIS 35



May 3, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: May 3, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: ADMINISTRATIVE APPEAL FROM THE TAXATION & REVENUE DEPARTMENT



DISPOSITION: We affirm the decision and order of the administrative hearing officer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the decision from appellee New Mexico Taxation and Revenue Department, which denied its protest of an assessment of gross receipts tax, interest and penalties upon it for food and supplies sold to restaurants in New Mexico. The taxpayer contended that the tax violated the Commerce Clause and a blanket exemption certificate substantially complied with N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-9-43 (1978).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contested the assessment by the department of the state gross receipts tax upon it for food and supplies sold to restaurants in New Mexico. The taxpayer contended that the assessment violated the Commerce Clause and that a blanket exemption certificate obtained from Denny's substantially complied with N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-9-43 (1978). The court affirmed the department's assessment. The court held that: (1) where the taxpayer's employees delivered food into the state and the taxpayer had a policy of visiting its customers' restaurants in New Mexico, there was sufficient nexus for the state constitutionally to impose the gross receipts tax upon the taxpayer's activities; (2) the assessment on the total receipts of goods sold to the New Mexico restaurants did not subject the taxpayer to double or triple taxation and was fairly apportioned to its activities within the state; and (3) the blanket certificate did not substantially comply with state requirements where it was not in a form prescribed by the department and would have required the department to revamp its processing and verification procedures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revenue department's determination assessing the state gross receipts tax upon the taxpayer for food and supplies it sold to restaurants in New Mexico.

State v. Curry


No. 10470


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


107 N.M. 133; 1988-NMCA-031; 753 P.2d 1321; 1988 N.M. App. LEXIS 24



March 31, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 26, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CURRY COUNTY, REUBEN E. NIEVES, District Judge 



DISPOSITION: Based on the reasons stated above, we affirm defendant's convictions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which convicted him of attempted trafficking by possession with intent to distribute, a violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-31-20(A)(3) (1987), § 30-28-1 (1984), and of conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: A package was delivered to defendant and was left at his neighbor's apartment, with a notice of delivery on the door of the building. Defendant's neighbor inadvertently discovered that the package contained drugs and drug paraphernalia, and she delivered the package to the police. Defendant made several attempts to collect his package from his neighbor but was unsuccessful. He was arrested and convicted of attempted trafficking by possession with intent to distribute and of conspiracy. On appeal, he argued that an attempted violation of the trafficking statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-31-20(A)(3) (1987), was not a crime under New Mexico law. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and held that it was possible for defendant to intend to possess a controlled substance and to intend to distribute that controlled substance without the person actually possessing the controlled substance. Under the general attempt statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-28-1 (1984), defendant could have attempted possession with intent to distribute; the attempt applied to the possession, not the intent. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-31-20(A)(3) was not applied in an overbroad and unconstitutional manner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Ensenada Land & Water Ass'n v. Reynolds (In re Sleeper)


Nos. 8782, 8830


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


107 N.M. 494; 1988-NMCA-030; 760 P.2d 787; 1988 N.M. App. LEXIS 62



March 29, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Quashed August 2, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF RIO ARRIBA COUNTY, Art Encinias, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant owners and respondent state engineer appealed the judgment of the District Court of Rio Arriba County (New Mexico), which reversed an order of the state engineer. The order granted a modified application of the owners to change the purpose and place of use and point of diversion of surface water rights appurtenant to a water source against the contentions of protestants, a land and water association and others.


OVERVIEW: The owners sought to transfer their water rights for irrigation purposes to the creation of a lake. The trial court reversed the state engineer's decision, which allowed their application, on the grounds that the requested transfer would impair existing water rights on the stream system and would be contrary to the public interest. The court disagreed with the reversal. The court found, inter alia, that (1) under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-5-23 all water used for irrigation purposes could be transferred for other purposes, without losing priority of right theretofore established, if such changes could be made without detriment to existing rights; (2) the long-standing administrative constructions of statutes by the agency charged with administering them were to be given persuasive weight, and were not be lightly overturned, such that the state engineer's orders were presumed to be proper implementations of the water laws; and (3) inherent in a water right was the right to change the place of diversion, subject only to the requirement that the rights of other water users not be injured or impaired thereby.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. On remand, it ordered that the inadvertent omission of a requirement for monthly metering be corrected.

Gallegos v. State


No. 9072


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


107 N.M. 349; 1987-NMCA-150; 758 P.2d 299; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 815



December 15, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Quashed June 30, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, BRUCE E. KAUFMAN, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Cert. Quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former inmate challenged an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which denied the inmate's motion to amend and granted summary judgment for defendants, state and prison officials, in the inmate's action under the New Mexico Tort Claims Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-4-1 to 41-4-29 (Repl. 1986), and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, for injuries sustained when the inmate was assaulted by other inmates.


OVERVIEW: The former inmate initiated an action against the state, the state department of corrections, the former governor of the state, and the former warden and assistant warden after another inmate battered the former inmate with a mop wringer, alleging that the state was liable under the theory of respondeat superior and that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-6 operated to waive state immunity for the maintenance of equipment. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment, and the former inmate filed a motion for leave to amend his complaint. The trial court denied the motion to amend, and granted summary judgment for defendants. The former inmate appealed, and the court affirmed, holding that § 41-4-6 did not provide a waiver of immunity for the inmate's claim because no claim was made that any physical defect existed with the mop wringer or that a defect caused the former inmate's injuries. The court found that the inmate's civil rights claim failed because the inmate did not demonstrate an "affirmative link" between the deprivation of the inmate's rights and the actions or inactions of defendants and the harm done to the inmate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants in the former inmate's tort and civil rights action for injuries sustained when the inmate was assaulted by other inmates. The court affirmed the denial of the inmate's motion to amend.

State v. Lynn C.


No. 10268


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 681; 1987-NMCA-146; 748 P.2d 978; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 804



December 10, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied January 20, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY, Robert M. Doughty, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sought review of an order of the District Court of Otero County (New Mexico), which revoked her probation.


OVERVIEW: As a condition of probation, respondent was required to follow the rules of the group home where she resided. Respondent violated one of the group home rules prohibiting smoking. Respondent also told the group home director that she was not going to stay at the home or work the program. The trial court granted the state's petition to revoke respondent's probation based on evidence of her statement to the director, her smoking, and her admissions of violating the group home rules. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order, holding that (1) there were no violations of respondent's rights of confrontation and cross-examination where her admissions of violating the group home rules were sufficient to establish a probation violation; (2) the evidence of smoking was not based on hearsay where respondent admitted the smoking incidents either in her docketing statement or in a statement to the group home director; and (3) there was no due process violation in revoking respondent's probation as a result of her smoking because she had sufficient notice that smoking could result in probation revocation where she was required to follow the home rules as a condition of probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's revocation of respondent's probation.

COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO

Rubio v. Carlsbad Mun. Sch. Dist.


No. 9646


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 446; 1987-NMCA-127; 744 P.2d 919; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 775



October 6, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: October 6, 1987, Filed; Certiorari Not Applied For


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Eddy County, Harvey W. Fort, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents sought review of an order from the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which granted a motion to dismiss made by defendant, the Carlsbad Municipal School District (district). The parents brought a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action as well as alleged negligence and breach of contract. The court awarded attorney's fees to the district pursuant to § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The parents brought an action because a teacher employed by the district obtained marijuana for their minor children who were students at the school. On appeal, the court affirmed dismissal of the action. The court held that no waiver of sovereign immunity was made by the district pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-4-5 through -12. Therefore, the parents' claims for negligence in hiring and retaining the teacher could not go forward. The court also held that a claim for educational malpractice was not recognized by the state and, even if it was, it was a form of negligence barred by sovereign immunity. The court held that the breach of contract claim was properly dismissed as well because payment of taxes did not create a contractual relationship with the district. The court also held that the parents did not meet the requirements of a § 1983 action because they failed to allege that the district sanctioned distribution of marijuana to its students either by custom or policy. The court found that the award of attorney's fees to the district under § 1988 was proper because the parents failed to do even minimal research, which would have revealed that they had no § 1983 claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which granted the district's motion to dismiss the parents' § 1983 claim as well as their claims for negligence and breach of contract.

The jury rendered a verdict in favor of the property owner. The injured party appealed, and the property owner sought recovery of his jury expenses. Ct. 1-038(H) costs were property awarded to the prevailing party. The court affirmed as to the injured party's objections and reversed and remanded as to the property owner's costs issue.

Amerada Hess Corp. v. Adee


No. 8393


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 422; 1987-NMCA-117; 744 P.2d 550; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 772



September 1, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 21, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HARDING COUNTY, STANLEY F. FROST, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners appealed a summary judgment of the District Court of Harding County (New Mexico) in favor of plaintiff company in the company's action that sought an injunction and a declaration that it had the right to construct and operate a carbon dioxide gas distribution pipeline within the easement granted by the landowners to the state highway department.


OVERVIEW: The company filed a complaint for declaratory judgment and for an injunction requesting that the district court declare it had the right to construct and operate a carbon dioxide gas distribution pipeline within the easement granted by the landowners to the state highway department. The landowners objected to the construction of the pipeline, counterclaimed for an injunction prohibiting the company from further burdening their lands, and sought damages. The trial court granted the company's motion for summary judgment on the basis that the state highway department had the power to authorize the placement of pipelines, and that highway easements could be used for pipelines without constituting an additional burden on the servient estates. On appeal, the court affirmed. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 67-3-12(C) was an implicit delegation of power to the state highway commission to permit pipelines under public highways. The company had a permit for the emplacement of its pipeline on the state's right-of-way and no contention was made that the permit procedure was violative of law. Private corporations or persons that were not utilities were not excluded from the coverage of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the company in the company's action that sought an injunction and a declaration that it had the right to construct and operate a carbon dioxide gas distribution pipeline within the easement granted by the landowners to the state highway department.

State ex rel. Stratton v. Sinks

COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 213; 1987-NMCA-092; 741 P.2d 435; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 748



July 2, 1987

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant business solicitor sought review of the judgment by the District Court of San Juan County (New Mexico) in favor of plaintiff state in a civil suit for injunctive relief, restitution, and civil penalties under the Pyramid or Multilevel Sales Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 57-13-1 to -18 (1978) and the Unfair Practices Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 57-13-1 to -18 (1978).


OVERVIEW: The business solicitor operated a business whereby he solicited membership into the Rocky Mountain Traders and for a fee members joined, and then those members were instructed to solicit new members. The jury determined the business solicitor operated a pyramid chain, while it was in the guise of being a multilevel sales program, no product was ever sold and no goods were ever placed in the stream of commerce. The court also held the Act was not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad as people of common intelligence did not have to guess as to its meaning. Finally, the court held a statute was sustainable proper as a proper exercise of police power if it was reasonably necessary to prevent manifest evil or reasonably necessary to protect the public safety or general welfare and New Mexico had personal jurisdiction.

City of Farmington v. Wilkins


No. 9912


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 188; 1987-NMCA-088; 740 P.2d 1172; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 743



June 30, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied August 14, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of San Juan County, James L. Brown, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the owner of a commercial truckwash, appealed a judgment of the District Court of San Juan County (New Mexico), which convicted him of violating the general noise control ordinances contained in Farmington, N.M., City Code §§ 21-48 and 21-49.


OVERVIEW: The owner of the truckwash broadcasted music through loudspeakers. The parties stipulated that the sound created by the loudspeakers was within the decibel limits permitted by Farmington, N.M., City Code § 20A-6, and that a number of private citizens who lived in the vicinity of the truckwash found the noise to be loud, irritating, and disturbing to their comfort and repose. Defendant was convicted in municipal court of violating Farmington, N.M., City Code § 21-49. He appealed to the trial court, which found him guilty of violating both Farmington, N.M., City Code § 21-48 and § 21-49. The court held that: (1) § 20A-6 was not a specific statute that prevailed over §§ 21-48 and 21-49 because the former was a strict liability statute based solely on decibel levels, while the latter sections concentrated on the character of the noise and its effect on others; (2) § 20A-6 and §§ 21-48 and 21-49 were distinct from each other because the latter required proof of facts not required by the former; and (3) §§ 21-48 and 21-49 were not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

586 of 795 DOCUMENTS


In re Samantha D.


No. 96910


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 184; 1987-NMCA-082; 740 P.2d 1168; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 741



June 23, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied August 14, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Children's Court of Bernalillo County, John E. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the Children's Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which terminated her parental rights. Appellee prospective adoptive parents sought review of the trial court's finding that there was no abandonment under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32-1-54(B)(1), that the mother's consent form for adoption was invalid, and that there was no waiver and estoppel.


OVERVIEW: The trial court terminated the mother's parental rights. The mother and the parents appealed. The court held that the mother physically gave up her child when the infant was less than 48 hours old and executed a consent to adoption form, which was defective, five days after the child's birth. A key element in determining whether parental rights should be terminated under § 32-1-54(B)(4) was whether the parent-child relationship had disintegrated. The child's extended absence from her natural mother led to the disintegration of the parent-child relationship. Thus, the trial court did not err in terminating appellant's parental rights under § 32-1-54(B)(4). The mother failed to overcome the statutory presumption of abandonment. The trial court retained the power to determine custody in the absence of a legally valid consent, and it was within the authority of the trial court to continue the child in the custody of the parents. Because the mother's consent was invalid and because she did not give up a known legal right, waiver did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

587 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. McDuffie


No. 9657


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 120; 1987-NMCA-077; 739 P.2d 989; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 730



June 4, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Bernalillo County, Joseph F. Baca, Judge.



DISPOSITION: In sum, we hold that it was error for the trial court to proceed with the suppression hearing in defendant's absence and reverse and remand.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) dismissed defendant's appeal of his conviction in the trial court of carrying a concealed weapon in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-7-2 (Supp. 1986). Defendant appealed the district court's dismissal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a "street person" with no permanent address. Notice for defendant's appeal trial in the district court was given by the clerk to defendant's counsel, who was under the mistaken belief that the clerk would also notify defendant. When defendant's counsel realized the error, she asked for a continuance of the suppression hearing and received a one-day continuance. Inexplicably, defendant's counsel did not take advantage of the continuance, waived the presence of defendant, and proceeded with the suppression hearing. The district court denied the motion to suppress and, the next day, with defendant still absent, denied defendant's motion for a continuance and dismissed defendant's appeal. The court reversed and remanded, holding that defendant was entitled to be present at the suppression hearing, absent a voluntary, knowing, and intelligent waiver. N.M. R. Ann. 5-612(A) required that defendant be present at the arraignment, at the time of the plea, and at every stage of the trial. Because defendant had not spoken to his attorney or received notice of the suppression hearing, the court held that he could not have validly waived his presence at the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

 

588 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bernal


No. 9670


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 117; 1987-NMCA-075; 739 P.2d 986; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 731



June 2, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied July 13, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Rio Arriba County, Patricio M. Serna, Judge.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, the sentences imposed by the trial court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court of Rio Arriba County (New Mexico), which increased his basic sentences, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-18-15.1 (1981), for second degree criminal sexual penetration, kidnapping, false imprisonment, and assault with intent to commit criminal sexual penetration.


OVERVIEW: At a sentencing hearing following defendant's convictions for sexual assault-related crimes, the trial court increased his basic sentences and stated orally that it did so because defendant's conduct was brutal and he may have been a power rapist whose violence was triggered by uncontrollable alcohol abuse. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court's consideration of the physical injury suffered by the victim in enhancing his sentences exposed him to double jeopardy, holding that the trial court properly considered the circumstances surrounding the offense and concerning the offender in making its decision and that its consideration of circumstances surrounding an element of the offense did not expose defendant to double jeopardy. The court further held that the trial court's oral statement of its reasons for increasing defendant's sentences constituted a brief statement in the record of the case of its reasons for altering the basic sentence, as required by § 31-18-15.1(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentences.

 

589 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Climax Chem. Co. v. New Mexico Envtl. Improvement Bd.


No. 8896


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 14; 1987-NMCA-065; 738 P.2d 132; 1987 N.M. App. LEXIS 718



May 5, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY: ADMINISTRATIVE APPEAL FROM THE ENVIRONMENTAL IMPROVEMENT BOARD'S ADOPTION OF AMENDMENTS TO THE LIQUID WASTE DISPOSAL REGULATIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chemical company sought review of a decision from appellee environmental improvement board (New Mexico), which adopted a revised liquid waste disposal regulation pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 74-1--8(A)(3) (1978, Repl. 1986).


OVERVIEW: The environmental improvement board had issued a decision that adopted a revised liquid waste disposal regulation pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 74-1-8(A)(3) (1978, Repl. 1986). The chemical company then filed an appeal before the court challenging the board's adoption of the revised regulation. The court issued a judgment that found the board did not abuse its discretion in adopting the regulation. Specifically, the chemical company challenged that certain provisions in the regulation were unconstitutionally vague. The court disagreed, and did not find the regulations facially vague. The court found the terms in the regulation of "more stringent" and "degradation of a body of water" had provided clear and specific guidelines, which was clear enough to keep the regulation from being constitutionally vague. The court held that it was not necessary that a regulation be drafted with absolute precision, but only that it could be construed using known and accepted rules of construction.


OUTCOME: The court issued a judgment that found the environmental improvement board did not abuse its discretion in adopting a revised liquid waste disposal regulation pursuant to the New Mexico statute.

 

590 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crenshaw


No. 9069


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


105 N.M. 329; 1986-NMCA-132; 732 P.2d 431; 1986 N.M. App. LEXIS 703



December 23, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LINCOLN COUNTY, Richard A. Parsons, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Lincoln County (New Mexico), which convicted him of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: After obtaining a search warrant based on observations of defendant going in and out of an area containing suspected marijuana plants, the police conducted a search and seized marijuana plants. Defendant appealed his conviction. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the search warrant was invalid and part of the evidence obtained was inadmissible as the product of an illegal search and seizure. The initial search that formed the basis for probable cause for the warrant was illegal because the officers intruded onto the curtilage of the cabin, which was an area protected by the Fourth Amendment. The open fields exception did not excuse the lack of a search warrant because the police had no right to be on the curtilage when they observed marijuana growing in close proximity to the cabin. Further, the plain view exception did not justify the intrusion onto the curtilage of defendant's cabin. However, the court found that some of the evidence found outside the curtilage of the cabin was admissible. The court remanded the cause with instructions that the trial court determine if there were any means of distinguishing the admissible evidence from the inadmissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and defendant's conviction for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. The court remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

591 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gattis


No. 9176


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


105 N.M. 194; 1986-NMCA-121; 730 P.2d 497; 1986 N.M. App. LEXIS 681



November 26, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Not Applied For


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CURRY COUNTY, REUBEN E. NIEVES, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment and sentences are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which convicted him of use of a telephone to harass, annoy or offend, contrary to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-20-12 (1978, Repl. Pamp.1984), and sentenced him to 18 months on each count to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of use of telephone to harass, annoy or offend after he frequently called two ex-girlfriends making lewd comments to them. He argued that to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-20-12(A) was overbroad, prohibited conduct that was constitutionally protected, that § 30-20-12(A) was too vague and indefinite, and that there was a failure of proof under the circumstances. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence finding that § 30-20-12(A) was directed at conduct concluding that the making of the call was the prohibited act, not the speaking of any particular words. The court concluded that the crime could have been committed without any words being spoken, and that it was not unconstitutionally overbroad. The court concluded that § 30-20-12(A) was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness because it set out terms that the ordinary person exercising ordinary common sense could have sufficiently understood and complied with. The court found there was substantial evidence to support the conviction where defendant showed a pattern of behavior toward the women that supported a finding of malicious intent in making the telephone calls.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for use of a telephone to harass, annoy or offend his ex-girlfriends.
