State v. Johnson


No. 8904


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


105 N.M. 63; 1986-NMCA-084; 728 P.2d 473; 1986 N.M. App. LEXIS 658



August 19, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 16, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Lea County, Paul Snead, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which convicted him of 12 counts of fraud, one count of conspiracy, and one count of racketeering.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a used car and automotive repair business. Defendant was charged with fraud, conspiracy, and racketeering arising out of allegations of overcharging for vehicle repairs, falsifying claims to insurance companies, charging for work not performed, billing for new automotive parts which were not installed, and falsifying documents regarding sales of vehicles. The trial court convicted defendant of 12 counts of fraud, one count of conspiracy, and one count of racketeering. On appeal, the court determined that the instructions had adequately alerted defendant to the offenses charged and the victims involved. The court also found that the convictions were supported by substantial evidence. The court also found that New Mexico's Racketeering Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-42-1 through 30-42-6 was constitutional. Finally, the court fond that the trial court's jury instructions properly covered the essential elements of the charged offenses and conformed to the proof presented at trial. Accordingly, defendant's convictions were affirmed. The court remanded for resentencing on one of the fraud charges because the sentence exceeded the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-18-15.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The court remanded for proper sentencing on one of the fraud charges.

 

593 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Cano v. Lovato


Nos. 7915, 7926


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


105 N.M. 522; 1986-NMCA-043; 734 P.2d 762; 1986 N.M. App. LEXIS 712



April 29, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Quashed March 12, 1986 (Cano). Certiorari Denied June 24, 1986, (N.M. Title and Estate of Robinson).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, PHILIP R. ASHBY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: IT IS SO ORDERED. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants estate, buyers, and title company sought review of a decision by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which quieted titled in the buyers and granted a lien against the property to appellee good faith purchasers.


OVERVIEW: The buyers purchased real estate at a tax sale and filed an quiet title action against a title company, good faith purchasers, and the estate of the former property-owner. The good faith purchaser and the estate argued that the buyers' title was defective and that the good faith purchaser had superior title. The court affirmed the judgment because the deed was issued pursuant to the New Mexico Recording Act and the tax sale and deed were not invalidated on the basis of a claimed jurisdictional defect. The court remanded the case for a determination of whether the good faith purchaser executed its deed prior to the tax sale, which occurred on the same day. The court found that the good faith purchaser, who was unaware of the tax deficiency, acquired equitable interest in the property by paying value. The court held that the title company failed to exercise ordinary care, or reasonable diligence, to communicate to both the good faith purchaser or the estate knowledge acquired in the course of its agency. The court also stated that the good faith purchaser was entitled to a lien for the fair market value of the improvements made prior to notice of the buyers' interests.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally affirmed the judgment based on the outcome of a fact-finding remand involving the good faith purchasers' execution of the real estate contract.

 

594 of 795 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. AQUI


Nos. 8857, 8914, 8940 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


1986 N.M. App. LEXIS 612; 25 N.M. St. B. Bull. 662



February 27, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, BURT COSGROVE, Judge, GERARD W. THOMSON, Judge



DISPOSITION: The orders concerning Aqui and Sena are reversed and their cases are remanded to the trial court for determination of the amount of good-time credit to which they are entitled and entry of an appropriate order. The appeal of Gobel is dismissed.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from orders of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which denied motions for additional credit for good time spent in jail because they were unable to make bail and spent time between arrest and sentencing in jail.


OVERVIEW: Three defendants were sentenced, but because they were unable to make bail, they spent the time between arrest and sentencing in jail. All three defendants were given credit for this time served. Each filed a motion for additional credit for good time spent in jail. The theory of these motions was that a person admitted to bail during this time would be able to earn good-time credit for each day spent in the penitentiary pursuant to the sentence and would serve a lesser sentence than a person unable to make bail during the presentence period of the case since N.M. Stat. Ann. § 33-2-34(A) authorized the corrections department to award good-time credit of 10 days per month to prisoners based on good conduct. The trial court denied each defendant's motion. Two defendants filed their motions for the credit within 30 days as required by rule. The other defendant filed her motion after 30 days. This late filed appeal was dismissed. The court held that the other two defendants were entitled to a good time credit for presentence confinement given defendants' substantial liberty interest and how the denial of good time credit presentence significantly impaired that interest and reversed.


OUTCOME: The orders concerning the two defendants who filed motions within 30 days of the trial court order denying their motions were reversed and their cases remanded to the trial court for determination of the amount of good-time credit to which they were entitled and entry of an appropriate order. The appeal of the other third defendant was dismissed.

Deer Mesa Corp. v. Los Tres Valles Special Zoning Dist. Comm.


No. 8024


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 675; 1985-NMCA-114; 712 P.2d 21; 1985 N.M. App. LEXIS 620



December 5, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TAOS COUNTY, Frank H. Allen, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: The summary judgment is affirmed. No costs are awarded.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Los Tres Valles Special Zoning District Commission appealed a decision of the District Court of Taos County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff corporation in an action brought against it and against defendant Board of County Commissioners of Taos County that was related to the constitutionality of the Special Zoning District Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 3-21-15 to 3-21-26 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The corporation applied to the County for preliminary plat approval of a subdivision it wanted to build. The district commission found that the proposed subdivision did not comply with its ordinance as to lot sizes and number of lots. The corporation brought an action against defendants for relief that sought, inter alia, a declaratory judgment that the Act was unconstitutional because it delegated power to private persons and allowed arbitrary exercise of power by individuals. The corporation filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted. The trial court held that the Act was an unconstitutional delegation of power to individuals. The district commission appealed, contending that the trial court should not have decided the constitutional question. The court affirmed, holding that § 3-21-18, which permitted private individuals to "create" a special zoning district without any limitation on the size and location of the district, was void as an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power because there was no standard to guide the private individuals in determining the size or location.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the corporation in an action it brought against defendants that alleged the Act under which defendants refused to approve its planned subdivision was an unconstitutional delegation of power to individuals.

 

596 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lujan


No. 8161


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 667; 1985-NMCA-111; 712 P.2d 13; 1985 N.M. App. LEXIS 618



December 3, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied January 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Phillip R. Ashby, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court.

IT IS SO ORDERED. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) for aggravated assault and child abuse when defendant and four others attacked victims and threw beer bottles so as to hit a child.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the conviction, finding that there was substantial evidence to allow the jury to determine that defendant was aware of the child's presence and that he shared in the intent to assault the victims. The victims testified that they entered their vehicle carrying their child and that defendant participated in the verbal and physical attacks. The court found that defendant's actions came within the child abuse statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-6-1(C), which forbade anyone from endangering the life or health of a child. Defendant was not put into double jeopardy because under the jurisdictional exception defendant was indicted for felony offenses which were outside the jurisdiction of the metropolitan court, which had dismissed the misdemeanor charges for failure to timely prosecute. The court found that there was no prosecutorial vindictiveness at the pretrial stage and that defendant did not show that the state's charging decision was motivated by a desire to punish him for having exercised a legal right. It was not error to admit extrinsic evidence to impeach defendant that the other occupants in his vehicle were hitchhikers whom he did not know.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated assault and child abuse.

 

597 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Sanchez v. M.M. Sundt Constr. Co.


No. 7964


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 294; 1985-NMCA-087; 706 P.2d 158; 1985 N.M. App. LEXIS 586



August 29, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, THOMAS J. MESCALL, Judge



DISPOSITION: The order of the trial court dismissing plaintiff's complaint against defendant with prejudice is affirmed. Each party will bear their costs on appeal.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father, as the personal representative of the estate of his son, appealed a judgment from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which dismissed his wrongful death complaint with prejudice against defendant, the employer of his son.


OVERVIEW: The son was killed in an accident that occurred in the course of and arose out of his employment. The trial court ordered the complaint against the employer dismissed under N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 52-1-8 and -9, the exclusive remedy provisions of the Workmen's Compensation Act. In affirming the judgment the court held that the Act did not violate equal protection. Specifically the court held that the discrimination between non-dependent survivors of employees subject to the action and non-dependent survivors of ordinary torts was reasonable, because the purpose of the Act was to mitigate the financial hardship suffered by dependent survivors. The court also held that it was reasonable to discriminate between non-dependent survivors, who under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-46(A), received mostly expenses, and dependent survivors, who were entitled to additional compensation under N.M. Stat. § 52-1-46(B)-(F), for the same reason. Finally, the court held that the punitive purpose of the Act, which was secondary, was vindicated by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-10(B) and (C) in cases where an employe lacking dependents was injured.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the wrongful death action.

 

598 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Doe


Nos. 8019, 8211, 8377


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 233; 1985-NMCA-065; 704 P.2d 1109; 1985 N.M. App. LEXIS 650



June 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied August 13, 1985.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three consolidated appeals by three defendant minors were filed to challenge orders of the Children's Court (New Mexico), which issued transfer orders pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32-1-30 (Repl.Pamp.1981). Each child raised one common issue: whether § 32-1-30 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The three juveniles, two very close to the age of majority and another aged 16, were each charged with serious crimes, such as first degree criminal sexual penetration of a child under 13 years of age, aggravated assault, and murder. The trial court ordered the transfer of the juvenile cases to the district court based on a jury determination pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32-1-30. The three juveniles, in a consolidated appeal, challenged the transfer order. Each child contended that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32-1-30(A)(4) was unconstitutional on the basis that it was impermissibly vague, failed to provide a discernible and constitutional standard of proof, failed to give the child adequate notice regarding the factors against which he was required to defend, and worked to deprive the child of meaningful appellate review. The court affirmed the transfers and held that § 32-1-30 was constitutional. The court held that proof or disproof of amenability was not requisite to a transfer under § 32-1-30; (2) nothing in the constitution required amenability to even be considered; and (3) the children did not challenge what was required under § 32-1-30, or the standard of proof for it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the transfer orders and the constitutionality of the statute at issue.

 

599 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aaron


No. 8028


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 138; 1985-NMCA-060; 703 P.2d 915; 1985 N.M. App. LEXIS 648



June 11, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied July 16, 1985.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Bernalillo County District Court (New Mexico), which sentenced him for his multiple convictions of issuing worthless checks and fraud.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to correct his sentence during the pendency of his first appeal. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant appealed. In dismissing the appeal of the denial of the motion, the court first noted that the appeal was untimely, but that this defect was the fault of the clerk of court. Nevertheless, the court held that the trial court had lacked jurisdiction to hear defendant's motion to correct, because the pendency of the first appeal divested the trial court of jurisdiction. The court noted however that under N.M. Stat. Ann., R. Crim. P. 57.1 (Repl. Pamp. 1980), the trial court could correct an illegal sentence within 30 days of the appellate mandate. The court held that under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-20-12 (Repl. Pamp. 1981) defendant was entitled to one credit of 200 days for presentence confinement, and one credit only. The court rejected defendant's contention that he was entitled to 200 days credit for each of his 26 sentences.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal of the denial of his motion to correct sentence.

 

600 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gillette


No. 7667


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW MEXICO


102 N.M. 695; 1985-NMCA-037; 699 P.2d 626; 1985 N.M. App. LEXIS 555



April 11, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, JACK L. LOVE, Judge



DISPOSITION: The convictions and sentences are affirmed.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) convicting him of 16 counts of sexual penetration in the second degree, five counts of attempted first degree murder, arson, residential burglary, and contributing to the delinquency of a minor.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose from his sexual relationship with the minor victim. After learning that the victim and the victim's family were about to move to Australia, defendant attempted to poison the victim's mother by mixing pentobarbital into a can of soft drink and attempted to burn down the victim's home. On appeal, defendant claimed he was denied due process for the attempted murder charge because none of the soft drink was left, after testing, for an independent analysis by defendant's chemist. The court held that the introduction of the poison into evidence was not reversible error because the "lost" evidence did not prejudice defendant's case. There was no substantial basis for supposing that the "lost" evidence would have undercut the state's case in light of the amount of evidence presented by the state. The court also held that the trial court was within its discretion in not permitting defendant to question the minor victim concerning the child's prior sexual conduct with persons other than defendant. Defendant was allowed during his case in chief to testify about what the victim told him at the inception of their relationship about his past sexual conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction against defendant.
